the road not taken (among the wildflowers)

by greatwarsenal

Summary

Agatha and Rio, once inseparable childhood sweethearts, took different paths — one chasing city dreams, the other finding comfort in farm life. Agatha left; Rio stayed.

Now, as Agatha faces her past choices and sacrifices, she sees how much they’ve both changed. The love they once shared feels distant, and they hardly recognize each other.

What carries the greater pain: The past abandoned for an uncertain future, the present that turned out to be empty and agonizing, or the realization of what life could have been?

How can everything be different when time cannot be reversed and the lingering hurt refuses to fade?

Notes

hello, my name is madu (@greatwarsenal on twitter), and i’m excited to share my very first story here. i kindly ask for your understanding as english is not my first language, and i've never visit the united states so please excuse any geographical inaccuracies in my references to places and distances that i may not fully grasp. thank you for your patience! i truly hope you enjoy this long journey i'm about to take you on

Chapter 1: to float

"It's the first kiss, it's flawless, really something. It's fearless" - Fearless, Taylor Swift.

Twenty-six years ago

Riandra was oblivious to time. Estimating hours or time in general was a challenge for her. She often heard the familiar complaints—about it being too early or too late, about the hours dragging, or her father sighing over how quickly time flew. Yet, she had no real concept of it. She distinguished day from night by the sky's colors; humidity signaled dusk, and the scent of the earth told her when to water the plants.

Numbers baffled her; they held no charm or clarity. Clocks seemed pointless, and the meaning of those three hands escaped her. The endless ticking made her anxious, an absurd, perpetual cycle. It was far simpler to observe the world around her. Roosters announced morning, dairy cows sought shade on hot days, and cattle grazed from dawn until dusk, moving as the sun set.

The truth was, Rio couldn't tell time. Every attempt left her frustrated, so she learned to rely on her senses instead. Nature's scents, colors, and sounds were far more trustworthy. Rio was always on time, unlike Agatha, who constantly fought punctuality despite the clocks filling her home.

With narrowed eyes, she studied the bright, gently glowing sky while floating at the lake's edge, now scattered with a few wispy clouds. It was definitely past noon. She tilted her head, considering, as the cool water enveloped her. Perhaps it was around two o'clock in the afternoon. Stretching out her hand, she noticed the wrinkles forming on her skin from her long soak. She pushed herself closer to the bank, her toes brushing the warm, dry gravel. It was definitely two o'clock.

She needed to feed the horses by six. A sigh escaped her lips. Agatha was very late.

Rio’s mind raced, a whirlwind of ideas that never settled. Everything came and went in a blur; it was easy to start with one thought and find herself lost in something entirely different. Agatha's tardiness bothered her. It was Saturday; they always met at noon by the waterfall lake trail. If it was already two in the afternoon, they had lost two precious hours, leaving them with only four hours together. But she also had to factor in the travel time back to the farm and the stables. Could Agatha even make it today? Why was she late?

"I'm not late!" Agatha's voice sliced through the chaos of her thoughts, causing Rio to lose her balance and momentarily sink beneath the water. She kicked her arms to resurface, just in time to see Agatha rushing toward her, boots flying off and a dress tossed aside.

"Yes, you are!" Rio retorted, splashing water with her arms.

"My dad thought Mimosa was going into labor," Agatha explained, diving into the lake and swiftly gliding toward her. Rio playfully splashed her face in defiance, causing Agatha to roll her eyes. "I had to help, you know," she continued, exasperated, "but it turned out to be a false alarm."

"I told you it was too early," Rio shrugged. She had voiced her concern countless times, yet, as usual, no one seemed to take her seriously. "The calf isn’t positioned right yet; you can feel it. And she’s been walking too much. She’ll only calve after the full moon."

Agatha let out an amused sigh, her expression a delightful mix of exasperation and laughter that Rio adored.

"And since when are you a vet?" she teased, raising an eyebrow.

Before Rio could respond, she launched herself out of the water, sending a huge splash toward Agatha. Agatha cursed as she dove after her, and their playful chase across the lake erupted into a joyful water fight.

In that moment, Rio completely lost track of time; she always did when they were together. It felt as though time had stopped, holding them in an alternate reality. She felt limitless—truly boundless. Alive and joyful, time ceased to matter. Nothing else did. The colors of the sky, the sounds of nature, and the scent of the earth were merely markers for when they would meet again.

Fortunately, every day belonged to them.

Each day unfolded in a similar pattern, and truthfully, Rio had nothing to complain about. She cherished every moment, never yearning for more. The difference between happiness and dissatisfaction never crossed her mind; there was no need. This daily rhythm had been a constant in her life for as long as she could remember, and it brought her deep contentment.

Agatha had been her loyal companion for as long as she could recall, and their daily routine was a beloved ritual. Not a single day passed without them meeting; separation, when it happened, felt like an unbearable weight. They went to school together, shared their desks, walked home side by side, and when responsibilities weighed them down, they eagerly looked forward to their reunion.

Lost in their own world, they splashed through the lake, one chasing the other, their laughter mixing with the sound of the water. Their joy continued until the breeze turned cool, prompting them to seek shelter in the sun-drenched crevices of the large rocks. Sitting side by side, hands intertwined, they always had something to talk about.

Agatha gazed at the sky while Rio watched her features—the way her nose crinkled when she squinted at the sun, the faint freckles beneath her eyes, and the way she bit her lip in contemplation. Agatha was her favorite person, her other half. Endless days in this blissful state felt like a dream, and usually, that’s exactly how Rio spent her time. Yet lately, new feelings had begun to stir inside her. Whenever Agatha smiled, a flutter danced in her stomach; when she brushed Rio's hair or kissed her cheek, it felt as if a flock of birds took flight inside her. Her hands grew clammy, and a wide smile would spread across her face.

A few nights ago, after sleeping over at Agatha's, they lay wrapped in each other's arms. Agatha’s nose nudged against Rio’s neck, followed by a soft kiss. A delightful warmth enveloped Rio, creeping into her cheeks, her toes curling with joy. She felt a mix of nerves and excitement, a powerful urge to hold Agatha’s hand and never let go. She couldn’t stop staring at her. Despite trying to suppress these feelings, Agatha’s affectionate nature made it impossible. Rio wasn't usually fond of physical contact, but Agatha was the exception, and now they were constantly holding on to each other.

She remembered what Bucky had said at school—that they looked like a couple. In that moment, Rio froze, wide-eyed, while Agatha merely laughed it off, dismissing it as jealousy because he didn't have a girlfriend. Agatha squeezed Rio's hand tightly, intertwining their fingers, and the comment lingered in Rio's mind.

"Do you think everyone sees the same sky?" Agatha’s voice cut through Rio’s daydream, bringing her back to the present. Rio blinked, her brow furrowing as she noticed Agatha's intense gaze fixed on the heavens. "If someone, somewhere else in the world, is looking up right now, do you think they see the exact same thing we do?"

"Probably not," Riandra replied almost instinctively. Agatha's eyes sparkled with curiosity as she turned her focus toward Rio. "The sky itself might be the same, but while it's sunny here, it could be snowing somewhere else. It can't possibly look identical."

"So, even if the sky is uniform for everyone, you believe it appears different everywhere?"

"I think so." Rio shrugged, playing with their intertwined fingers. "Different places observe different sections of the sky."

Agatha bit her lip in contemplation, her gaze fixed upwards. Rio offered a faint smile, knowing Agatha often pondered such questions; her mind was a constant swirl of thoughts. It was a captivating trait that made her the smartest person Riandra knew.

"I wish I could see it," Agatha murmured softly. "I wish I could see the other parts of the sky, to know what it looks like elsewhere."

"Why?" Rio asked, her curiosity piqued, but Agatha simply shrugged.

"We only ever see this part. Don’t you want to see the others?"

"No," she replied honestly. "I quite like our part." Rio shrugged in response, prompting Agatha to roll her eyes playfully before turning her gaze back to the sky.

"But how do you know you wouldn't like another one better? You've never seen it."

"I don't need to," Rio replied, now fully facing Agatha. Their hands were intertwined, and their feet brushed together in a gentle, familiar way. "If I went somewhere else, I'd probably just want to come back. There's no better place than home."

"You don't want to see anywhere new? Discover other places?" Agatha asked, and Rio shook her head, her gaze fixed on Agatha's intense blue eyes, which were filled with questions.

"Do you?" Rio countered, and Agatha nodded eagerly.

"I want to go to Los Angeles." The mention sparked a light in Agatha's eyes, and Rio noted the excitement dancing in that vibrant blue.

"Why?"

"I want to go to the beach," Agatha exclaimed, her infectious smile pulling Rio into her excitement. "Like in the movies, you know? Surfing, walking on the sand, surrounded by all those people." She continued, her face alight with a wonder that Rio found difficult to share. "Can you imagine how many people live in Los Angeles? So many faces to see, so many adventures waiting to be had..."

Rio remained silent, unsure how to respond. She knew about Agatha's passion for movies, especially those depicting glamorous lives filled with designer clothes, glass-walled houses, and sleek convertibles. To Rio, it all seemed quite ordinary. She couldn't picture herself in those flowing dresses, walking down gray streets marked with yellow lines. There were no horses in Los Angeles, at least not in the movies she'd seen. What was the appeal of a house with a pool when she had lakes and waterfalls at home?

"Don't you want to go to Los Angeles?" Agatha inquired with an eager smile, and Rio shrugged, her expression shifting to one of mild indifference at the thought.

"I don't know," she replied, which wasn't entirely true. While she had no desire to go, she hesitated to admit it, especially with Agatha looking at her like that. "I suppose not."

"I do," Agatha stated firmly.

In that moment, Rio felt an unfamiliar sensation — a sharp pang of unease that wasn't like her usual flutters. She frowned and instinctively tightened her grip on Agatha's hand.

"Would you go without me?" The question slipped out, and Agatha's expression shifted into a delightful mix of confusion and amusement.

"What?" she laughed, frowning playfully before leaning closer. Rio held her breath as Agatha rested her forehead against hers, shaking her head. "Are you crazy? How could I possibly go anywhere without you, silly? You're coming with me."

"What if I don't want to go?" Rio teased, a sly smile creeping onto her lips. Relief washed over her when Agatha caressed her face, rolling her eyes with that familiar look — the one that playfully called her silly without saying a word.

"As if you could live without me."

Now it was Rio's turn to roll her eyes, stifling a smile.

"I can't."

"I know," Agatha replied, smiling as she pressed her forehead against Rio's. "You'll just have to come with me."

"But we're coming back home afterward."

"We can come back later, but there are so many other places to visit." Rio's expression darkened slightly, and Agatha's smile widened, aware of her reluctance to travel. "I want to see the whole sky with you."

Rio fell silent, lost in thought, mesmerized by that hopeful blue gaze. The initial pang of reluctance vanished, replaced by a thrill of anticipation. How could she refuse?

"With me," Rio finally agreed, and Agatha nodded, sealing their decision.

As Agatha’s nose brushed against hers, a rush of emotion surged in Rio’s stomach, her heart racing as if it might jump into her throat. Their eyes locked — Rio's brown eyes filled with questions, while Agatha's blue ones radiated certainty.

When Agatha closed her eyes, so did Rio. Fireworks erupted within her. When their lips met, it surpassed anything she had ever seen in the movies; it was messy and wet, delightfully different and undeniably good. In fact, she had just discovered that the feeling of Agatha's lips on hers, the taste of her mouth against her own eager tongue, was literally the best thing in the world.

Eventually, Agatha broke the kiss. When Rio opened her eyes, she was met by that captivating blue gaze. A symphony of sensations — tiny birds, fireworks, crashing waves, and fluttering butterflies — swirled inside her all at once. And when Agatha smiled, Rio couldn't help but smile back.

Chapter 2: the cycle

Chapter Notes

hi! i made a playlist for this fic bc all my writing is heavily influenced by music, it just helps me get those deep feelings across. this is a super emotional story, so if you're interested it's on my fixed tweets (@greatwarsenal on twitter) in the the road not taken (among the wildflowers) section. it’s a still growing playlist, and i tweak it constantly, but enjoy!

"All the death and the glory, believing they’re one and the same. Now I’m saving my strength for running" – Cavalry, Watchhouse.

Twenty-six years ago

When Javier arrived home, the clock had already struck five in the afternoon. Yet, it was summer, and the sky still glowed warmly—a gift he cherished, as he truly thrived in the summer heat. He carefully wiped his boots at the door and took off his hat, running a hand through his damp hair. He announced his arrival, as he did every day, but barely had a moment to appreciate the festive decorations before little Benito rushed toward him, arms wide open and stumbling in his newly mastered, eager steps.

"Mi frijolito!" he exclaimed, lifting the boy into the air as his son’s laughter filled the house. Benito clung to his neck, and Javier covered him with kisses.

"Mama! Papa's here!" Benito shouted with pure joy, making Javier chuckle as he set him down, holding back a grin while watching him dash toward the kitchen. "It's Papa!"

With slow, deliberate steps and hands on his hips, Javier wandered through the spacious living room, a smile growing on his face. The room was beautifully decorated; a large "Feliz cumpleaños!" banner hung prominently, and colorful balloons floated everywhere. The cake was a true masterpiece — three layers high and larger than anything he had ever seen. He marveled at how Maria had managed all this while keeping up with the little whirlwind now running through the house.

"Honey?" he heard her call from the kitchen. Still awestruck, he leaned against the doorframe, grinning like a fool at his wife, who was rolling sweets in front of an enormous tray.

"How did you pull all this off by yourself?" he asked, laughter bubbling in his voice, and she simply smiled back.

"Lilia and Eva helped a lot; they just left. They need to get ready for the party too," she explained, turning to the sink to wash her hands.

He approached her, wrapping his arms around her from behind, gently pulling her close and resting his chin on her shoulder. Maria didn’t even pause to dry her hands; instead, she turned in his embrace to kiss him, her smile radiant as she gently stroked his stubbled cheeks.

"Happy birthday, mi amor," she whispered softly, and he beamed, kissing her again.

He considered himself an incredibly lucky man, fully aware of his life's blessings. He had never faced major hardships; instead, he was raised in a wealthy, loving family on a sprawling farm of over eighty hectares. He genuinely couldn't imagine wanting anything more than what he possessed. Surrounded by many men whose experiences were vastly different, he knew he was truly blessed, yet it wasn't the land, the wealth, or the influence that mattered most—it was the joy of his family that filled his heart.

Despite his wealth, he was shaped by hard work and the land, like his entire family. He took a hands-on approach to the farm, overseeing every task and product. The satisfaction of witnessing prosperity and creating with his own hands was unparalleled. Even with a large crew working alongside him, he had little tolerance for idleness; he immersed himself in every detail. Many called that success. For him, however, no amount of money compared to the feeling of being home, surrounded by love, waking up each day next to the woman he adored, and watching his children play.

"Where's Rio?" he asked, scanning the room while still holding his wife close. "She was asleep when I left; I haven't seen her today."

His expression shifted as his wife raised her eyebrows and took a step back, avoiding his gaze. She moved a few steps across the kitchen, and he crossed his arms, watching her with growing apprehension.

"What's going on this time?"

Indeed, they were incredibly happy, yet not everything was perfect; every family faced its unique set of challenges. He certainly didn't see Rio as a burden — in fact, she was perfect in his eyes — but it seemed not everyone shared that opinion.

When Maria announced her pregnancy, Javier had initially hoped for a boy and grumbled about it for a while. Yet, all thoughts of a rough-and-tumble heir vanished the instant he gazed into his little girl's dark, jabuticaba eyes. Riandra was perfect—his sun and stars. She was the missing piece he hadn't known he needed, and to his delight, she bore an uncanny resemblance to him.

From an early age, she was captivated by animals, thriving in the freedom of the farm. Most days, despite his wife's protests, he took her along to work. Rio loved getting her hands dirty, indulging in grapes straight from the vine, and was feeding the horses even before she could speak clearly. They were her passion, just as they were his. By the time she turned eleven, she had become the finest horsewoman he had ever known, a true Vidal in every sense.

And therein lay the problem: she loved farm chores just a bit too much.

Maria remained silent, simply handing him the piece of paper taped to the refrigerator. Their daughter's report card was a disheartening collection of zeros, with her highest mark being a four in science. He let out a deep sigh.

"You know she doesn't like school," he said nonchalantly, shaking his head and scratching the back of his neck, his brows furrowing under his wife's intense gaze.

"She doesn't have to like it; it's school, Javi!"

This wasn't a new conversation. The ease Rio displayed on the farm, surrounded by the land and animals, was completely absent in the classroom; this had been true since kindergarten. Javier didn't see it as an issue, but Maria clearly did. Disliking school was common; many kids felt that way; Rio simply had different strengths.

Rio wasn’t outgoing; she had always been reserved, a child of few words, and while Maria labeled her slow, he didn’t see it that way; she was simply uninterested. While his wife focused on her challenges, he celebrated her talents. She might not excel in academics, but she succeeded in everything else she pursued. In just a few months, she had taught herself to play the guitar. She didn’t invest effort in what failed to capture her interest, and while he admitted that wasn’t ideal, he didn’t consider it a problem — not from his viewpoint.

"I'll talk to her teachers," he murmured, taking a deep breath, but Maria shook her head firmly.

"You do this every time, and she keeps moving up grades without earning the marks she needs. That's why she puts no effort into it."

"Not every child thrives academically, Maria," he insisted, a frown creasing his brow. "All that tedious material, thick books full of text, and now she has what? Eleven subjects?"

"Yes, eleven subjects, just like everyone else in her class who manages to score at least a five!"

"From seven in the morning until one in the afternoon, confined to a classroom—she can't stand it," he defended his daughter, eliciting an incredulous sigh from Maria. "Sure, she could try harder, but she has the potential to excel when she wants to. I don't pressure the teachers to pass her; I simply discuss alternative assessments with them, which works because she’s reluctant to spend two or three hours on a test. Yet, when asked questions, she knows the answers. She's incredibly bright!"

Maria simply shook her head, crossing her arms.

"If everyone else can take the test, why can't she?"

"Because she doesn't want to!" he exclaimed, exasperated.

"Then she needs to start wanting to!" Maria raised her voice, prompting him to shake his head and take a deep breath. She mirrored his action, gathering her thoughts before continuing. "She has to realize that not everything in life revolves around her desires. If her grades don't improve, I'll have to enforce consequences. No riding, no racetrack, no stables; she’ll be stuck indoors." When he frowned, Maria raised her eyebrows, her steady gaze emphasizing her seriousness. "You spoil her; she runs wild every day, but she must learn responsibility."

For Javier, the real issue would be if she failed to learn, yet he recognized Rio's intelligence and the multitude of skills she possessed that went far beyond mere grades. To him, this felt like bureaucratic nonsense. The school system confined children as if they were all identical, yet people are inherently unique, learning and expressing themselves in countless ways. He refused to punish his daughter for thinking differently, for having her own interests, and for not conforming. She was truly remarkable.

Still, he wouldn't start another argument with his wife over this.

"I'll talk to her," he agreed, lowering his head in resignation.

"Thank you," Maria replied, her voice now gentle and soothing. He let out a tired sigh, and she leaned in to kiss his cheek. "However, there's something else." Her tone shifted; it was neither angry nor frustrated, but subtly suggestive. She pressed her lips together, suppressing a smile while closely observing his reaction.

"What?" he inquired, raising an eyebrow in curiosity. She shyly rolled her eyes, a hint of amusement dancing across her face. "What is it?" He smiled inquisitively as she stifled an awkward laugh.

"Agatha," she replied, her eyebrows arched and that same teasing smile lighting up her lips, prompting him to lean back slightly and raise his own eyebrows in response.

Javier often mused that Agatha was the one thing Rio adored even more than the farm. The two had been inseparable since their diaper days. While his daughter was reserved at home, she blossomed into a chatterbox around Agatha. They were constantly together; if you found one, the other was sure to be nearby.

He wholeheartedly approved of their friendship; after all, the Harkness family was practically his own. Richard lived on his land, cared for his horses, and was an exceptional veterinarian. Javier felt fortunate to have persuaded him to move to Darby and work alongside him. Richard was not only a diligent worker but also a true friend, and their families shared a deep bond.

Richard, the dedicated veterinarian, and his wife Evanora, an expert in agronomy. He had met the couple at a rural conference. Their contributions were vital to the farm's prosperity, leading Javier to invest significantly in bringing the finest talent to Darby. They lived in a spacious family home nearby, part of the property, and the hierarchy between them was merely a formality. Javier had come to view them as family, especially after he became Agatha's godfather.

The girls grew up side by side. Rio was almost two when Agatha was born, and she was thrilled at the prospect of having a best friend. For as long as he could remember, since they began talking and truly understanding each other, they had been inseparable. It was quite amusing, really, given their contrasting personalities.

Agatha was a social butterfly, and Rio, despite being older, thrived in her vibrant presence. Unlike his daughter, Agatha took longer to learn to ride and enjoyed farm life, though not the necessary chores. She preferred the world of books and excelled academically. Her love for animals and the excitement of witnessing births was clear, yet her care often seemed clumsy, and her attempts at gardening never succeeded. Still, they shared a bond that surpassed all others.

Rio blossomed around Agatha; she made her laugh and talk. They could often be seen riding horses or racing along trails, spending sunny afternoons by the lakes and waterfalls. They were inseparable. While Rio had other friends, like Bucky and Natasha, she was rarely seen with anyone else after school; it was always Agatha by her side.

In truth, things were different with Agatha; he had sensed it already; he knew his daughter well.

"I think they’re dating," Maria said, stifling a laugh. Javier couldn't quite discern if her expression held disapproval, but the look she gave him next suggested there might be some in his own.

"Dating?" he asked, a frown momentarily crossing his face. It wasn't that he was opposed to Rio dating; she was entering adolescence, and it was bound to happen. But two girls... While not entirely surprised, the idea still stirred something in him. "What do you mean by dating?"

"Promise you won’t tell her I said anything," Maria cautioned, wagging her finger at him. Despite the amusement in her eyes, she was serious. He nodded his agreement. "I saw them kissing."

"Kissing... on the lips?" he asked, feeling a bit uncomfortable, which made her chuckle at his unease as she nodded.

"In the stables. I was looking for Rio, not spying," she explained, though he raised an unconvinced eyebrow. "They were all over each other."

He shook his head, lost in thought.

"But they're both girls."

"Javi, they like each other," she said sweetly, shrugging as if it were nothing. He continued to shake his head in disbelief. "They're thirteen; it’s the age of first love, right? How old were you when you had your first girlfriend?"

"Eleven," he confessed, somewhat reluctantly.

"It could be worse, don't you think?" she teased, enjoying his disapproval. "Would you prefer she was kissing that Barnes boy, Bucky?"

"At least he’s a boy," he shot back, grimacing in slight distaste.

"Is that really a problem?" Her brows furrowed in genuine curiosity.

"I'm not sure," he confessed, feeling a twinge of embarrassment.

Maria pulled back the kitchen window curtains and motioned for him to look outside. There they were—Rio riding Gaia, circling Agatha on Scratchy. They seemed deep in conversation, their laughter ringing out as they were lost in their own world.

He let out a deep sigh, realizing just how happy Rio looked; she always radiated joy around Agatha.

"I was going to ground her for her grades before we even had a chance to talk, but I just couldn't bring myself to do it," Maria confessed, capturing his attention. "You should have seen her face when Agatha arrived; she was all ready, waiting eagerly for her." She looked him in the eyes, a smile spreading across her face. "It was just too sweet."

"You really don't see any problem with this?"

"No, mi amor, they truly adore each other." Maria's demeanor softened completely as she spoke about the two, and he found himself softening as well. Maria and Riandra had him wrapped around their little fingers. "I even heard Rio call her mi cariño." She pouted, as if lost in thoughts of love, and Javier couldn’t help but chuckle. “It’s their first love!”

He shook his head, caught between conflicting feelings and amusement. Being a father often meant navigating moments where words failed him, unsure of the right response. Ultimately, everything boiled down to one goal: ensuring his children’s happiness.

“I’ll talk to her about this too.”

“Just don’t mention that I said anything.”

“I promise. I’ll ask her.”

"Ask her about what?" She playfully swatted his shoulder with the dish towel, catching him off guard with his own uncertainty.

"I'm not sure. I'll just talk to her," he said, fumbling for the right words. "Maybe she'll open up a little bit."

***

Javier stood by the front door as the girls arrived, the clock inching toward seven in the evening with the party scheduled for eight-thirty. Although he could have reprimanded them for their lateness—especially since they needed to get ready—he decided to let it go, eager for a moment to chat with Rio. He also knew all too well that Agatha was usually the one running late.

As soon as Agatha hopped down, she sprinted toward him, exclaiming, "Happy birthday, Uncle Javi!" Her radiant smile brightened his face as he pulled her into a warm embrace, playfully ruffling her hair.

"Gracias, mi tesoro," he replied, noticing her wet, mud-stained dress. "You need to get ready. We can't have you late for your godfather's party, can we?"

"No, sir," she answered sweetly and promptly. "I'll be right on time, I promise."

"She'll be late," Rio chimed in with a laugh, her tone teasing yet light, still perched on her mare.

"I will not!" Agatha shot back but quickly turned her attention to her godfather. "I will not."

"Go get ready, tesoro," he encouraged, giving her a gentle pat on the back. She nodded eagerly and dashed off through the brush toward the other house.

When he turned back to Rio, he noticed her preparing to dismount. He gently interrupted her movement, eliciting a smile and a curious glance as he steadied her waist to help her mount again.

"How about a ride? Just the two of us."

Without missing a beat, she replied, "Won't we be late for your party?" He shook his head dismissively, grinning as he watched her smile widen, clearly favoring a ride over mingling at a busy gathering.

"I'm the birthday boy," he remarked with a casual shrug, as if that explained everything. "I can show up whenever I like."

That was all the persuasion she required. Firmly grasping the reins, she swiftly pivoted while Javier rushed to mount his horse, and together they took off, galloping across the open land.

They hadn't charted a specific course, but whenever they rode just for the sheer pleasure of it, they inevitably found themselves at the vineyard for a leisurely stroll, and today was no different. He secured both horses, and they walked in quietude along the meandering paths between the grapevines.

Rio wasn’t much of a talker, and he didn’t see that as a fault; he cherished these moments of comfortable silence with his daughter, where they could both lose themselves in thought while she picked bunches of grapes to share. This was a beloved routine. Words weren’t necessary; they simply valued each other’s company in a moment that was uniquely theirs. Sometimes they chatted, sometimes they didn’t. But this quiet setting was perfect for meaningful conversations, and throughout the ride, Javier had been refining his thoughts, determined to speak in a way that would encourage her to open up as well.

“So…” he began casually, glancing down at his feet as he noticed his daughter’s inquisitive stare. “You and Agatha…” Her eyes widened instantly, and he bit his lip to suppress a laugh, striving to keep his demeanor relaxed while watching her cheeks flush with color.

“How do you know about that?” she replied, a hint of anxiety creeping into her voice. He shrugged, trying to signal that it wasn’t a big deal.

"I don't know, that's why I'm asking."

She fell silent, now focusing on her own feet. Sensing her embarrassment, he gently draped an arm around her shoulders, walking beside her in comfortable silence before broaching the subject again.

“Are you… dating?” he asked tentatively, earning another look of mortification from her. He couldn’t help but think that pre-adolescence was quite the entertaining stage. She quickly turned her gaze away.

“Are you okay with this?” she whispered, avoiding his gaze and focusing on her footsteps. He furrowed his brows, feeling a surge of empathy for her uncertainty. Maria had asked him the same question, and he had responded with hesitation; he couldn't give Rio the same answer. He just couldn't. “Because we’re two girls,” she added softly, her voice barely audible, and in that moment, any reservation he had instantly evaporated. He couldn’t say anything that would deepen her sense of vulnerability. He felt proud of her, and that was the feeling he wanted her to hold onto — pride in herself.

“Do you have feelings for each other?” he asked gently, and she looked up, nodding shyly.

“I really like her. A lot. It’s different; it’s not just friendship.”

“And she feels the same way?”

“Yeah.” A faint smile lit up her face, and he returned the smile, affectionately rubbing her shoulders. "She likes me too."

"Then there's no problem at all, mi cielo," he said. She looked at him with admiration, clearly impressed, as if she had expected a different reaction. A wave of pride washed over him; he was being the good father he wanted to be. "You like her, she likes you—that’s exactly how it should be. If you’re happy, then I’m happy too."

She smiled and extended her hand. With gentle care, Javier cradled hers between his.

"I thought you’d find it weird," she admitted.

"Some might, but I don’t." She nodded again, and this time, he noticed the smile she was trying to hide. "You know I love you more than anything, right?"

"I love you too, dad."

"You can talk to me about anything. I’ll always be in your corner."

"You promise?" She extended her pinky finger, just as she used to when she was younger, and he smiled, nodding as he linked his pinky with hers.

"But there's one thing I'm on your side about, and your mother isn't..." he said cautiously, and she immediately huffed.

"It's about school again, isn't it?"

“Could you put in just a bit more effort? Just a little." She huffed again. "You could use your homework time to study with Agatha," he suggested, causing her to blush. "You’d get to spend more time together."

“I’ll try,” she replied, somewhat reluctantly. It was now his turn to extend his pinky. Rio grumbled but linked hers with his, a satisfied smile spreading across his face.

***

Present Day

Natasha fought to maintain her composure as Evanora wept on the couch, sobbing like a child. Deep down, she knew she had to be the strong one; someone needed to anchor them in this storm. So, she paced back and forth, taking deep breaths and running her hands over her face.

How she managed to hold it together was a mystery, but she knew she must. The knot in her throat felt like a physical ache, yet she pressed her lips together, determined to keep the tears at bay. However, when Wanda burst through the doors, Natasha's resolve crumbled. Their eyes met — Wanda’s anguished green gaze locking onto her blurred vision — and Natasha shook her head, tears streaming down her cheeks.

She fell into Wanda’s embrace, a sob escaping her lips as she felt the warmth of her wife’s arms enveloping her, cradling her head and holding her face. Taking a deep breath, she reminded herself to breathe, to think, to find clarity amidst the chaos.

"Where are the boys?" she inquired, her voice trembling with tears. Wanda gently cupped her face, wiping away the evidence of her distress. No words were necessary for Natasha to grasp the message: take a breath, I'm here for you.

"They're sleeping. Yelena stayed with them. She wanted to come, but I insisted she remain there. They couldn't be left alone, and you're needed here," she explained, and Natasha nodded, still sniffling.

Natasha knew Yelena was likely in tears at home. Since moving to Darby, Javier had embraced her like a daughter, often saying their farm resembled a mother's heart, always open to welcome one more. Natasha recognized Yelena's deep affection for Javier, but her love for Rio was even greater, which is why she chose to stay home with the boys.

While Javier served as a father figure to Natasha, Yelena viewed him as a grandfather. It might sound unusual to others, but she considered Rio a maternal influence despite their relatively small age difference. When she first arrived in Darby, she wanted nothing to do with the place, but Rio, with her complex nature, took her under her wing. They shared a profound, unspoken bond, and Rio became her mentor.

“How is he?” Wanda asked, and once again, a sob escaped Natasha’s lips, followed by an unexpected groan that dissolved back into tears.

No further words were necessary for Wanda to grasp the gravity of the situation. “Honey, I’m so sorry.” Wanda’s face radiated compassion, and Natasha noticed the glimmer of tears in her eyes as well. Seeking solace, she leaned into Wanda’s embrace, and her wife held her close.

“Rio doesn’t know yet,” Natasha managed to say, and her wife’s eyes widened with concern as she cupped her face. “I just couldn’t tell her, not over the phone.”

"Where is she?"

“I don’t know, probably out of town with Bucky,” Natasha replied, shaking her head as tears streamed down her cheeks. “But she’s on her way.”

“She left him here alone?” Wanda’s voice carried a sharp edge of indignation. “How could she—”

"He was doing better this morning," Natasha interjected, tears in her eyes but determination in her gaze. Wanda shook her head in disbelief, her expression clearly disapproving.

Natasha sighed heavily; this wasn’t the time for that argument.

"He really was, Wanda! She spent the morning with him; they walked through the vineyard. She left here feeling optimistic, saying he was strong as a bull."

"It's been months," Wanda murmured quietly, lowering her face to ensure Evanora wouldn't overhear. "He hasn’t been well for months, and she hardly stays home, always drinking out there—"

"Honey, please, not now." Natasha implored, her voice barely above a whisper. "Just... please," she added, worry etched on her brow. Finally, with a heavy sigh, Wanda relented.

Their moment was abruptly interrupted as the doors swung open. Stumbling in, Rio kicked off her boots to shake off the dirt, blissfully unaware of the situation as always.

"I was in Bell Crossing, but I rode my horse," she whispered urgently, brushing herself off and stomping her boots while awkwardly smoothing her jeans.

Natasha could feel her wife's intense gaze without even turning: "She's drunk," Wanda murmured, her sigh tinged with disapproval.

"Even at a gallop; it took me over an hour, but I came as fast as I could. What happened? How is he?"

Rio finally took in her surroundings, her flustered expression quickly morphing into confusion as she sensed the heavy atmosphere. Her brows furrowed upon seeing Evanora in tears, and her gaze immediately turned to Natasha for answers. All Natasha could do was lower her head, but before she could speak, Lilia appeared at the top of the stairs with Doctor Morrison.

"I'm so sorry; there wasn't much that could be done," the doctor's sorrowful tone resonated through the living room. "It was sudden."

"God..." Lilia cried, tears streaming down her face. "I'll call Benny."

"What happened?" Rio's voice pierced the silence like thunder. "Where's my father?"

Her demeanor shifted completely, her brown eyes wide with urgency and her brow deeply furrowed. With determined strides, she hurried toward the stairs, only to stop short at the sight of Lilia's bowed head. Rio let out a dry, scornful laugh, shaking her head as tears began to well up in her eyes.

"He was fine!" she shouted, fervently rejecting the harsh reality, her gaze searching each person in the room for answers. "He was fine this morning! I was with him!" she fumed, yearning for someone to break the heavy silence of grief that enveloped the room.

"Rio..." Lilia spoke softly, her eyes cast down.

"No." Her tone was resolute.

"Rio, I'm so sorry," Lilia offered gently.

"No!" she shouted, storming out with fierce determination.

"Rio!" Natasha called out loudly, but she was already rushing through the door. "Rio!" she cried, but Rio didn’t look back, mounting her horse in one fluid motion. "Rio, please!"

But she didn't hear, nor did she glance back, galloping away into the night.

 

 

Chapter 3: doldrums

“I got the things I wanted, it’s just not what I imagined. Sometimes I feel like I don’t wanna be where I am, counting all of the beautiful things I regret, pushed away all the people who know me the best. But it’s me who’s been making the bed” – Making the bed, Olivia Rodrigo

Agatha let out a heavy sigh as she walked deliberately through the school corridors. She gave a hesitant nod to a few teachers and staff members she recognized, unfortunately, for all the wrong reasons. This was the third or fourth time that month, and she felt utterly lost. Deep down, she knew exactly what needed to be done, yet she felt powerless and mentally exhausted.

Taking a deep breath, she stepped into the room, feeling a wave of disappointment as the teacher welcomed her with a kind smile. In one of the back chairs, Nicholas was absorbed in his own world, coloring with a vibrant array of colored pencils. If he noticed her arrival, he certainly didn't show it, and the familiarity of his indifference only compounded her hurt.

"Hi, Agatha. I’m sorry to pull you away from work," Alice, the teacher, said in a soothing tone that only amplified Agatha's sense of helplessness. Still, she managed a weak smile and shook her head, downplaying the seriousness of the situation. After all, she hardly worked anymore. "But we really need to talk."

With a resigned sigh, she sat in the chair pulled out for her, a few feet away from her son, who remained engrossed in his coloring, his expression calm as ever.

"I spoke with your wife on the phone, and she wasn't very receptive. That’s why I thought it best to reach out to you directly. Nicky is a wonderful boy, but you know he requires... special attention."

Agatha was fond of Alice; she was attentive and persistent, truly a natural with children. Among all Nicholas's teachers, she was the most concerned and insistent. Agatha pressed her lips together, imagining Tessa's reaction to that phone call.

"He really needs this, Agatha, especially at this stage of development. He requires proper support." As Alice spoke, Agatha nodded, her gaze fixed on her son, who remained absorbed in his coloring.

"Is he falling behind in class?" she asked softly, her brow furrowing as she watched him.

"He's exceptionally smart—far beyond his peers," Alice explained, causing Agatha to raise an eyebrow and glance at the papers laid out on the table. With warmth, she examined her son's assignments. "He has an impressive memory, easily identifies patterns, shows a knack for numbers, is already reading with strong comprehension, and starting to write too."

As she listened, Agatha noted his handwriting — clumsy and slightly uneven as he wrote his name, Nicholas, the name she had lovingly chosen.

"However, he no longer participates." Agatha nodded, already aware of this. "He completes his tasks with ease, but he remains silent; there's no interest in engaging."

Agatha struggled to remember the last time he had uttered a word; it felt like ages ago.

From his earliest developmental milestones, Agatha recognized that Nicholas was unique. Initially, this distinction filled her with pride. He was eager to learn, stacking objects at an early age and identifying numbers and colors, yet he grappled with social interactions. Public environments overwhelmed him; loud noises and chatter unsettled him. He often cried and covered his ears, and babysitters found it challenging to manage his behavior.

Nicholas struggled significantly with self-expression, often finding it difficult to finish a sentence without feeling frustrated or upset. His communication relied heavily on gestures, grunts, and occasional outbursts. Tessa described him as having a strong personality, possibly with anger issues, while also noting his shyness. They tried various activities — music, arts, sports — where he found fleeting joy when engaged, but she sensed deeper struggles beneath the surface. He had no friends and seldom interacted with other children, primarily communicating only with family members, and even then, his words were limited. This led her to research autism spectrum disorder.

Nicholas exhibited signs of selective mutism.

Yet, he did speak, at least to her. He communicated with Benito, Kate, Alex, and his teachers, but only in comfortable environments with familiar faces. Over time, however, his verbal communication decreased until he barely spoke at all. Despite their attempts to engage him, he often remained silent, occasionally uttering a word or two when necessary.

"He hasn't been speaking at home either," she admitted, lowering her gaze.

"Please don’t take this the wrong way, but have you thought about my suggestion?" Alice asked softly.

Agatha raised an eyebrow, opening her mouth to reply but struggled to find the right words, her expression betraying her discomfort.

"We're working on it," she finally said, attempting to inject certainty into her voice, but Alice's hopeful nod only deepened her unease. "It's a sensitive subject."

***

Still parked, Agatha gripped the steering wheel tightly and took a deep breath. In the rearview mirror, she spotted her son, his head resting against the window, silent and distant, his expression utterly apathetic.

"Nicky," she said softly, watching as he finally turned his gaze toward her. She furrowed her brows, her plea evident. "Can you talk to me?" He met her eyes for a brief moment before returning his focus to the window. Defeated, she closed her eyes.

As tears threatened to spill, Agatha swallowed hard and squeezed her eyes shut, determined to hold back her emotions. When she finally opened them, her gaze fell upon her hands, lingering on her wedding ring: a thick white gold band adorned with tiny diamonds, delicate flowers glimmering in the light.

She couldn't help but wonder how things had spiraled to this point.

***

Thirteen years ago

Agatha had grown accustomed to Tessa's spontaneous ideas; they were part of her charm from the start—a true free spirit, always unpredictable and impulsive. She vividly remembered Tessa's first unexpected invitation, delivered with such casualness that it felt perfectly normal. After all, what better way to connect than by traveling together?

They first crossed paths on campus. Agatha, a freshman, had just started classes, and her roommate Alex was relentless in trying to convince her to attend a senior party. "It's not just a party; it's networking. That's how law school works," she insisted.

The party was held at a fraternity house, an overwhelming sight for Agatha, who had never experienced anything like it. The place buzzed with students from every major and year. Yet, the first thing that caught her eye was Tessa.

It was hard to miss her, considering two enormous, shirtless guys were hoisting her onto their shoulders while she laughed, a whimsical crown perched on her head. She had just set a record for most wins at beer pong.

Agatha had seen Tessa around campus before; she was one of the senior students tasked with welcoming freshmen that semester. With her layered brown hair cascading to her shoulders and striking blue eyes, Tessa radiated a carefree spirit, always laughing. Coming from a long lineage of esteemed judges and well-established in foreign trade, Tessa epitomized old money.

"Hey there, freshman! I heard you're from Derby," Tessa began, casually handing Agatha the beer bottle she had been sipping, her smile filled with mischief. Agatha rolled her eyes, "Where’s that?"

"It’s Darby," she corrected, and Tessa nodded, licking her lips, her gaze fixed intently on Agatha. The crooked crown atop Tessa's head made Agatha chuckle. "It’s in Montana."

"I’ve never heard of it. Maybe I’ll add it to my travel plans if you promise it’s as beautiful as you are."

At first, Agatha had no interest in Tessa. For months, she remained indifferent to everyone, steadfast in her feelings. Yet, Tessa's unwavering persistence slowly won her over.

It was the small gestures that started to captivate her — Tessa's thoughtful acts.

Throughout the first semester, while Agatha buried herself in hours of studying at the library, reluctant to admit her struggles, Tessa would simply show up, sit at her table, and quietly study alongside her. Whenever Agatha frowned or lingered too long on a challenging topic, Tessa would spark a conversation about it. This was one of the first things that piqued Agatha's interest: Tessa's remarkable intelligence; she excelled in every subject they covered. Almost daily, she spent her late nights in the library with Agatha, willingly revisiting topics from previous semesters, all just to spend time with her.

Then came the flowers, sweets, and chocolates; Tessa would occasionally send them to Agatha's dorm, each time accompanied by a poem or a book recommendation. As time passed, Agatha found herself eagerly awaiting Tessa's little verses, immersing herself in the books she suggested, even waking up early to catch her at the debate club. Their connection flourished, leading Agatha to finally agree to a first date. And who could blame her? She was trying to move on.

Tessa was a whirlwind, unlike anyone Agatha had ever met; she always had something unexpected up her sleeve. Agatha couldn't quite grasp how, but Tessa was an endless source of surprises, turning every moment into an adventure.

Before classes began, Agatha ventured to Los Angeles, eager to explore the landmarks that had filled her dreams. She made it a point to visit every tourist spot, yet Tessa always had something new planned, introducing Agatha to the city's hidden gems that she never would have considered.

Like Agatha, Tessa harbored an insatiable thirst for adventure and discovery; she was never one to settle down, always looking for the next thrilling destination. As a result, Agatha experienced moments and places she had never dreamed of.

As her first year of college drew to a close and vacation approached, Agatha found herself nearly packed for her trip home. Despite her best efforts to ignore it, the butterflies in her stomach were impossible to shake. She and Tessa had been casually dating for a while, but nothing too serious. Just two days before her departure, Tessa suggested they spend New Year’s Eve in New York.

“What?” Agatha exclaimed, her expression a blend of disbelief and surprise, while Tessa dismissed it casually, as if suggesting a simple outing to watch the sunset at the pier.

"Haven't you ever wanted to go to New York?"

"Are you kidding?" Agatha asked, a look of confusion crossing her face, but Tessa's demeanor remained earnest.

"New Year's Eve in New York is the most magical experience ever, trust me," Tessa insisted, her excitement palpable. Agatha almost laughed; she had never been to New York, but the allure was common knowledge. "I'ts something you absolutely have to do at least once in your life and I really want you to go with me."

"Are you truly serious?" Agatha questioned, and Tessa nodded emphatically. Agatha burst out laughing.

"You always say we're getting to know each other," Tessa shrugged. "What better way to connect than by travelling together?" Agatha opened her mouth to respond, but Tessa was quicker. "Seriously, I'm sure you'll love it. I know I will if you come with me."

From that moment on, the world felt smaller for the two of them.

Years later, they had traveled almost everywhere in the country together, even venturing overseas to sections of South and Central America. Tessa, always brimming with fresh ideas, always seeking out new destinations.

Yet, when Tessa brought up a trip to Paris, Agatha felt a hunch that this time, Tessa had something grander in mind. And she was right.

Tessa had chosen a rooftop restaurant with a dazzling view of the Eiffel Tower, and Agatha had to concede that, despite having been to countless places, nothing could compare to the beauty of the Parisian night. The glowing Tower, the warm yellow lights, the lush gardens, and the distant couples looking like tiny ants from that height — it was a picture straight out of a movie. A romantic movie, like the ones she had loved since childhood.

Usually, Agatha would be ecstatic, but Tessa’s palpable nervousness and anxiety confirmed her long-held suspicion; her premonition had been a constant whisper for months. She knew. More than anything, Agatha wanted to embrace the happiness, yet guilt was consuming her from within. As Tessa’s sparkling blue eyes shone, all Agatha could see were those deep, jabuticaba eyes, holding a completely different emotion just a few days ago. The joy in Tessa's gaze sharply contrasted with the emptiness in Rio's, and though Agatha desperately tried to push the thought away, remorse continued to tear at her.

When Tessa pulled a small box from her pocket, her eyes glistening with tears and a nervous smile trembling on her lips, Agatha finally grasped the meaning of bittersweetness.

Guilt wrestled fiercely with her rising happiness. She felt joy; she truly wanted this; it was the life she had always dreamed of. She loved Tessa. So, she smiled, and before the affirmative left her lips, she made a silent promise: to never again let the past cloud her present, to fully honor the gift of living this dream with a woman who seemed almost too good to be true, a woman who embodied everything she desired. And then, she said yes.

She said yes to the life she had always longed for. The past would finally be behind her; her future was anchored firmly in this present moment.

***

Present Day

Agatha couldn't pinpoint when her dream life started to fall apart. It dissolved so subtly that by the time she noticed, it was already in ruins.

She should have seen the signals — the moment the sparkle faded from Tessa's eyes when she looked at her, the first hint of possessiveness. She should have reacted when Tessa's voice rose, when the intention was clearly to silence her. As the moments of anger began to overshadow the affection, she should have stepped in, should have spoken up. Instead, she stayed quiet, convincing herself it was just a temporary phase, a difficult patch. Every marriage endured rough times; theirs would too. Then came the late nights, the incessant business trips — did a prosecutor genuinely need to be away so often? The indifference was undeniable. The full realization hit her only when her life had morphed from a fairy tale into that of a standard housewife, one face among countless others.

She was no longer Tessa's partner, travel companion, favorite person, or the adventurous young woman eager to explore the world. She had become Tessa's wife — Agatha, the wife and mother, the stable one.

She couldn't recall when this shift started, when she began prioritizing stability, building a home, and setting down roots. Yet, Agatha believed this evolution was necessary; they were married now with a child. Stability was vital for a family. The adventurous girlfriend had become the dependable wife — a constant fixture. It didn't take long for her to realize this transformation was deeply incompatible with her wife's free spirit.

Whatever Tessa had envisioned for her future and her marriage, it clearly involved spontaneity and freedom. They had both said "I do" to their individual dream lives, but it took years for them to realize those dreams were fundamentally mismatched.

In her office, Agatha held her face in one hand, her gaze fixed on the single photograph on her desk: a treasured snapshot from New Year's Eve in New York, where she and Tessa were each kissing the cheek of their son, then only a few months old.

That day remained vivid in her memory; it had felt like an absolute dream. She genuinely believed they were living a fairy tale. Two women deeply in love, first-time mothers, giddy with joy over the little one that had just joined their family.

Nicholas cried incessantly, prompting Tessa, on the night of December 31st, to embark on a frantic search for baby earmuffs. She hunted across the city for an open children's store, and when she finally found one, she called Agatha, celebrating the victory as if she'd won a race. They spent hours laughing, jokingly teasing each other about how the two clumsiest people they knew had somehow become mothers.

Agatha had been utterly happy. They were consumed by joy.

The most painful truth was that her past, which Agatha had always feared would ruin things, hadn't shattered their life. No, she had genuinely moved on, honoring her promise. Not only did she want to keep living that dream, but she also wanted Tessa to fulfill her dreams, and for them to share those aspirations. When she said "yes," she committed completely, dedicating herself from that moment on to nurturing their present with love, care, partnership, and the unique spark that defined their connection.

It wasn't the past or her loyalty that unraveled their marriage; it was Tessa.

Tessa, with her deep need for freedom, her aversion to settling down, and her craving for the unexpected, struggled against routine. Tessa constantly chased novelty, eager for fresh experiences. But as the years of marriage passed, finding those new adventures became progressively harder.

As Agatha continued to stare at the photograph, the phone rang. Confusion washed over her as she saw Darby's area code light up the screen. Her mother rarely called; Agatha was usually the one initiating her trips to Los Angeles.

"Mom?" she answered, her brow furrowing in confusion. She tried to steady the slight tremble in her voice, which always surfaced when she reflected too deeply on her current circumstances.

"It's Lilia, my angel," the voice on the other end replied, and for the first time in days, a genuine smile crossed Agatha's face, despite her tears.

"Lilia, I've missed you so much!" The warmth in her aunt's voice soothed her. "How are things? Is Mom alright? Did something happen?"

"She's fine, dear." Agatha frowned at the curt reply and noted the unusual lack of enthusiasm in her aunt's tone. "But yes, something did happen." Lilia's voice broke, and Agatha soon heard her sobbing. Instantly, she sat bolt upright, a wave of alarm washing over her, accompanied by a gnawing sense that something was seriously wrong. Lilia rarely cried over anything minor. "Have you spoken to Benito? Have you seen him today?"

"He was supposed to come here this weekend with Kate, but I haven't heard from him today," she admitted, her curiosity intensifying. "I saw he called several times, but I was at a parent-teacher meeting, and then I..." Agatha hesitated, unsure how to explain. What could she say? That she'd been crying about her life for hours? "I was going to call him back later. But what happened?"

"Agatha, your godfather has passed away."

Agatha was instantly speechless. It felt as if her thoughts, words, and energy had been completely drained, leaving only a profound emptiness in her chest. This void, first created after her father's death, was one she had tried to mend by moving forward. Now, that emptiness grew vast, igniting a deep internal ache, as if an old wound had been violently torn open.

"Agatha?" Lilia's voice broke through, checking if she was still there.

"I'm here," she managed to whisper back.

"I called Benny; he was trying to reach you because he needs you to come for the funeral, to come here to Darby. I know it's been a long time, and you prefer not to talk about it, but he'll need your support. Your mom will too—all of us, honey."

The last time Agatha had set foot in Darby was thirteen years ago. She hadn't been back since months before her wedding. Her mother and Lilia often visited her in Los Angeles, and Benito lived just a few blocks away. Javier came to visit sometimes; there had never been a reason for her to return.

"Go to Darby?" Agatha managed to say, her voice thick with reluctance.

"He was your godfather, Agatha, practially your second father."

That was undeniably true. Javier had always treated her like his own daughter, seeing her as such. Every time she came home from college, she was welcomed with celebrations. After her father died, Javier stepped into that role; when Benito went to college in Los Angeles, he stayed with her for a long time, and Javier was always closely involved. He even traveled all the way to Los Angeles just to be there for Nicholas's first birthday. He never missed sending gifts on her wedding anniversaries — presents Tessa adored — along with letters that Agatha kept hidden. In those letters, he expressed his happiness for her but confessed he had always pictured himself as her father-in-law. He wrote that every single year. More than just a godfather, he truly was her second father.

"Lilia, I-" She faltered, exhaling deeply, still grappling with the heartbreaking news. "I need a moment to breath. Can I call you back later?"

"Of course, my dear. I know this is a heavy loss for you too."

Still, the second she hung up, her mind zeroed in on Rio. No one could be feeling this profound loss as intensely as she was; no one had loved Javier more. He had always been Rio's hero, her secure harbor. Rio and her father shared a bond that was truly unique. Agatha's hands shook as she forcefully shook her head, trying to ward off those memories. She didn't need to dive into that history now; she just needed to steady herself.

She absolutely could not think about Rio, not now, not ever again. She had given up that right thirteen years ago.

It was time to concentrate on herself: take a deep breath, confront her own emotions and sorrow, and figure out the path forward.

Slumped in her office armchair, lost in a blur of tears and scattered thoughts, she tried calling Tessa at least twenty times, but every call went unanswered, routing straight to voicemail. Uncertainty hung over her; she had no idea if Tessa would even come home that day, as she sometimes stayed out without a word.

She desperately wished Tessa would pick up, just to show she cared.

Agatha quietly entered Nicholas's room, careful to open the door with minimal sound. Her son was asleep, clutching the stuffed horse Benito had given him. In that silent moment, seeing his serenity offered a glimmer of solace; watching him at peace allowed her to finally breathe.

She grabbed her phone one last time and dialed again, but Tessa still didn't answer.

In that very moment, she decided she had to take control.

Chapter 4: dream

Chapter Notes

hi, just a quick note: the story's present isn't set in our current present. it's about ten years ago. while characters have laptops and smartphones, the cultural landscape differs significantly from today. social media isn't THAT dominant yet; people are less reliant on constant connectivity and screens in a way that digital life was present but not all-consuming like today

“That’s a real fucking legacy, to leave” – Maroon, Taylor Swift.

People often praise the virtue of perseverance and the honor of commitment, but few recognize the profound courage required to simply choose to let go. To release your grip, to pause, to step away when everything you want feels just within reach. For Agatha, surrendering was the toughest act of all.

It's hard to explain where an idea starts or the precise moment it blooms in our minds. It's even harder to understand why we sometimes become fixated on things born purely from imagination. Everyone holds a unique vision of happiness, success, and love—concepts that change as we do, remaining abstract and often detached from reality. Even when we have so much, we inevitably long for what is just out of our reach; we constantly chase what we don't possess. This is the paradox of dreams: their enchantment lies exactly in their distance from the reality.

Plato captured this idea, using love as a metaphor for desire: love is the pursuit of the beloved, not the act of possession, but the journey itself. We rarely desire what we already have; there's no necessity for it. If we crave something, it's because we lack it. Once we obtain it, the desire often vanishes.

When you aspire to something, it suggests a lack, meaning you don't dream of what you already possess. The urgency of need drives determination; it pushes us ahead. This explains why ambition feels endless: there is always a craving for something extra — something better, something still outside your grasp. While we often associate ambition with massive success, it also influences the minor details of daily life, showing up as a constant drive for improvement or acquisition. There is always that push for more.

An ideal is permanently an abstraction, constantly evolving, forever just beyond our reach — a goal we strive to meet, yet one we never fully grasp. If we were to achieve an ideal, it would stop being an ideal and become our reality instead.

Agatha had always been a dreamer.

Growing up on a farm, she yearned to explore the city. Once she saw the city, her visions grew grander, until she discovered Los Angeles—the city of angels, where dreams supposedly came true. All the excitement happened in Los Angeles, the sanctuary of success, films, and aspirations. Her goals were about two thousand kilometers away. When she finally arrived in California, clutchng her university acceptance letter, she was ecstatic, spending days exploring rather than confining herself to her room. With endless places to see, books to read, and people to meet, the initial excitement eventually gave way to routine, leaving her with a lingering question: "now what?"

Unbeknownst to her, her initial dream had transformed into a new one, and her desires constantly seemed just ahead, pushing her to strive, to succeed, to meet her potential. Throughout her life, she fought tirelessly for her dreams, yet each success led to a new challenge; the struggles were continuous. She never saw her choices as a series of losses; she always felt she was gaining, not giving up.

She had always focused on her aspirations, never grasping that moving forward also meant leaving things behind. Gaining one thing often necessitated losing another; they weren't opposites, but inseparable parts of the same journey.

Her heart no longer craved something more; instead, it sorrowed for what she had given up. It was deeply ironic, since her losses were only concepts; what she mourned had never truly had the chance to materialize. She couldn't even name exactly what she had lost — how could she? If a single detail had been different, everything would have changed. But now, she found herself completely devoid of dreams. All that remained was despair, an emptiness filled not with her failures, but with a sharp sense of nostalgia. The drive to continue moving forward had vanished.

Thirteen years ago, she promised herself that the future would become her present. Now, she understood this was her mistake. The future is an ideal, not a reality. In chasing that ideal, she sacrificed the one thing she possessed — the present — failing to realize that tomorrow would always just turn into today.

For the first time in over a decade, she decided to stop pushing forward. She surrendered.

Stepping out of the autopilot that had always propelled her, she felt completely disoriented. Agatha knew she was terrible at assessing the fallout of her decisions, and as they landed at Missoula airport, a knot of fear tightened in her stomach.

Darby didn't have an airport; reaching the town meant flying to Missoula and then driving for an hour and a half. Gripping the steering wheel of the rental car, she started to wonder if this had been a good decision. It didn't take long to conclude that no, it was a terrible idea, yet it was the only option left. If she wasn't going to keep moving ahead, there was only one direction she could go: home.

With her eyes on the road, she nervously bit her lip, desperately trying to convince herself that she hadn't fled. It wasn't an escape; it was a visit—she had always enjoyed traveling. Not to Darby, she chided herself, letting out a frustrated sigh. Her godfather had died, her family needed her, and she needed to navigate that grief too; this was a family trip.

So what if it had been thirteen years since she last saw Darby?

"Family trip," she repeated mentally.

Yet, a red siren blared in her mind, that unsettling knot in her stomach continued to twist, and her palms grew slick. "Family trip." She forced herself to recite the words, inhaling deeply, trying to believe that if she said it enough, it would become true.

It wouldn't be long before Tessa realized she was gone. Tessa never stayed away from home for more than a couple of days and might not even care, but Agatha knew perfectly well that it wouldn't take her long to notice that more than half of the wardrobe was missing.

"Family trip." It wasn't a total lie, but she would soon have to commit to a decision.

Through the rearview mirror, she caught her son’s eye and swallowed hard when their gazes met. He remained silent, never questioning her frantic packing, never protesting at any point. While she packed, tears streaming down her face, he simply watched, his brow furrowed with concern.

She could sense the questions in his eyes, alongside a glimmer of understanding, and she longed for him to speak. For a brief second, she thought he might, but he remained quiet.

Nicholas had large brown eyes with a gaze that seemed to pierce her soul, as if he could read every detail, every emotion, every thought. He didn't need words to communicate his understanding of the situation or the reason for her tears. Silently, he met her gaze and began helping her gather clothes from the closet, sorting through his toys and colored pencils, filling a backpack with his favorite things. Agatha said nothing, and he asked no questions, yet he understood. He recognized this was more than just a family trip. Even in his quietness, she felt his steady support.

His eyes, locked onto hers in the rearview mirror, radiated genuine curiosity and empathy, tinged with a hint of affection. Though he didn't speak, his insight was profound.

Nicholas’s large brown eyes resembled polished marbles, and Agatha would be lying if she didn't admit they reminded of her. His were a rich, dark brown, like an earthy, almost black tree trunk. When Javier first saw him as a baby, he remarked that the boy had little jabuticaba eyes. Tessa found the compliment sweet, but Agatha couldn't help but think that he indeed shared Rio's jabuticaba eyes.

She stopped trying to suppress thoughts of Rio; it was futile now that she was returning home. It was impossible to think of Darby without thinking of Rio; they were intertwined in a way that had forced her to stay away for so many years. She had to abandon Darby to escape Rio.

Amidst the emotional chaos surrounding her, she wondered how Rio was coping now. Likely devastated after her father's death, a complete wreck. But beyond the immediate grief, Agatha found herself curious about Rio's life—what she had been doing and how she had moved on. Throughout her own journey of moving forward, she had never dared to ask if Rio had done the same, or what path she had chosen. Despite spending significant time with Javier and Benito, she lacked the courage to ask; she felt she had no right.

It had been thirteen years since she had stepped foot in Darby. Thirteen years since their last conversation. In that time, they had only been in the same place once — at Agatha's father's funeral, but that was different, it didn't truly count as an encounter. Their last genuine conversation happened thirteen years ago, and it was hardly a pleasant memory; it left her with nothing good to recall.

Now, she couldn't help but wonder how Rio would react upon seeing her there, in their hometown, after all this time.

***

Thirteen years ago

Las Vegas was undeniably exhilarating, and both Agatha and Tessa savored every moment of their first honeymoon day, enjoying drinks at the city's most famous casinos. Their rule was simple: just one poker game at each venue. By the end of the day, they had visited over seven casinos, each time spinning a new tale about how they met and fell in love.

Back in their hotel room, tipsy and carefree, they shared their first night as a married couple on the sofa, their movements slow and clumsy, punctuated by the lingering laughter from their evening of revelry. It was a beautiful moment: their bodies entwined without haste, exchanging deep, languorous kisses accompanied by soft sighs.

A wave of satisfaction washed over Agatha, her earlier intoxication mellowing into gentle drowsiness. It wasn't long before they both tumbled into bed, falling into a deep slumber while holding each other close.

When the incessant ringing of a phone roused Agatha, she groaned in protest and buried her head under the pillow, but the sound didn't stop. With another grunt, she nudged Tessa gently. Tessa stirred, confused, and let out her own protest, pulling Agatha back into a warm embrace.

"Baby..." Agatha managed to groan, gesturing toward the persistent phone ringing. "My head is throbbing; please make it stop."

With an annoyed sigh, Tessa reached for the phone on the nightstand but found it turned off. "It's not mine," she mumbled, sinking back into the pillow.

Still with her head under the pillow, Agatha groped for her own phone on her side of the bed and grasped the vibrating, ringing device. The tequila had left her with a pounding headache, so she answered without checking the caller ID.

"Hello?" she mumbled groggily into the phone.

"Why did you answer?" Tessa grumbled, rolling over in bed. "You should've just hung up."

"Hello, my love. How's your honeymoon?" That all-too-familiar voice instantly chased the sleep from Agatha's body, making her sit up straight in bed, eyes wide, heart pounding with anxiety. "Did I call at a bad time, or are we still in the same time zone?"

"Who is it?" Tessa asked, still half-asleep. Agatha waved her hand dismissively, indicating it was nothing serious. "Then hang up."

"I'll hang up shortly, love, just a minute." She kissed Tessa's forehead before slipping out of the room.

"I hate it when you call her 'love'," Rio grumbled on the other end of the line.

"Are you out of your fucking mind?" Agatha hissed in a low, urgent tone, glancing over her shoulder to ensure Tessa was still in the bedroom and couldn't hear. "Why are you calling me in the middle of the night? During my fucking honeymoon!"

"Ouch!" Rio replied, feigning offense, which only made Agatha's anxiety worsen as her palms grew sweaty. Tessa remained blissfully unaware of the unexpected call. "I thought you'd show a little more affection after our encounter two nights ago, or have you already forgotten?"

"No, I haven't forgotten what happened two nights ago: my wedding." Agatha kept her voice steady, ensuring her resolve was clear.

"C'mon cariño, you know I'm not referring to that part." Agatha silently cursed herself as her cheeks flushed, betraying her reaction to Rio's suggestive tone, but she refused to engage further and simply let out a sharp breath.

"Rio," Agatha whispered, pacing the suite's living room, her eyes glued to the bedroom door — Tessa couldn't possibly imagine this conversation. "Don't call me again. Ever."

"Agatha, please don't hang up! This is serious!" Rio nearly shouted from the other end, prompting Agatha to let out a heavy sigh. "I was arrested. I'm at the police station right now, and I only get one call—this one."

"You what?!" she nearly shrieked, quickly clapping a hand over her mouth, hoping she hadn't woken Tessa. Too late. Seconds later, Tessa appeared, groggy and clad in a bathrobe, leaning against the bedroom doorframe, her sleepy eyes filled with curiosity.

"They caught me in the car, and you know they have that breathalyzer thing now..." Rio's casual tone only escalated Agatha's anxiety, especially under Tessa's inquiring gaze.

"How much did you drink?" she asked, striving to maintain her composure.

"Enough for them to arrest me."

"Was there an accident? Are you okay?" she asked with an exasperated sigh, glancing back at Tessa, who was now fully alert and signaling for details. Agatha mouthed that she would explain soon.

"No, no accident, I was just driving... fast." Rio confessed with a mischievous tone, eliciting another frustrated huff from Agatha. "The police stopped me, made me take the test, and brought me here."

"Here? Where is here?" she asked, her patience wearing thin as her palms began to sweat.

"San Diego."

"What in God's name were you doing in San Diego?" Agatha couldn't hide the irritation in her voice.

"Who is it?" Tessa asked. Agatha paused, staring blankly at her for a moment.

"My godfather. He got caught drunk driving," she blurted out thoughtlessly, causing Tessa to roll her eyes before turning back toward the bedroom.

"Did you really tell your wife you're talking to my dad, or did I mishear?" Rio chuckled, and Agatha could only let out a puff of air, her hands clammy.

"Yes, Uncle Javi," she replied through gritted teeth, as Rio's laughter echoed across the line. "It sounds like you need a lawyer."

"You are my lawyer," Rio stated, as if it were the most obvious fact in the world.

"No, I'm not, and even if I were, I'm currently in Las Vegas in the middle of my fucking honeymoon," Agatha hissed, dropping her voice now that Tessa was out of earshot.

"Agatha, I only had the right to this one call, and yours is the only number I know by heart. I can't call another lawyer."

"I can call your dad; I'm sure he knows someone."

"Agatha, no! You can't tell my dad I got arrested! Absolutely not!"

"The only person who might agree to help you—to help me—is Alex, but she left for New York yesterday. She's not going to San Diego just to bail you out."

"Agatha, please."

"What do you expect me to do? Fly to San Diego in the middle of my honeymoon to pay your bail and get you out of jail?" Agatha let out a humorless laugh, rolling her eyes at the sheer absurdity. It was pathetic. She and Rio were two utter fools.

"Yeah, that's why I called you. It's less than two hours away; there's no need to be dramatic."

"You must be kidding me."

"I'm sorry, okay? But my dad can't find out. He has no idea I'm in California, and I'd be on my way home if these idiots hadn't arrested me. You can't tell him, or your mom, or Lilia—seriously. I'm begging you, Agatha. I know this is a messed-up situation, but I didn't do it deliberately. I genuinely need your help here, come on."

This felt like a nightmare, a cruel joke; there was no other explanation for why life was dealing her this hand.
