As Rio voiced her frustration on the other end, Agatha squeezed her eyes shut, trying to filter her thoughts and feelings, an immense weight pressing on her chest. She glanced at her left hand, the white gold wedding band adorned with tiny diamonds, and closed her eyes once more. This would be the last time, she promised herself.

***

Among all the scenarios she'd imagined for her honeymoon, a heated argument with Tessa was definitely not one of them. Yet, here they were.

Despite her own justifications, Agatha knew she couldn't ignore Tessa's point of view. She couldn't help but wonder how she would react if their roles were reversed — if Tessa had booked a flight and, barely a day into their honeymoon, announced a family emergency in the middle of the night. As Tessa paced the room, radiating frustration, Agatha found it impossible to meet her gaze.

"You've got to be kidding me!" Tessa exclaimed, her laughter humorless, arms tightly crossed as she moved back and forth, shaking her head in disbelief. "Agatha, it's our honeymoon!"

Agatha raised her head but quickly looked away from Tessa's wide, furrowed brows that clearly showed her anger. Tessa had every right to be furious, and Agatha was consumed by self-reproach. She always hated lying to Tessa, but this time it felt particularly excruciating. The confusion on Tessa's face and the hurt reflected in her blue eyes made Agatha feel like the worst person alive.

But that was exactly why she had to do this; Tessa deserved more than a partial love — she deserved all of Agatha. She had promised herself she wouldn't make this mistake again; she genuinely wanted their relationship to thrive. She had chosen Tessa and intended to commit completely, just as Tessa had done years ago.

Tessa deserved all of her, so Agatha had to finally bury her past once and for all.

Just one more lie to bring closure to all the others.

"What do you expect me to do?" Agatha replied firmly, still unable to meet her eyes. "It's my godfather, Tessa! He doesn't know a single person in California; he's miles from home! Do you want me to let him to spend the night in jail?"

Tessa let out a sharp, purely disbelieving laugh, devoid of any humor.

"Are you the only lawyer on the planet? He's rich, Agatha! He knows dozens of lawyers! It's our honeymoon!" she nearly shouted, her tone emphasizing the sheer ridiculousness of the situation, making Agatha drop her head. "I'm not suggesting you leave him locked up; I'm asking why you can't just call someone else for help."

"He's family, Tessa; he trusts me." Tessa narrowed her eyes, clearly unconvinced. "I don't know anyone in San Diego who can help right now; who am I supposed to call in the middle of the night? Do you think anyone from my family, way out in Montana, knows a lawyer in San Diego? The only person who could help is Alex, and she's in New York right now."

"What was this hick doing driving drunk in San Diego instead of mucking out a barn in Montana?" Tessa grumbled, her voice rising in frustration.

Agatha felt an immediate urge to reprimand her; she hated Tessa speaking about her family like that, but she held back.

"I don't know, I didn't ask, but he rarely travels. He probably thought he'd extend his stay after our wedding to explore California. He's such a country bumpkin; he must have gotten excited about the big city." She murmured the last sentence with a hint of sarcasm, causing Tessa's brows to furrow in annoyance as she let out a heavy sigh.

Their eyes locked for what felt like an eternity until Tessa let out a heavy sigh that was half huff, half release.

"Why do I feel like you're always looking for an excuse to run away from me?" she asked, her voice tight with hurt, her brows still knotted in confusion.

That question stung more than any physical blow, and Agatha felt utterly ashamed.

"I love you," Agatha said, but Tessa looked away. "I didn't want to go, but I need to." Now, she was finally speaking a truth, however warped. She stepped closer to Tessa, reaching out to cup her face, sighing in relief when Tessa accepted her touch. Looking deeply into those blue eyes, she vowed never to inflict that pain again. "It's only a few hours, I promise." Tessa's brows narrowed, seeking reassurance, and Agatha mirrored the look, striving to convey the sincerity of her words. "Less than four hours, I promise, darling. Go back to sleep, and when you wake up, I'll already be here. I never want to run away from you; I love running away with you."

"You better be here when I wake up," Tessa murmured softly. Agatha offered a small smile.

"I will, honey. Every day." She wiggled her left hand, showcasing her ring, and Tessa rolled her eyes before leaning in to kiss her.

***

No one enjoys working late into the night, especially not police officers on duty. Thankfully, the bureaucracy presented no trouble; it took her only an hour-long flight to post bail and sign a few documents. Agatha leaned against a patrol car, watching as Rio emerged from the police station, a wide grin spreading across her face as she threw her arms out in a mock triumphant gesture.

"Free as a bird," Rio teased, shaking her now uncuffed wrists. "You truly are the best lawyer in the world."

It was clear Rio was still drunk; the scent of alcohol was obvious even from a distance. Agatha shook her head disapprovingly, but Rio simply smiled and shrugged.

Agatha couldn't help but wonder if she bore some responsibility for Rio's recklessness. Deep down, she knew she did, just as Rio’s choices reflected on her own life. Two days ago, she had tried to end this cycle, but now, in the early hours of her honeymoon, she needed certainty — it absolutely had to stop. They both need closure.

"Did you do this on purpose?" Agatha asked, a frown creasing her brow. Rio's face instantly shifted into confusion.

"Do what?" Rio replied with a laugh.

"This," Agatha said, gesturing toward the police station.

"What? Do you think I intentionally ruined your honeymoon?" Rio laughed, but Agatha remained silent, holding her gaze steady, watching as the mockery drained from Rio's expression. It hurt Agatha to see how transparent Rio was, how easily she could read the pain. "Do you truly think I would spend a night in jail just to pull you away from your madam? You've already married her; what would that achieve? Do you think I want to see that ring on your finger?" Rio let out a sarcastic breath, quickly trying to mask her feelings. "Besides, I expected more from her; she has so much money, and that's what she put on your finger?"

Agatha instinctively curled her fingers around the ring, feeling its weight as her heart began to sink.

The intensity of Rio's brown eyes shouldn't have been so painful, yet it was, as if they were crushing her heart in their grip.

"If you didn't do it on purpose, why are you still in California?" Agatha asked, her voice barely above a whisper. Rio shrugged, looking away.

"Honestly? I don't know." Rio's tone was serious now, her eyes locked on Agatha's, making a lump form in Agatha's throat. "I was just driving around; I guess part of me wanted to understand why these big cities mean so much to you." Rio shrugged again, and this time Agatha was the one who couldn't hold the eye contact. "I didn't do it on purpose, Agatha. I wouldn't do that. I wouldn't have the courage."

"But you did."

"Agatha-"

"We can't keep doing this, Rio," she said softly, and Rio frowned. The sheer vulnerability in her eyes hit Agatha like a physical blow. But this was necessary; they couldn't continue this way. "I married her."

"You love me." Rio began, as if that simple statement explained everything. "I lo—" But Agatha cut her off, shaking her head, pleading for her to stop. She couldn't bear to hear it.

"You love your home, Darby, your horses, your family, your farm... You would never give that up. You never wanted to come with me, Rio."

"That doesn't change how I feel," Rio replied, her voice thick with emotion, tears brimming in her eyes.

"You made your choice, and I made mine." Rio frowned, shaking her head, her eyes pleading with Agatha to stop. "If you truly love me, you need to let me live my life, and you need to live yours, too."

Rio stayed silent; the tears glistening in her eyes said everything. They held each other's gaze for an eternity, the silence heavy as tears streamed down Rio's cheeks. Agatha bit her lip, forcing herself not to cry; she couldn't break down in front of her.

"Take care, Rio," she whispered, but as she turned to leave, Rio grabbed her wrist with a trembling hand.

"If you walk away now, I'm not coming back, Agatha." Despite her tears, her tone was firm and absolute. "If you walk away, it's over for real."

In that moment, Agatha understood that this was genuinely the end.

"I know, that's why I have to go."

***

Present Day

Just as Agatha honored her promise, Rio did the same; she genuinely never came back. Now, as Agatha drove toward home, she wondered how Rio would react upon realizing it was she who was returning.

Agatha had no idea what Rio had become, what she did, or how she had lived her life. Since that fateful night thirteen years ago, they had crossed paths only once, at Agatha's father's wake. Their interaction was fleeting and overshadowed by Tessa’s presence. Aside from that solitary meeting, they had not seen or spoken to each other again, and their families had long since stopped meddling, carefully avoiding any mention of the other woman.

It was a cruel irony: after their final separation, only loss could bring them back together. It felt like a grotesque metaphor—they had shattered each other, and now they found themselves standing amidst the rubble.

Agatha's thoughts were abruptly interrupted by her phone ringing. She glanced at the screen, seeing Tessa’s name flash before her.

She let the call go to voicemail.

Chapter 5: emptiness

“Well, I’m tired of losing, I used to win every night of the week” – Tomorrow, Shakey Graves

Agatha was trying to focus on the road while ignoring the constant ringing of her phone. By now, she had even started to hum along to the familiar ringtone. She had lost track of how many times Tessa had called, choosing not to answer or even glance at the screen. Fortunately, Nicholas seemed equally unconcerned, absorbed in the scenery around him.

Agatha was grappling with a whirlwind of thoughts and feelings; Tessa could certainly wait. It felt refreshing not to be the one perpetually waiting for a call or a sign. She exhaled softly, imagining how her wife might react to this sudden shift in their dynamic.

Part of her was afraid; she didn't know what to expect from this and had learned a long time ago not to react. It was her role, her part. Agatha was the wife who cared for the house and the kid, who gave up her career for the marriage, while Tessa was the working wife, who had a busy social life and kept things in order. She couldn't even recall when she had stopped questioning, fighting back, or trying to understand what was happening and why. She just accepted it; it felt like the right thing to do. She felt as if it was the price she had to pay for the life she had always dreamed of.

Ultimately, she believed it was the cost of pursuing everything at once, living as if her actions had no consequences. Her feelings took precedence, overshadowing the emotions of others in her quest to fulfill her desires. After yearning for countless things simultaneously, she found herself letting them slip from her grasp. When she finally committed, the tables had turned.

She was overwhelmed with guilt, convinced she deserved her current predicament — the chaos around her was entirely her own creation. Years spent focused solely on the future had blinded her to the snowball of issues accumulating behind her. The ensuing avalanche still took her by surprise, a massive force built from her own choices, flake by flake.

As she drove down that road, it felt as though her entire life were unfolding before her like a cinematic reel.

For a decade, she made that journey every few months, and each time she passed the "Welcome to Darby!" sign, she left behind a cherished piece of herself in search of the other. For ten years, she lived two lives, divided by months, miles, and conflicting emotions she struggled to navigate, never knowing how to choose. In truth, she didn't want to; she realized that picking one would mean losing the other. So, for as long as possible, she sought to harmonize the two Agathas: the ambitious dreamer in California and the passionate spirit in Montana.

Ultimately, she became neither; she had morphed into a gray, formless entity, stripped bare of dreams.

She attempted to find solace in her new identity as Agatha, the mother, but it seemed she couldn’t even succeed at that.

Then she heard a soft, astonished "Wow," and her eyes shot to the rearview mirror, her heart racing as if jolted by a wave of euphoria. She rarely heard that voice, so each word he uttered rang like a thousand bells, no matter how quietly he spoke.

In the back seat, Nicholas was tangled in his seatbelt, attempting to kneel on the seat, his face and small hands pressed against the window, lost in a wonder she couldn't recall witnessing in a long time.

The scenery had remained largely unchanged since they hit the road in Missoula — brush, cattle, and fences stretched as far as the eye could see. Now, however, they had arrived in Darby, a land renowned for its horses, and he found himself captivated by their beauty.

The Vidals owned almost all the land in that town. Javier dabbled in various agricultural ventures, but his heart belonged to horses—a passion that deepened with Riandra by his side. Expansive stables dotted the landscape, and he had even constructed a sprawling hippodrome dedicated to equestrian pursuits, which had grown over the years; the Vidals were renowned for their equine excellence.

She knew that Rio shared her father's passions, and from what she had gathered over the years, she had turned that love into a thriving empire. Benito had mentioned a couple of times how the town was now bustling with visitors drawn in for competitions and breeding, noting how Darby had expanded to accommodate these changes. She typically dismissed such comments, often steering the conversation away whenever he mentioned Rio, but now she realized the truth of it.

The last time she visited, she had spotted a few horses from the house and noticed some in the stable; they were constructing more facilities to keep pace with the breeding, and she had seen a handful running freely in the fenced fields. Now, however, there were over a dozen — some grazing peacefully, others meandering together, and a few galloping with their manes flowing in the wind.

Nicholas was captivated, his face pressed against the window with a beaming smile, while Agatha felt an involuntary warmth spread through her heart.

She was aware of his fondness for horses, yet she had never given it much thought. After all, Los Angeles wasn’t exactly known for such pastimes, especially in their bustling, commercial neighborhood, surrounded by towering buildings and heavy traffic. The closest encounter with nature was the beach, always teeming with surfers and tourists. Nicholas wasn't fond of the beach, nor of crowded places; he had been raised in serene, enclosed environments, much to Tessa's liking.

Her wife focused more on piano lessons, languages, painting, swimming in olympic-sized pools, and other structured activities. "These are the skills he’ll showcase on his résumé one day," Tessa would often say.

Nicholas's only connection to the wild was through Javier's occasional, laid-back visits. Unfazed by the boy's quiet demeanor, Javier captivated him with tales of the ranch and its majestic horses. Though he didn’t speak much, Nicholas cherished those moments, his wide eyes filled with wonder, silently craving more stories. In an effort to draw him out, Benito began sharing his own stories, showing him photographs, and showering him with gifts: a pair of boots, a cowboy hat. It was Benny who presented him with a plush horse that Nicholas clung to even during bath time, leaving it perched on the toilet — his loyal companion and quiet confidant, Señor Scratchy.

Tessa hated it, saying she didn't want her son tainted by those "hick western tales," so Agatha refrained from sharing any. She couldn't anyway; all of hers featured Rio, and that was a name that had been banned in that household for years. Out of respect for Tessa, and everything she had caused them throughout their dating years, she kept her stories to herself, burying them so deep inside that sometimes she forgot to remember them.

All the stories of her past were buried as an apology she thought was fair at the time. Darby was left behind, along with the ranch, the vineyard, the cows, the horses, the waterfall lake, and Rio. Her life was California, tall buildings, contractual negotiations, and Tessa, her wife, who adored big cities and their expensive lifestyle. Tessa had no desire for Agatha to revisit the past, let alone for her son to aspire to be a country bumpkin.

But now, Tessa wasn't there, and she couldn’t help but feel a flicker of joy watching her son delight in his surroundings.

"Did you like the horses?" Agatha inquired, her voice laced with uncertainty as she smiled, her eyebrows furrowed in anticipation while she watched him through the rearview mirror. Doubtful that he would respond, she still held onto hope.

Her smile blossomed when he turned to her, his big brown eyes sparkling with joy, beaming a clear affirmation.

Agatha's heart swelled with love. His broad smile radiated warmth, free from his usual indifference, and she felt tears of joy welling up, all because of that smile.

"Did you know I once had a horse?" she ventured, her palms slick against the steering wheel, yet her gaze remained warm in the rearview mirror.

She noticed her son's expression shift to one of clear suspicion, his eyebrows knitting together.

"I really did! My house was practically next to a massive stable." He leaned in, intrigued, eager to catch every word. Agatha struggled to suppress her smile. "Grandma lives on a ranch brimming with Uncle Javi's horses." His brown eyes lit up. "When I was a bit older than you, I spent entire days with the horses, galloping across vast fields."

He nodded, silently urging her to continue, and all of Agatha's worries faded away, replaced by a soothing sense of nostalgia.

"My— My..." She stammered, a frown crossing her face.

How could she talk about Rio? It had been thirteen years since she last tried. The thought felt strange, sending a flutter of discomfort to the pit of her stomach. She struggled to find the right words.

"I had a... She—"

By this point, Nicholas wore a look of confusion. She sighed, letting out a nervous laugh.

"Did you know Uncle Benny has a sister?" Nicholas shook his head, his curiosity piqued. "We, she and I—" Agatha paused. "She was my best friend." It wasn't a lie; they had been best friends. "She taught me how to ride, and we would spend all day riding around these parts." She gestured toward the dirt road, and he glanced around, trying to picture it. "Look over there!" She pointed to a large construction in the distance, and his gaze snapped to it. "That's a hippodrome. Do you know what a hippodrome is?" He shook his head, his attention fully on her.

Agatha felt a surge of happiness; she couldn't recall the last time he had engaged like this.

"It's a place dedicated to horse riding. You can play polo, do vaulting, and jump with the horses. All the races take place at the hippodrome." Now he was looking at her with those wide brown eyes, filled with excitement. "Do you want to go there?" He nodded eagerly, his face lighting up like Christmas lights.

***

Like almost every decision she had made throughout her life, visiting the hippodrome was an unplanned impulse. She was so delighted by her son's excitement that she hardly considered the significance of being there — a place transformed over the years, yet heavy with countless memories and feelings.

Nicholas squeezed her hand, walking with small bounces, eagerly moving forward. Trying to disguise her furrowed brow, she swallowed hard. It was as if she had been hit by a powerful wave that had suddenly transported her nineteen years back into the past. Her son's hand was the only tangible connection to the present, while her mind painted everything in the colors of her past, as if she were still that recent college freshman on her first winter break, reuniting with family after a year apart and seeing Rio again.

It was an out-of-body sensation; everything was different, but inside, she felt the same, as if she was twenty years old again. She struggled to match Nicholas's pace, breathless from an overwhelming surge of emotions and a heavy weight in her chest. Her son’s excitement was a distant echo as she took in all the changes around her — a place that felt both familiar and foreign, much like herself.

The first time she had set foot in the Casa Vidal hippodrome was nineteen years ago, shortly after its inauguration. Before that, it was just a field with equestrian equipment and some bleachers where Javier taught riding and trained a few kids. It hardly resembled a true hippodrome. But after her departure, a lot changed, and she learned that he had built the hippodrome for Rio, so she could race.

Rio had built an empire, something she never envisioned in Darby. The main facade stood grand and symmetrical, featuring wide columns and arches, crowned by a striking Casa Vidal carving at the entrance. It seamlessly blended modernity and tradition. Every aspect of the building reflected Riandra's essence — her taste evident in the grandeur, the neutral tones, and the exquisite stained-glass windows.

As remarkable as it was, she couldn’t shake the thought that Javier had created all of this out of love, solely for his daughter to pursue the one thing he had always loathed: racing.

Javier had a deep passion for his horses; he bred them out of affection, never intending to turn it into a business venture. They were his cherished companions. He only sold the offspring to ensure he wouldn’t take on more than he could genuinely care for and oversee. Riding was merely a pastime for him; he taught children and trained them for competitions, but nothing beyond riding and jumping.

Agatha recalled vividly how adamant he was about this — his disdain for those who bred horses for profit, treating them as mere commodities, profiting from betting while the animals were exploited and discarded once they no longer performed on the tracks.

When she was just a child, Javier introduced her to the world of horses, teaching her how to care for them, showing her the joy of riding, and instilling the belief that her horse would be her lifelong companion. In the realms of riding and jumping, a horse typically reaches its prime between seven and twelve years old; it’s a journey where both horse and rider grow and evolve together. However, in the world of racing, it’s the youngest horses that often steal the spotlight. Many of them lack the physical maturity required for the strenuous demands of racing, yet the focus remains on results rather than the well-being of the horse. Breeding farms operate like factories, constantly in search of the next fast stallion that can sprint to victory and generate greater profits.

She had never seen him angry until the day he discovered Rio was racing.

Rio always held a deep passion for racing; it was an undeniable part of her. Agatha, fully aware of Javier's opinions, still couldn't blame her. She had watched this fervor blossom over the years. When Rio raced, it felt as though she and her horse moved as one. A fierce determination sparked in her eyes; nothing made her glow quite like the thrill of racing.

During their teenage years, they would hit the road together, traveling to nearby towns where Rio eagerly entered every race she found. Victory was hers, regardless of the horse — she even triumphed on those deemed unrideable. Racing ignited a flame within her that Agatha struggled to articulate; she simply saw its beauty. Rio stood apart from other racers — the look on her face, her unwavering dedication, and the profound connection she shared with her horse. Winning wasn't her goal; she raced for the sheer joy of it, she just wanted to run.

After a while, Rio started gaining a reputation. Everyone wanted to see her race, and it wasn't long before the news reached Javier's ears.

At a race in Bell Crossing, a quaint town near Darby, Rio was leading by a significant margin when Javier suddenly appeared on the track. She narrowly avoided trampling him with her horse. Though she had never heard him raise his voice before, that day, she understood why he commanded such respect. He halted the race and forcefully pulled Riandra away, shouting, while Agatha still recalls the sight of Rio with her head down, tears streaming down her cheeks. He banned her from riding for months, and they clashed daily. It felt as though a part of Rio had shattered, and she held onto her resentment for a long time, even after she was eventually allowed to ride and care for the horses again.

Despite her deep love for racing, she chose to respect him and stepped away from the sport. Occasionally, during heated arguments — whether with her or her father — she would slip away and run for hours, though she never participated in a competition again. Running was her sanctuary, a way to release her emotions and sort through her thoughts.

Rio only returned to racing after her mother's death.

When Maria passed away, it felt as though Rio had lost its heartbeat. Agatha, who had just embarked on her college journey, wasn’t there to witness the impact, but she could envision it clearly. During that time, she exchanged letters with nearly everyone back home — Javier, her parents, Wanda — and each one echoed the same sentiment: Rio was lost, drifting aimlessly, engulfed in sorrow and grief. After Maria's death and Agatha's departure, she became a specter, aimlessly wandering and drowning her pain in alcohol. It was racing that brought her back to life.

Javier gave in out of love, unsure of any other path. He had already lost his wife and couldn’t bear the thought of losing his daughter as well; he wanted to prevent her from withering away in her living sorrow. He created the hippodrome as a heartfelt gift, a sanctuary where she could race and compete to her heart’s content, as long as she promised to approach it with love, not greed.

When Rio made her comeback to racing, she began to thrive once more. At least, that's what Agatha had heard. It was what she saw when she returned home for the first time nineteen years ago. Now, Agatha recognized that this was her whole life — her empire.

She had never seen so many people in Darby before. As they passed the towering structures marking the corners of the construction, the crowd only grew. Nicholas was practically sprinting, tugging at her hand, and she did her best to keep pace while soaking in the atmosphere. The stands lined the track, divided into sections — some featuring concrete benches, while others boasted elegant lounges with plush seating, complete with restaurants and bars.

Nicholas only stopped running when they reached the ticket booth, practically bouncing with excitement. Acting on instinct, she purchased two tickets for seats close to the track, eager to relish her son's enthusiasm — after all, that was the purpose of their visit. However, when she spotted the banner featuring the racers, she froze, nearly yanking her son, who was pulling her along.

Rio.

Rio was one of the racers.

Agatha hadn’t laid eyes on her in years, and then, out of nowhere, there she was — looming on a massive banner right before her. "Rio and Raio, place your bets!" It was the same Rio from thirteen years past, yet completely different: more mature, with expression lines etched into her face, sun-kissed skin, a radiant smile, arms crossed over a red flannel shirt, and her old family hat perched atop her head.

Nicholas tugged at her, but Agatha couldn't move.

She was at a loss for how to feel, unable to pinpoint the emotions swirling within her. It was an overwhelming storm that led to a profound emptiness.

It had been thirteen years since she last saw Rio. Rio was set to race, and she had just purchased a ticket to witness it. She had made the decision to compete mere hours before her father's funeral. In just a few hours, she would be saying goodbye to him, while simultaneously engaging in the very activity he had loathed the most.

A mix of nostalgia, confusion, and resentment washed over her; she was feeling everything at once.

For years, Agatha had pondered what she had become, but now her thoughts turned to who Rio was. The Riandra she knew would never behave this way. It would be dishonest to deny that during the trip, her mind had drifted to her, imagining how she was coping with the loss of her father, picturing her heartbroken. Never in a million years did she expect to see her racing.

With her brow furrowed and her thoughts tangled, she let her son lead her, his impatience guiding her toward the stands. At that moment, she could barely focus on him; her mind was consumed with the question of why Rio was there, racing, when she should have been preparing for the funeral, saying goodbye to the father she cherished deeply.

The seats she purchased were positioned perfectly right by the starting line, and Nicholas was ecstatic, captivated by the spectacle. His bright eyes took in every detail with wonder as he gripped the safety rail of the parapet, bouncing with excitement. Agatha was ready to soothe him, but then she caught sight of her.

Rio. Her heart pounded in her chest.

After thirteen years, Riandra had become little more than a ghost, a shadow of a memory she buried each time an inch of it threatened to resurface. At times, she questioned whether she even remembered the sound of her voice or the warmth of her smile; more often than not, she chose to forget. Yet there she stood, alive and real, clad in dark boots, thick jeans, a black dress shirt, and that old hat that never left her head. A chill ran down Agatha's spine. How could the past manifest so vividly in the present? Once again, she felt as if she’d been transported back nineteen years.

While the other riders chatted with their sponsors and nearby bettors along the track, Rio was the only one standing next to her horse, an imposing black stallion. A man was speaking to her, gesturing animatedly as if instructing or persuading her, yet she didn’t seem to care, her expression disinterested as she gently stroked the horse's muzzle. Agatha squinted for a better look, and the man began to seem oddly familiar... Bucky?

Nicholas excitedly murmured and pointed down the track. Agatha felt her body tremble and sweat as she tried to restrain him, but he was too agitated, fixated on the horse. His enthusiasm quickly caught attention, and Bucky turned toward the stands, his blue eyes widening as they locked onto her. The moment she cursed, he nudged Rio, who abruptly turned her gaze in Agatha’s direction, her eyes wide as if she were seeing a ghost.

Those brown eyes, which she hadn't seen in years, pulled her in with a flood of questions that made the atmosphere feel suffocating. Agatha yearned to look away, to escape, to pretend she hadn’t noticed her, but she was ensnared in the gravitational pull of her gaze. Even from afar, they locked eyes, a silent connection that felt impossibly close.

She experienced a whirlwind of emotions, like a roller coaster racing, spinning, and plunging through the years —every high and low. Affection, tension, confusion, resentment, longing, curiosity — she felt it all at once. It was as if she were twenty again, standing in that same place, seeing her there for the first time. Her heart raced, heavy in her chest, just like that fateful day. Agatha felt exposed and vulnerable, as if she were reliving it all, while the skeleton she had tried to bury for years clawed its way back to the surface, demanding her attention. The promise of a fresh start she had clung to during the trip crumbled before her eyes as she gazed into those brown eyes, pulling her back to the origins of all that chaos.

Then the siren blared, and Nicholas screamed, covering his ears. She snapped out of her reverie, kneeling beside her son and whispering that everything would be alright.

"My love, that was just the signal for the race," she whispered, gently cradling her son's face to guide his gaze toward hers while tenderly caressing his cheeks. He tightly shut his eyes, and she leaned her forehead against his. "It's the signal for the race to begin. It's all over now. Look, the race has started," she said softly, and slowly, he opened his eyes.

The moment he caught sight of the horses galloping, he pushed her away with outstretched arms and leaned back over the railing, captivated by the relentless thundering of hooves.

It was truly mesmerizing. The track quaked beneath the galloping hooves, manes billowing wildly in the wind, while the rhythmic pounding sent clouds of hot dust soaring into the air. The race itself was thrilling, but Rio... it transcended all that.

Rio racing was nothing short of otherworldly, almost ethereal; it felt like witnessing something sacred. In that moment, nothing else mattered —just Rio. The way she ran commanded undivided attention, casting a spell of enchantment. All the riders leaned slightly over their horses, but Rio became one with Raio, her body seamlessly merging with his, as if they were two parts of a single whole. She navigated the curves with an intensity in her gaze, burning with a determination that suggested she wasn’t just racing — she was living, as if her very life depended on it. There was no hesitation, only pure speed and focus. It was as if they breathed in perfect harmony.

Though she didn’t start with an advantage, it didn’t take long for them to surge ahead. One, two, three competitors fell behind. The stands erupted in a deafening roar—a symphony of hooves, voices, and enthusiastic cheers.

In the penultimate turn, Rio took a daring risk; she only needed to pass one horse to clinch the victory. With a bold inside line maneuver, she pushed forward, and for a moment, Agatha felt a surge of nervousness. Yet, Rio maintained her composure, leaning deeply over her horse as if she were one with him, urging Raio into a fierce gallop. It was as if they were in perfect sync, instinctively knowing what to do together. They surged ahead, seizing the lead, and Nicholas let out an exhilarated shout that made Agatha laugh nervously, overwhelmed by the whirlwind of emotions unfolding.

As they approached the final straight, Agatha rose to her feet, equally captivated as Nicholas. Rio's name spilled from her lips, an uncontrollable cheer fueled by adrenaline, mirrored by her son’s excited yelps every time another horse threatened to overtake. On the track, Rio embodied pure speed — her hair whipping in the wind, hands steady, and eyes focused like a razor. Together with her horse, they were a single, electrifying force.

Agatha stood captivated, the shouts of the bettors around her fading into a distant murmur as the horses crossed the finish line, like sounds echoing from beneath the waves. All she could see was Rio — she was a force of nature.

In that instant, she recognized the déjà vu, reliving the moment with intense clarity. She felt breathless, as if she were the one racing down the track. Her heart raced in her chest, and a bittersweet wave washed over her mind. She was feeling everything all over again. She felt vulnerable, foolish, and inexplicably drained.

She may be experiencing similar feelings, but she couldn't turn back the clock twenty years. In an instant, all that euphoria transformed into pain; she felt trapped. She wasn’t ready for this; she couldn’t just let everything pour out like that. Her palms were clammy, and her breathing was shallow.

As Rio dismounted her horse, a wave of dizziness washed over her. Nicholas was cheering with enthusiasm, and she truly wanted him to savor the moment, but she couldn't remain there. Not now. She needed to get out of there.

***

Rio struggled to dismount the horse, surrounded by a throng of more than ten enthusiastic bettors lifting her up and cheering. Typically, she would revel in the moment, but not now. Her thoughts were scattered, far from the celebration.

She couldn't even recall how she had won the race; everything felt like a hazy dream, as if she were in a trance. Ignoring the buzz around her, she searched the stands but couldn’t spot her. Was she imagining things, or had it truly happened? Agatha had been there; she was certain of it. Yet now, she was nowhere to be found, leaving Rio questioning her own sanity.

It felt like she had been jolted awake. After catching sight of Agatha, everything else had faded away. But how could this be? What was she doing here? Why? Her mind was a jumble; she was utterly bewildered.

Just as the race had been a whirlwind, the chaos around her was almost too much to grasp. She couldn't focus on anything; it was as if she was on autopilot. She collected her check and trophy, all the while scanning the stands in utter confusion. She was unsure of her emotions, only aware of a sharp pain, like salt on an open wound — a knife twisting in a scar. Though part of her longed to escape, her gaze kept searching for her, drifting over every inch of the stands.

She needed a drink to clear her head. She was probably hallucinating.

For days, her thoughts had spiraled out of control. Concentration eluded her; ideas slipped away moments after they surfaced. Her mind felt like a raging storm, and no matter how hard she tried, she couldn’t rein it in. She really needed a drink. In less than four hours, she would bury her father. It was too much. Her mind couldn’t process it; nothing felt tangible. After encountering Agatha’s ghost, she feared she might truly be losing her grip on reality. Perhaps a beer — or two — would help.

She needed to get ready for the wake. Her father's wake. Her thoughts were a chaotic mess, and honestly, how could this be real? Her father. She looked around, but heard nothing, as if everyone were suddenly mute. Nothing made sense.

Her father, her hero, her father who despised racing, but she kept racing; who disapproved of her drinking, but she kept drinking. Who would stop her now? She was the epitome of everything he most hated, but still, he loved her more than anyone ever could. Who would love her now?

She cast a final glance at the stands, met once more by a void. Agatha wasn't there this time. Why would she be? She wouldn’t dare show up. Still, her mind drifted back nineteen years to when Agatha truly was there, and more than ever, she longed to rewind time and do everything differently. She wished she could change everything, but she couldn't. She could win every single race in the world and amass countless trophies, but in the end, all Rio truly knew was how to lose.

Even with a trophy in her hand and a hefty check in her pocket, she felt empty, alone. The void left by those who had departed ached in her heart, and while the celebration swirled around her, she wanted to cry. No matter how much she won, in the end, she kept on losing.

She was a fucking loser.

Chapter 6: edging

Chapter Notes

this chapter is long, and the next one is even bigger like HUGE but i hope that's okay bc both are important flashbacks to contextualize the foundation of their relationship

"There's an ache in you put there by the ache in me, but if it's all the same to you, it's the same to me" – 'Tis The Damn Season, Taylor Swift

Nineteen years ago

It was jarring how profoundly things could change in less than twelve months.

Just last January, Agatha had traveled this road in reverse. Packed into a truck with her parents, smiles wide and future bright, she was on her way to the airport, bound for Los Angeles. Now, in December, she was back in Darby. With just a small suitcase and backpack, she gripped the wheel of a rented sedan — a vehicle surely unsuited for these dirt roads — and inhaled the familiar scent of wet dirt and sagebrush. She still hadn't reconciled her feelings about being here.

Staying away this long was never the plan, she’d meant to return during the spring break, but life took a completely different turn. Rio’s complete silence over the months made her too vulnerable to come home, forcing her to find time and space to process her hurt.

In June, her parents had been eager to book her flight for the summer, but she couldn’t, she didn’t want to face the truth. Agatha couldn’t bear to admit the painful truth that the entire town already knew. She didn't want to face it and knew that, by returning home, she would have to call a spade a spade and admit that she and Rio were no longer together, that she was an idiot for believing they would make it. She refused to accept their separation as final simply because she didn't believe in half-words, much less none and Rio had offered no explanation; she deserved more than Riandra's unspoken farewell.

She couldn't return home, and luckily, she didn't have to because her roommate — now her best friend, Alex Cabot — always had a solution for any and every problem. They had been roommates since the start of the first semester and by the middle of the year, they were inseparable, and Agatha considered her a sister.

Alex was there every step of the way, seeing her spend sleepless nights writing letters almost every day, taking photos to send to Rio. They spent early mornings together where Agatha told her absolutely everything about her life, her home, and her love, all the plans they had together, how much she missed her, and how she counted the days to see her again. Alex was also there when she rushed to the mailboxes in anticipation of Rio having written to her, and after a few months, she already expected her to return with a tub of ice cream and a couple of beers, knowing she would come back empty-handed and heartbroken. Though her letters grew sparser, and the excitement curdled into angry, questioning monologues about the distance and her own feelings, Agatha never stopped writing. Every word she sent poured into a void, as Rio never once replied.

One morning, right before spring break, Agatha finally confessed to Alex that she dreaded going home. She had learned through friends that Rio was already seeing other people, and the thought of facing that hurt was unbearable. Darby was her hometown, but Rio was her home and the realization that she no longer had that made her claustrophobic. Her roommate intervened, suggesting Agatha skip the trip. Having heard so much about the "famous Agatha Harkness," Alex’s parents were keen to meet their daughter’s loyal sidekick. Agatha accepted the invitation, informed her family, and spent her two-week break in Vancouver with the Cabots.

After that pivotal break, Agatha made a conscious effort to live a little. She went out more, met new people, and, finally, she gave Tessa a chance.

Agatha always found it strange that college was popularly viewed as a time for casual fun, dating, and experimentation. For her, it was simply the realization of a lifelong dream: going to Los Angeles, seeing California, and charting her course in the world. Romantically, she had no plans, she already had Rio. Their separation was temporary, a prerequisite for college. Rio was supposed to attend college in Montana, close to home, and eventually, they would devise a strategy — any strategy — to remain together.

They had their differences, but the mutual desire to be together superseded everything else, or so Agatha thought.

Agatha acknowledged that their goodbye had been strained, though she felt neither was truly to blame. Her acceptance letter to UCLA had arrived the upon Rio’s mother passing — a profound loss that affected everyone. Understanding Rio’s overwhelming grief, Agatha delayed her departure as long as she could to offer support. Ultimately, she had to leave before classes started; after years of striving for this dream, she couldn't say no to college.

When she left, they had been arguing, but Agatha attributed Rio's hostility to pain. The immense grief outweighed her frustration over Agatha’s departure, though the leaving itself certainly hurt. Still, Agatha believed their separation was temporary. Their plan was for life: Agatha would pursue her dream at UCLA, return as soon as possible, and Rio would visit when she could. It was never a breakup.

For weeks, Agatha's letters poured out apologies, worries, and longing. She encouraged Rio to continue her studies and asked after her, even the horses. She wrote pages daily, meticulously recounting every detail of her life, always emphasizing that her studies were part of a larger strategy — a foundation for their future together. She promised that soon, things would return to normal, with them together, as always.

She sent photos of all the places she visited, wrote about her classes, and always included an affectionate little verse in which she melted with longing. In the first few months, in all her letters, Agatha marked how many days were left until the holidays, and alongside it, a question mark, an invitation, for Rio to shorten that time and come visit.

Initially, Rio's silence felt understandable. Losing a mother is a grief that defies easy sharing, everyone navigates such a loss uniquely. Rio needed time and space to redefine herself outside of that enormous pain and time’s relentless march. Maria’s death, coupled with Agatha’s departure, had created a deep wound, and Agatha refused to blame her. She accepted the distance, hoping that Rio would eventually heal, settle into a new routine, and finally be ready to talk.

The thing is, time kept passing, and Rio never wrote back.

Agatha diligently kept up correspondence with her parents, Javier, Wanda, and a few other friends from home. Their letters arrived weekly, providing comfort and connection. They worried about her, shared details of their days, and asked about hers; Agatha and Wanda, in particular, maintained their close bond, making the distance feel manageable. This network of communication was a blessing until it became a source of pain: after months, she was close to everyone except Rio, who hadn't sent a single word since her departure.

Agatha refused to view the silence as a breakup. To her, the separation was a temporary necessity, a step toward the grand future they had planned. They had always agreed that if college didn't work out together, they would reunite as quickly as possible. A formal breakup had never been on the table. But every day, Rio’s lack of communication grew heavier, making the physical distance feel increasingly threatening. Agatha was living without Rio, and Rio without her. Slowly, the shared plans for their future shrank, replaced by a solitary image of Agatha's life. Rio had disappeared, and Agatha realized she was in a one-sided relationship, mailing letters that were never returned.

Her mind furiously generated excuses for Rio’s distant behavior: grief, loss, a change of heart about college, anger over the timing of Agatha’s departure, or simply not knowing how to manage the distance or respond. Agatha accepted every justification, believing their bond was strong enough to survive this phase. Two or three months of separation wouldn't destroy a lifelong love; they were grown ups facing a difficult circumstance. This silence wasn't a final period but a pause, an ellipsis — and so, she kept writing.

When she met Tessa, she found it funny. She had never been in this position. Rio was her everything: her first love, first kiss, first girlfriend. Their love had always been reciprocal, and in high school, no one dared challenge their status as a couple. Tessa was the first person to openly flirt with her. Agatha, loyal to Rio, learned only how to politely deflect attention, refusing Tessa's invitations and everyone else’s.

Rio needed space; this was just a phase, Agatha convinced herself. They were still together.

Months dragged by before the painful realization finally hit: she didn’t have a girlfriend anymore.

In May, a letter from Wanda arrived. Agatha was used to their weekly exchanges, but this one was different. For months, Agatha had cautiously probed Wanda about Rio, fearing that asking her parents or her godfather would pressure her. Wanda was her only confidante and her previous replies had been vague, reinforcing Agatha's belief that Rio simply needed time to deal with her trauma. But in her last letter, Agatha had expressed genuine distress — she was wasting away without any word from Rio, worried sick about her well-being.

She braced herself for any kind of reply, yet nothing prepared her for the letter she read on May seventh:

Dear Agatha,

First of all, I'm sorry.

I'm sorry for not having written to you as I really should have. I’ve talked about my day, the weather, school, about whom I'm meeting, avoiding the real questions you kept asking. I didn't know how to tell you the truth. I see how upset you are about Rio, and honestly, as your friend, I can no longer talk about trivial things when the truth is out and about. I held back because I didn't want to hurt you further, but leaving you guessing is just as cruel, especially since everyone here already knows what's going on.

I read your last letter with my heart sinking, you wrote that you were wasting away from missing her, so worried about her. Aggie, I reread your words, desperately trying to find a way to protect you, but you truly deserve the truth. I sincerely regret not telling you sooner, I genuinely thought this was just a phase. I wanted to write something comforting, but you don't deserve half-truths. I can’t lie to you or hide this, I can only promise that I will remain here for you, even from afar, just as you have always been there for me.

The truth is, Rio has drastically changed since you left. She hasn't just changed the way people do when they’re lonely or adjusting to a new routine, she has completely transformed. The Rio we knew left with you.

Initially, we all assumed it was grief, that she would get better, we thought it was just a matter of time before she reapplied to colleges. But that hasn't happened. She’s isolated herself from everyone and started going out with different people, people you don't even know. Last week, she disappeared for days, traveling across Montana with people from the horse racing circuit.

She still talks to Natasha, I know because we talk a lot; she's always at the school, she teaches judo. Sometimes I mention you, and we talk about Rio too. But the truth is, she's even distanced herself a bit from Natasha. All she cares about now is parties, racing, and drinking. She and Bucky are now inseparable; they always had that odd, tight-knit friendship, and I still don't know why Rio tolerated him, as he’s always been despicable, but now they are permanently attached at the hip. He’s studying vet in Bell Crossing, and Rio spends most of her time there, attending all the college parties.

I can't tell you when it started, but she's seeing other people. It's not like she's hiding it, I saw her with a girl at the bar the other day, and it wasn't the first time. She brings some girls back from parties sometimes, goes out with them, and, you know... Unfortunately, everyone knows already.

I truly didn't want to be the one to tell you this, Agatha, I swear it. I tried to believe she was just making new friends, but Natasha confirmed she is actively dating other girls. Nat even made me promise not to tell you, but I just couldn’t, it would be unfair to you. Aggie, I hated being the one to deliver this news, but seeing your last letter, so full of longing, your hopes so utterly intact, trusting her blindly, it just wasn't right. It's not fair for you to keep waiting for someone who is no longer waiting for you.

I'm so sorry, but you deserve to know. And honestly, you deserve so much more than her silence. She should have been honest and upfront with you.

But I also tell you this: you are the most wonderful, incredible person I know. I miss you every single day, and you are destined to become the smartest lawyer in California. You are building a beautiful path, your own path, living your dream. I know how much Rio means to you, but please don't let her overshadow your dreams for yourself. You were faithful and chose her, if she couldn't give that back, the fault lies entirely with her. She should have been honest, it was the least you deserved. My advice is to read her silence as the final message: nothing she has to say matters, but you do.

I hope you'll be okay. I know it will be difficult, but you deserve the truth, Agatha. You deserve sincerity, faithfulness; you deserve someone who gives you much more than an empty silence. She doesn't deserve your longing. Go out, live a little, you’re in Cali, I’m sure there are a lot of good things waiting for you to find them.

I’m here for you, even from a distance, whenever you need me. I truly apologize for not telling you sooner, you deserve the truth and I promise to always be honest with you from now on. I am truly here.

A very tight hug with a kiss on the forehead,

Wanda.

Agatha spent days weeping, skipping classes, and hiding in bed. It took Alex nearly a week to coax her out; she barely ate.

The concept of losing Rio was one she had never entertained, nor feared. What they shared felt transcendent, stronger than anything. The idea that they wouldn't eventually be together was nonsensical. They were simply apart, not broken up. Their separation for college was part of the plan they had long agreed upon. Agatha was utterly bewildered by the change: why had Rio changed? Why would she do this?

The most agonizing aspect was the how. Rio had offered nothing but silence. Years of shared love and history were discarded without a single word.

Yet, the true worst part was that despite the painful confirmation from Wanda, Agatha couldn't let go. Her feelings, the love she felt, were greater than the hurt or the anger of knowing the truth, greater than the anger over Rio's silence and actions. She couldn't accept a nonexistent breakup, she refused to allow their entire love story to end without closure. If Rio intended to throw everything away, Agatha deserved at least a few final words.

During her misery, Alex took one of Rio’s pictures from the refrigerator and turned it into a dart target. No amount of pleading from Agatha deterred her. Alex remained a fierce supporter, bringing food, taking class notes, and repeating her core belief: "You deserve much more than a cheating barnyard fowl."

It was Alex who ultimately convinced Agatha to give Tessa a chance, and she was right: Tessa deserved it. Since they met, Tessa had been nothing but kind and endearing, respecting all boundaries while subtly making it known that she was waiting for a chance.

Agatha did like Tessa, but their connection felt different, she couldn't tell if it was merely the novelty of being with someone other than Rio, or if her heart truly wasn't invested. It wasn't a negative difference, but something was undeniably missing. It felt cruel to look into Tessa's gentle blue eyes and force a smile. She liked Tessa, yes, but she still loved Rio.

Rio had made a huge mistake, yet Agatha still didn't view it as final. She despised herself for this reaction, for her immediate instinct to seek understanding, to figure out why Rio acted this way, why she discarded everything. She especially resented Tessa’s relentless affection, care, and princess-like devotion. It was agonizing to receive all that love while her mind remained fixed on Riandra.

Agatha wished she could simply follow her friends' advice and cut ties, start fresh, and accept that some loves, no matter how passionate, are destined to end without a storybook conclusion. But surrender was not in her nature, she was defined by her determination. She concluded that a final period must be earned with a full sentence. If her relationship with Rio was over, it needed to end properly; months of silence were an inadequate way to discard their entire history.

Rio had made a mistake, and now Agatha was making one, too. This put them on even ground, ensuring they could have a fair, decent conversation upon her return home. This calculated logic, of course, was kept secret, she preferred letting her friends celebrate the illusion that she was moving on.

In the ensuing months, she continued her secret correspondence with Rio, mailing the letters when Alex was out. The frequency waned, from weekly to once in two weeks, then to longer gaps, but never ceased. She poured out everything: first, a tirade of every imaginable insult, blaming Rio for the destruction. Then came the apologies, where she acknowledged that leaving during a vulnerable time might have hurt her, but argued it didn't invalidate their entire relationship. Rio's reply remained silence and Agatha didn't even know if the letters were read, though she desperately hoped so. Her writing chronicled her lonely separation, her longing, her desire to fix things, and her questions about Rio's actions. In short, Agatha produced months of endless monologues, some angry, some despairing, some loving, and some vengeful, detailing a healing process that only existed on paper. None were ever answered.

Meanwhile, her feelings for Tessa steadily deepened. They saw each other daily, went out constantly, and as their connection intensified, Agatha knew she needed to put a semicolon on their relationship.

She felt entitled to justify her actions by pointing to Rio’s infidelity, she would have been faithful forever had Rio not broken their trust first. Yet, she recognized that Tessa was innocent in their shared wreckage and didn't deserve to be collateral damage. Tessa was genuinely devoted, striving to be sweeter and kinder every day. She was patient and easygoing, sharing Agatha’s interests and aspirations. For the first time, Agatha felt understood in a way Rio had never quite managed. This ease with Tessa gave her pause. She had started dating Tessa to move past Rio, but she was now developing genuine feelings for her, even while her heart still belonged to Rio.

In September, when Tessa casually expressed her mother’s eagerness to meet her, Agatha confessed that she wasn't ready for a committed relationship, admitting she was still reeling from a recent breakup. She stressed that a serious commitment was impossible for her right now. They could continue their constant companionship and getting-to-know-you phase, but that was her limit, pushing further would be dishonest to both Tessa and her own feelings.

To her surprise, Tessa accepted the boundary with grace. Though clearly disappointed, she understood Agatha’s past and respected it, valuing sincerity above all else. Agatha, though relieved, felt terrible. She nodded, managed a smile, and kissed her, but internally, she worried: did she even have this much to offer? And what would happen to Tessa once she and Rio finally had their overdue conversation?

She was just a few minutes from home, and her hands grew increasingly slick on the steering wheel. This tension was not what she had anticipated. When she left, she expected to be desperate with homesickness, counting the moments until her return to Rio. Now, she was approaching home unsure of what awaited her.

She did miss her family, her parents' presence, her mother's food, time with little Benito. But amidst the wreckage of her relationship, she felt completely out of place. She didn't miss Darby itself, she missed the people she loved. Deep down, she wasn't yearning for home, she was yearning for Rio.

The sensory details of the countryside, the dirt road, the sweeping fields, the sound of wild horses galloping, the quiet, and the smell of wet dirt, all felt intrinsically linked to Rio. Though she never loved this end-of-the-world town, every good memory was infused with her. Rio, who detested hot asphalt but thrived running on wet dirt; who used rain showers to bathe the cows; who spent afternoons grazing on vineyard grapes; and who often slept in the makeshift stable attic, lost in the clear, starry sky. Every inch of this land carried Rio's essence. Nothing in the world was more beloved to Rio than this city.

But now, Agatha felt excluded from that cherished world, outside that circle of love and familiarity. She didn't know if she was still a priority in Rio's life. She should be angry, Rio's silence and actions were responsible for her pain, yet anger was the last emotion she could summon. She felt small and utterly insecure. She didn't want a confrontation, she just wanted clarity.

Her sense of belonging had vanished. She didn't want to live in Darby, but California didn't feel like home yet, either. She felt like a person without a place, adrift and directionless. How could she anchor her life without Rio? And though she had Tessa, their bond wasn't exactly a stable foundation. She felt like a wanderer, welcomed by people she loved, with places to explore, but at home nowhere.

Telling Tessa she valued sincerity now felt deeply hypocritical, she herself was lost and confused, unsure what to feel or say. Her homecoming felt less like a comfort and more like preparing for battle. Was she seeking truth from Rio, or simply trying to reclaim her? She knew she would swallow her pride instantly if it meant restoring what they had, but what were they now? They were certainly something, but they weren't what they once were, so what did that mean?

Agatha sighed heavily as her house came into view just yards away. She wished she could be the girl she once was, full of dreams and free from the weight of reality. Everyone said Rio hadn't grown up, but Agatha realized she was the one failing at adulthood, unable to face responsibilities, deal with frustration, or accept reality.

She yearned to walk through that door and magically restore the past. Yet, even if that were possible, it wouldn't be the same, because she had changed too. Worst of all, she still didn't know who she was or what truly mattered anymore. She was in the painful process of figuring it out, suspecting that even if nothing else had shifted, she would be just as lost as she was right now.

***

It was strange to realize how much had changed while, paradoxically, everything looked exactly the same. Her childhood home was untouched: the yellow curtains, the pale green porcelain set on the coffee table, the knitted sofa blanket, all exactly where they belonged. A faint, comforting smile touched her lips; it was as if she had never left.

Her moment of reflection was shattered by a booming, happy laugh. Her father had spotted her in the hallway, and before she could even register his presence, she was swept off her feet into a bone-crushing bear hug.

"I missed you so much, kiddo!" he declared, effortlessly spinning her around. She laughed, feeling momentarily like a child again, her recent worries forgotten. "You're finally home!" His blue eyes shimmered, and when he set her down, the tears welling up in his eyes made her laugh again. He held her face tenderly, pressing his forehead to hers and showering her face with wet kisses that tickled from his unshaven beard. "Eva!" he bellowed, and the sound of her mother’s quick footsteps echoed from the hall. "She's home!"

"Dad, it was only a few months," Agatha said, trying to play down the drama, but she was already overwhelmed with emotion, her heart warm at the sight of them. She had missed them terribly.

"You cannot stay away from home that long," he muttered, shaking his head with a frown. "Absolutely not! I won't go that long without seeing you again!"

"You know you can visit me—" She didn't get to finish, her mother interrupted the sentence with a fresh surge of tears and a tight embrace.

"Sweetheart, I missed you so much!" Her mother wept, and Agatha finally let out the breath she'd been unknowingly holding, clinging to her. She realized just how desperately she had missed her mother’s arms. "I missed you, I missed you so much! Oh my god!"

They spent hours in this flood of familiar affection, an endless, joyful reunion. Despite all the mixed feelings about her return, Agatha acknowledged that her longing extended beyond Rio. This was the first time she’d been away from her family for so long.

Though she was the black sheep who dreamed of big cities, her entire life had unfolded on that ranch, always within her parents' view. Her family was faultless: she had grown up in a loving home, and as an only child, she was always spoiled. Her parents ensured she had everything, not just materially, but emotionally, making sure they were present and affectionate. Agatha knew she was the center of their world, and her longing for them couldn't possibly match their missing her.

Despite corresponding faithfully throughout the months, her parents wanted to hear every detail as if it were brand new. They spent hours talking, nestled together on the living room sofa, treating her like a little girl again. Her father stroked her hair while her mother quizzed her on everything she already knew. She lost track of time talking about everything.

Agatha spoke of her classes, the difficult curriculum, and the adaptation challenges. She told them about Alex, showed them photos from the Vancouver trip, and mentioned how Alex dragged her to parties. She complained about the cafeteria food, and her mother immediately promised to send more money so she could eat properly, which Agatha loved. Though her parents were already aware of the facts, they asked for every minute detail, and she couldn't stop smiling, comfortable in their embrace.

Though she'd been away only a short time, she had packed a lot into her life. She took up surfing, discovered she was a total disaster, which made her father roar with laughter, but earned his proud encouragement when she joined the volleyball team. She and Alex were now on the debate club together, and they had successfully scheduled all their courses jointly. She'd explored many neighboring cities and genuinely loved Los Angeles, the constant sun, the proximity of the campus to the beach, and the strong prospect of a good internship next semester thrilled her.

"So, is this the famous Tessa?" her mother asked, holding a snapshot from Santa Monica beach a few days prior. In the photo, Agatha was smiling broadly on a surfboard while Tessa made a face, holding a paddle.

Agatha clenched her eyes shut, cheeks instantly flushing. Her mother chuckled, giving her a knowing look with raised eyebrows, clearly waiting for an answer.

"Are you certain you're spending most of your time with Alex?" her father inquired with the same playful skepticism, flipping through the rest of the developed pictures. He blushed her further by holding up a photo where Tessa was hugging her from behind, Agatha's head a blur as if she had been turning for a kiss when the shutter snapped. "You look very close, you and this Tessa."

She let out a mortified groan. In her defense, she’d asked for the entire film roll to be processed and had forgotten what certain shots contained.

"Yes, that’s Tessa," Agatha confirmed, then abruptly snatched the photos from her father’s hand. "And you already know who she is, I've sent pictures before."

"Yes, you also mentioned New York..." her father muttered, a mix of curiosity and subtle disapproval in his voice.

"Richard!" her mother sharply warned him. Then, stroking Agatha's leg with a smile, she added, "I’m happy, sweetheart. You always look like you’re having fun with her. It’s lovely to see you smile like that. I bet you’ll love New York; you’ve always wanted to go there."

"I know!" Agatha squeaked excitedly, and they laughed together. "Can you imagine? Mom, it must be the most beautiful thing! Tessa said Times Square completely shuts down, and it's a massive party!"

"I'll need to see every single picture!" Evanora matched her excitement.

"But why didn't you bring her here then?" Richard asked, folding his arms. Agatha rested her head on his lap to look up at him. "You spend so much time together, you're traveling together, she seems important to you."

"She is, but—" She stumbled, her deep-seated anxieties rushing back. With a sigh, Agatha merely shrugged. "Not in that way. I mean, why would I bring her here? We're just friends."

"Just friends?" He raised an eyebrow, waving the photo in question above her head. Blushing again, Agatha knocked his hand away, sending the picture drifting to the sofa. "Are you sure?"

"Dad..." It was Agatha's turn to scold him, and he just mimicked her shrug.

"It’s not that serious, Richard. They're just getting to know each other," Evanora intervened. Agatha pointed toward her mother, affirming her point as if that settled the matter.

"So you and Rio really broke up?" he asked. The question hit Agatha like a bucket of ice water. Her lips parted, unsure how to respond, but at that moment, her mother shot up, hands on her hips, directing a severe glare at her father.

"Richard." Her mother’s tone was sharp, a familiar warning. This was precisely why Agatha had avoided the topic, why she hadn't written home about the breakup. She knew they would inevitably intervene. They had watched the two girls grow up together their whole lives, interference was unavoidable. "We already discussed this."

"You and I did, but this isn't about us, it's about them," Richard countered, turning his attention back to his daughter. Agatha's eyebrows were tightly knit, silently begging him to drop the subject, but it was too late. "Of course I'm happy for you, honey, but I'm sorry, I have to ask."

"And she doesn't have to answer you," her mother insisted, letting out a frustrated sigh. "They are no longer together and you know that, everyone knows that. Riandra made sure that was abundantly clear."

"Everyone? Like, everyone everyone?" Agatha asked, her voice barely a whisper. Her mother took a deep breath, her eyebrows softening with compassion as she nodded. Groaning, Agatha buried her face in her hands, a childish but necessary action, she just wanted to disappear.

"Rio is no longer a child. We're family, but that doesn't mean I’m going to coddle her. She was a jerk to our daughter, there’s nothing more that needs to be said."

"Eva, this isn't our business, it's theirs," Richard said, softening his tone and shaking his head, attempting to prevent a full-blown argument. With her face still hidden, Agatha just wished she could vanish. "I know, Rio was... immature, irresponsible... there’s no excuse for it, she made a huge mistake. But is this something you resolve from a distance? You’re being naive to think they won’t at least talk."

"And what is left to discuss?" Evanora retorted critically. "Rio made her choices, and Agatha is now moving forward, making hers."

Agatha snatched a nearby cushion, clamped it over her face, and let out a stifled scream, followed by a heavy sigh — a silence-inducing maneuver.

"I am still here," she stated, sitting up and making eye contact with both parents. "Thank you for your concern." With that final, clipped statement, she got up and marched straight to her bedroom.

***

It was hardly helpful that her bedroom felt like a shrine, with pictures of Rio adorning every surface. Trying to stem the flow of tears, she stared at her dresser, which was covered in developed photos of their life together, forming a painful timeline. She wept as her fingers traced images from their childhood, noting how their affection intensified as they grew, seeing the undeniable history of their relationship captured in those snapshots — how everything had blossomed.

She was in her house, but she absolutely didn't feel at home, and the reason was clear: the gaze of those dark, jabuticaba eyes staring back from every photograph.

Agatha braced her elbows on the dresser and buried her face in her hands again, lost in a whirlwind of thought. Yes, she was hurt — more deeply than she cared to admit. While she had moved on and allowed herself to explore a relationship with Tessa, she questioned if that was truly fair or right, and she couldn't rationalize Rio’s actions. Yet, she found herself unable — or unwilling — to blame Rio.

Perhaps she had been naive to believe they were secure. Their parting was strained, Rio had made it clear she didn't want Agatha to leave and didn't accept the timing. The plans for their future had largely been Agatha's own design. Rio had always expressed a desire to stay in Darby, though she typically yielded to Agatha to avoid an argument. As Agatha waited for a letter that never came, perhaps silence was all Rio had to give, there was nothing left to say because Rio had already made her stand. Agatha chose to leave and Rio chose not to accept it. Rio remained true to her stated wishes, and it was Agatha who had stubbornly expected her to compromise eventually.

Still, Agatha felt cheated. She deserved more than this — more than vanishing into a silence that made their shared history feel nothing. It wasn't nothing, it was everything. She longed to feel angry, but the overriding emotion she felt for Rio was simply longing.

The creak of the door snapped her out of her thoughts. She quickly scrubbed the tears from her face, sniffling as she saw her father's reflection in the mirror. She knew it would be him to start the conversation, her mother would hold back.

The connection between their families ran deep, far exceeding the two girls' romance. Their friendship was established years ago — a bond so strong that not even their two runaway trains could derail it. Her father and Uncle Javi were practically brothers and her mother had helped raise Rio alongside Maria. Even after they fell in love, the families remained a unit. Agatha knew that despite her mother's current frustration, she still cared for Riandra, though her allegiance had shifted.

When they first started dating in their pre-teen years, the whole family became involved. They were always inseparable, destined to be best friends, but their romance had been unexpected. After hundreds of awkward conversations, everyone accepted it. Her mother, Maria, and Lilia often took them out, and her mother became her chief confidante, helping her navigate the discoveries of first love with her best friend.

Though they eventually became the romance's biggest fans, her father and Uncle Javi were hesitant at first, wary of their daughters dating at such a young age. As the years passed, her father truly embraced Rio as a daughter, genuinely believing their love was meant to be, something for a lifetime. Agatha often watched through the window as her father sat talking with Rio after dinner, sometimes for hours, listening to him say how happy he was knowing Rio truly loved her.

Her mother, while loving Rio like a daughter, harbored the inherent maternal instinct to side with her own. During high school, before Agatha left, Evanora frequently expressed concern about their future. She wholly supported Agatha's dream to go to college and pursue her life, even if it meant distance, but she doubted Rio's commitment to education. Rio, truthfully, never cared about college. Evanora loved Rio deeply but often warned Agatha that Riandra might not be the right person for her, urging her not to be tied down by a teenage romance, as life held much more.

Agatha's three years of high school were intense: maximizing courses and AP classes, volunteer work, excelling in sports — all focused on crafting the perfect college application. Rio, despite every incentive, was only invested in the ranch. Evanora’s stance was clear: she loved Rio, but she often voiced her concern that Riandra was an unsuitable match for Agatha’s ambitious path.

Agatha didn't have to keep her parents informed about Rio; while she was in California, they were right there, witnessing everything firsthand. Agatha was the one out of the loop, but her parents practically lived alongside Rio. If something was wrong, she didn't need to announce it — they already knew. This explained her mother's current protective stance and caution toward the subject. What Wanda wrote in her letter, Evanora had seen with her own eyes, which entirely justified her position.

It was clear her father was disappointed in Rio, but Agatha knew him well enough to realize his intention to bring balance to the situation. He didn't want bitterness to consume her, he wanted her to be truthful about her emotions so she could decide what was best for her.

He rested his hand on the chair she was occupying and kissed the top of her head, their reflection visible in the mirror. Agatha sighed as he gently hugged her shoulders, offering silent protection.

"I’m sorry about the way your mother and I spoke downstairs," he murmured. Agatha turned her chair to face him. Her father let out a tired sigh, sat on the bed a few feet away, and leaned forward, resting his elbows on his knees. He chose his words carefully, studying her face. "It’s not our place to make decisions for you. I apologize if I said anything you didn't want to hear, but I think you need to be honest with yourself instead of burying your feelings and pretending you don't care. I know this matters to you."

They held each other's gaze for a few seconds, and she saw the genuine affection in his eyes. He was hurting because she was hurting.

"I know, I just..." She couldn't articulate her thoughts, so she just shrugged and rolled her eyes, feeling exposed. She knew she could never hide anything from him. "I didn't want to talk to you guys about it, about her."

"Why, honey?" he asked softly, offering boundless patience. Agatha groaned, letting out a frustrated puff of air.

"Because you already know, I don't need to say it."

"I don't think anyone knows the full story," he replied with a sincere shrug. Agatha frowned. "I mean, everyone presumes you're not together anymore, that part is clear, but that's all we know."

"Is there more to know than that?"

"Agatha, there's no justifying what she did. She made a mistake, end of story," he said, resting his face in his hands. "But she... I am not defending her, okay? Let that be absolutely clear." He held up his hands to emphasize his point, and she raised an eyebrow, waiting. "She's been through a lot. What she did was wrong, but I don't believe she viewed your departure as see you later; for her, it was goodbye. She lost her mother, you left... I don't know, but she lost a tremendous amount. She thought she lost you, too."

"She didn't lose me, I made that extremely clear," Agatha insisted, struggling to control the frustration in her voice, her face heating up and tears welling up again. "I always told her this was temporary, that I was coming home. We never broke up! She never said anything to me. Did you know she never even wrote to me? Not once!"

"And I'm not saying you have to give her another shot. I'm just trying to show you that she's a person, and she's going through a lot. Is it fair to say she didn't lose you? You were in California, traveling, meeting new places, new people, while her life stalled here, kiddo. She had just lost her mother." He scratched his head thoughtfully, sighing.
