"You are my daughter. I love you more than anything, but I love her too, and I know she loves you."

"What do you want me to do?" Agatha asked in a shaky whisper, struggling to hide the tears choking her words.

“I don't want anything, this is up to you." She rolled her eyes, and he shrugged.

"I already intended to talk to her, dad. You don't have to plead, it's inevitable."

"She's not the same, Agatha," he said with a heavy sigh. "I don't think she was able to process the loss, she's shut down completely. We barely recognize her. I know you're hurt, and you have every right to be, you are entirely in the right. But she's sad too. I just wanted you to consider that."

"Are you taking her side?" Agatha questioned, narrowing her eyes, unable to believe what she was hearing.

"No." He promptly denied it, taking a deep breath and scratching his unshaven beard. "I almost punched her in the face, if you want to know."

"You what?!" she nearly shouted, and he nodded, clearly ashamed.

"I was at the bar with your uncle and the ranch crew when she showed up with a girl. She didn't even acknowledge us, she was so drunk she didn't recognize us. When she... when I saw her, you know..." He stumbled over the words, lowering his head, and Agatha nodded, confirming she did know. "She kissed the girl." Even though she knew, the admission felt like a punch regardless.

Her father lowered his head, letting out a heavy breath.

"I'd been drinking too, and I went to confront her. It was a messy argument. She shoved me, and Javier grabbed me instantly, before I could hit her. Then your uncle and I got into a fight." Agatha was stunned, eyes wide. "I would never hit a woman, especially Riandra. She's like a daughter to me, but I went blind, I was drunk. I'm not proud of it, but I swear to god, Agatha, if she'd been a guy, I would have landed a straight punch right there." She opened her mouth to speak, but he pressed on. "The worst part is she got involved in my fight with your uncle. Javier had to physically drag her away while we were arguing, and she couldn't stop crying. I was yelling, everyone was, and then she screamed in my face that you had left, claiming she was only moving on with her life because you had abandoned her."

Despite having so much to say, Agatha remained utterly silent. Tears streamed down her face. She continued to look at her father, who stared back with his eyebrows knit together, a look of pity and deep concern. Even if she could speak, she wouldn't know what to say or think.

“Your mother can barely look her in the face. Rio doesn't show up whenever we gather there. She knows she made a mistake, there's no way around it, but she is broken, kiddo. It's not your fault, it's nobody's fault. We can't get inside people's minds to control or guide their thoughts. No one is to blame for how she handled her mother's loss and your departure, and she is responsible for her actions, but I don't know, Agatha... You have every right to feel the way you do, but you don't have to go in there with stones in your hand."

"She cheated on me for everyone to see, and you want me to do nothing?" This was far from Agatha's true feelings, but she needed her father to keep talking, to keep hearing his perspective.

"I want you both to move on with your lives, whatever that means," he said sincerely, letting out a heavy breath. "You have everything in California: an incredible life, great friends, and now Tessa. You need to shed this sadness to fully embrace your life, and forgiveness is the only way, kiddo. She made a mistake, but what does it matter now? Soon you'll be back in Los Angeles, and she'll be stuck here, living the same life, consumed by the same losses. She needs to close this chapter, and so do you. It's painful, but you both need to move on, regardless of how."

Agatha looked down and nodded. She couldn't feel anger, though she knew she should. Instead, she felt a profound sadness. Moving on meant letting go, and despite knowing there was nothing substantial left to hold onto, she didn't have the courage to put a final period on it, even though she logically convinced herself it was necessary. Rationally, she craved closure, she knew her father was right — her life was full of good things. Yet, all she truly wanted was Riandra.

A part of her desperately wanted to rewrite their story, still believing they had an entire life left to explore together. She knew it wasn't practical, that their differences would resurface, but her mind and heart were at war. She needed closure, but her heart flat-out refused to close that chapter.

"I'll talk to her," Agatha murmured in a threadbare voice. Her father nodded, stood from the bed, and leaned in to kiss her forehead. "Mom said Uncle Javi is hosting a dinner for me. I suppose I'll have to deal with it then anyway."

"And you intend to go to the Vidals' for dinner without speaking to her first?" her father questioned, raising an eyebrow.

"What do you suggest I do? Barge in on her right now?" Agatha laughed without humor. "I bet she'd just love that surprise."

"Nah, she's not home. She has a race today," her father said casually, already standing in the doorway, ready to leave. "Javier expanded the equestrian center—it's a hippodrome now." He shrugged. "You know your godfather, he wanted to keep her close, so he preferred she race here at home."

This information was a shock. Not the hippodrome itself — her godfather had written to her about the construction —  but she never imagined he would do this for Rio. Uncle Javi despised racing and had forbidden it years ago. The thought that he would bring the races home just so Rio could compete was unthinkable. Agatha had always assumed the expansion was purely for money and visibility for the town.

"Racing is the only thing she still does with passion... She's improved a lot since he gave her the hippodrome. She's home more, she's bonding with Javier again... He never truly liked the idea, but he did it for her, and it's worked out well. She's taken the lead on the responsibilities, organizing and promoting the races, caring for the horses. Honestly, I think it's been wonderful. She seems to be slowly finding her footing. She genuinely loves it, it's done her a lot of good," her father explained, as though sensing her thoughts. "It's just a start, but it's a good one. She has a race today at two in the afternoon."

Agatha narrowed her eyes, knowing exactly what he was doing, but he just rolled his eyes in feigned innocence.

"Don't tell your mother I told you this," he added.

"I have no idea what you're talking about, and even if I did, I wouldn't."

"Of course not, you hate her now," he said in a falsely stern voice. Agatha struggled to keep her face blank, but her father let out a laugh. "Yes, pure hatred. Not a drop of love left."

"Stop," Agatha warned softly, but she couldn't suppress the ghost of a smile that touched her lips, even with tears still drying on her cheeks.

"Oh, the intense hatred! I bet you never want to lay eyes on her again," he said as he walked away down the hall, laughing to himself.

Yes, such profound hatred. Agatha truly hated the fact that her father knew her so completely.

***

The lunch at the Maximoff house was the breath of fresh air Agatha desperately needed, allowing her to set aside the anxieties that had been whipping at her mind since she got home.

While she had built solid friendships in college, nothing matched the comfort of reuniting with her lifelong best friend. She firmly believed in having multiple best friends, especially since Alex and Wanda held distinct places in her life. Although Rio had always been her person, their bond was unique, something beyond mere friendship. They were fundamentally different people who complemented each other, fitting together like missing puzzle pieces. Wanda, however, was the friend who felt like an extension of herself — an equal spirit in a separate body.

Agatha and Wanda had been close since childhood, growing up together in school, but their best-friend status was solidified in the turbulent pre-teen years when their individual identities emerged. Unlike Rio, with whom Agatha was inseparable but shared few interests, Agatha and Wanda were similar. In high school, they moved within the it crowd — the athletes and cheerleaders. Agatha was a social butterfly, charismatic, and excelled at everything she tried, making her widely popular, just like Wanda. Rio, on the other hand, only had two friends, Bucky and Natasha, who were largely invisible and often avoided as the weirdos who caused trouble.

Wanda was always the school's it girl — the prettiest and the one everyone sought to impress, with Agatha right behind her. They were confidantes, almost sisters, and their bond survived Agatha's move to California.

Despite the distance, they maintained their full stream of communication. Finally being back, sprawled on Wanda's bed and recounting the year's events, was the first moment Agatha truly felt at home since arriving at Darby.

And it wasn't just Agatha who had a busy year. Despite Darby being a quiet town, a lot had happened in Wanda's life too.

Throughout high school, Wanda had dated the school quarterback, Victor Shade (aka Vision). Honestly, Agatha always thought he was a complete non-entity — the stereotypical jock with an oversized ego. She endured him only for Wanda's sake. Upon graduation, Victor received an athletic scholarship to Babson College, and rather than attempt a long-distance relationship, they broke up — a consequence made easier by Wanda's own college application rejections. Agatha hid her relief that Wanda had gotten rid of the jerk, fearing the breakup would hit her hard, but Wanda seemed happier than ever.

Wanda used the year to bolster her resume and re-evaluated her career path. Her high school goal was English, but this sabbatical year revealed a passion for pedagogy. She quickly landed an assistant position at the primary school and, within months, wrote to Agatha about her joy in working with children. Her days were now filled with volunteer projects, charity fairs, and assisting teachers, devoting herself unconditionally to the little ones.

More recently, Wanda’s letters had mentioned a person she was seeing. To Agatha's frustration, Wanda was coy about the identity but bubbled with happiness and lightness. She was clearly in love, piquing Agatha's curiosity, especially because Wanda's consistent use of the gender-neutral term person had Agatha's ears perked up. Agatha suspected her friend was exploring her sexuality, and now, face-to-face, she was determined to find out.

"You have no more excuses, Wanda," Agatha declared, lying on her stomach beside her best friend after enduring another long monologue about this person, who was supposedly the greatest thing to ever happen to her. "Now you are going to tell me who it is."

In response, Wanda's face instantly turned a deep red, and she hid her embarrassment in the pillow, making Agatha burst into laughter.

"Why are you being so mysterious?" she insisted.

"Because it's new," Wanda replied, her voice muffled by the pillow. Agatha simply smiled, shaking her head at the excessive shyness.

"Is it because it's a girl?" she prodded, using a tone that was both teasing and careful. Wanda's face shot up immediately, her eyes wide with surprise.

"How did you know it's a woman?"

"I didn't know, you just confirmed it for me," Agatha said with a playful shrug. Wanda let out an embarrassed groan and buried her flushed face back into the pillow. Agatha burst into laughter again. "Wanda, what is that about? I'm your best friend and I've been a lesbian since I was literally a kid!" she said, laughing and poking her shoulder to make her look up.

"I’m not embarrassed," Wanda countered, her face still pressed into the large pillow. "I'm not ashamed of her or being with her. It's just that—I think I'm in love with her, like, for real."

"And what's wrong with that? Hon, that is incredible, that's beautiful!"

Wanda tried to look serious, raising her head with narrowed eyes, analyzing every fleeting expression on Agatha's face, who was smiling with anticipation. Finally, she let out a huge sigh and admitted:

"It's Natasha."

Agatha’s mouth opened and closed as she struggled for words, but she quickly lost the fight against amusement, falling back onto the bed with a loud peal of laughter.

"I knew you'd laugh! I knew it!" Wanda accused, pointing at her, but Agatha couldn't stop giggling.

"I'm not laughing about that, it's just—"

"Yes, you are!"

"How did this even happen?" Agatha asked, trying to stifle her laughter. Wanda simply shrugged. "No, seriously, how did this happen?"

"The way we treated her in high school—it was so unfair," Wanda said, shaking her head. Her tone was serious and regretful, prompting Agatha to press her lips together to show she was taking the concern seriously. "She's not a weirdo, and even if she were, that didn't give us the right to act like that. She is the absolute sweetest person, Agatha, I swear!"

"Wanda, we were kids, it wasn't malicious. And we never explicitly treated them badly, not even Bucky. They just kept to themselves."

"But everyone disliked them because of us."

"I hung out with them sometimes," Agatha offered in her defense, earning an eye-roll from Wanda. "I even went out with them! You know it's true! I did it for Rio."

“But we never liked them."

"And was there much to like?" she countered, but she softened her tone under Wanda's accusatory gaze, shrugging again. "They barely talked to anyone. My dislike wasn't unfounded, they were an exclusive bubble, and they didn't like us either."

"We weren't very approachable either, especially towards them."

"I believe they're great, but we were just too different. Even Rio acknowledged that, no one liked her either, but I loved her because I truly knew her, and I didn't care what others thought. But that was high school, Wanda, everyone gets slapped with a label," Wanda nodded thoughtfully, clearly feeling remorse. "I believe Natasha is amazing. Rio always said so, but I never saw that side. She never spoke to me, even when I tried, and I tried hard. She was my girlfriend's best friend, I wanted her to like me."

"She's a little closed off, but that's just shyness," Wanda admitted, shrugging with compassionate brows. Agatha immediately felt sympathetic, unable to stop smiling at her friend's completely softened demeanor.

"I believe it, and I'd love to meet this side of her that's got you all smitten." Agatha poked her in the ribs. Wanda laughed, collapsing onto the bed next to her. "But first, I need the full story on how this happened."

Wanda shrugged, staring at the bedroom ceiling with a dreamy smile. She was utterly adorable, Agatha had never seen her this enchanted, not even when she spent years swearing Victor was a prince.

"She’s studying Economics and Administration at the University of Montana, but she hasn't moved. She still lives right here in Darby, it's just an hour's drive, so she commutes daily, but she needed extra money for school. She came to the school to see if she could teach judo classes in the afternoons. That's how we started talking. Since I’m an assistant, they tasked me with setting up her schedule, contacting parents, and all that stuff. We didn't talk much initially, but then, I don't know, suddenly, we were eating lunch together every day, and she'd drop me off at home late in the afternoon. Honestly, I just craved more time with her. She's so funny, and I love our conversations. We just naturally got closer," Wanda recounted breathily. "She only asked me out about three months later."

"And how was the date?" she asked, and Wanda smiled back, completely lost in her thoughts. Agatha wanted to laugh; dear god, her friend was utterly in love.

"It was no big deal, I don’t think we knew it was a date. We went to the town square, bought a pie to share, and had a few beers. We talked for hours. She was so nervous and after her third beer, she confessed she had something to tell me, adding she didn't want it to change anything between us: she admitted she'd had a huge crush on me since high school, even before I started dating Victor."

"I knew that," Agatha blurted out, surprised. Wanda's eyes widened instantly.

"How did you know that?" she retorted, indignant.

"Rio told me once, but I didn't take it seriously," she explained. Wanda playfully slapped her shoulder. "Come on, Wanda! Everyone was into you!"

"You should have told me!"

"And you would have dumped Victor for Natasha? We were in high school, you wouldn't even look in her direction."

"That's fair," she conceded, defeated.

"Now finish the story!" Agatha nudged her gently, eager for details. Wanda smiled again, kicking her feet like a giddy teenager.

"I was a little tipsy, too, which I think gave me the courage. I told her I wanted things to change because I was into her, too." She shrugged casually. Agatha's jaw dropped, genuinely impressed. "Then we kissed, and it was perfect."

"Look at you, all full of confidence!"

"I was really into her, and it was confusing at first because I was never into girls and then all these intense feelings, this constant desire to be with her. I don't know, you know? Suddenly, I was waiting for her to get to school, anxious for our time together. Even though I kept questioning it because she was a girl and this was new to me, but I decided it wasn't worth ignoring, because she is just wonderful..."

"I'm so happy for you. I'm sure she's incredible just for make you all giddy like this. Not that you have the best taste in dating, but..." Wanda slapped her arm again, and Agatha laughed. "Seriously, I'm genuinely happy for you."

"I know."

"Do your parents know?" Wanda nodded.

"I told my mom a few days after our first date, and since we kept going out, I told dad too. You know how they are, they organized a dinner just to meet her, and it was great. My mom fell head over heels for her, and so did my dad. Now she eats dinner here almost every night and even helps my mom cook."

"So, is it official?” Wanda shrugged, shaking her head slightly.

"We haven't put a label on it or anything yet, but we're together, and I think that’s what counts, right?" Agatha nodded. "It’s been, what, seven months? We’ll talk about titles eventually, but yeah, we’re dating."

"And what’s that been like? I mean, you said it’s new. How was... you know..." Wanda gasped in mock horror, but Agatha shook her head, laughing. "No, you absolutely have to tell me! You always demanded to know every detail about me and Rio!"

"I was so nervous the first time, but she was incredibly sweet and attentive. She kissed my entire body, and it was... I've honestly never felt anything like it!" She sighed, closing her eyes, and Agatha let out a faint chuckle. "It felt like she worshipped me. It was better than anything I've ever experienced."

"Welcome to the club, girl!" Agatha said, laughing, and Wanda rolled her eyes.

"After the third time, there wasn't much left to learn. She already knew everything I liked, and I knew how she liked it, what she wanted, the way she asks me to—"

"I don't need any more details; I've heard quite enough," Agatha interrupted, dissolving into laughter.

Wanda then rolled onto her stomach, propping her face in her hands. She looked at Agatha with raised eyebrows, her eyes brimming with curiosity.

"Now it's your turn."

"My turn?" Agatha asked, lifting an eyebrow, which earned her another eye-roll from Wanda.

"Don't play dumb. I want to know about you and Tessa."

Agatha instantly scoffed, grabbing a pillow and covering her face with it.

"Why does everyone keep asking me this?"

"Why? Agatha, you've been writing about her for months!"

"And that's all there is. I haven't skipped any details, it's nothing serious."

"You've been hooking up for months, you send countless photos of you two doing everything together, always with a massive smile, and in two weeks, you're spending New Year's Eve in New York together. Are you seriously trying to convince me this isn't serious?"

"It’s not. We’re getting to know each other and hanging out, but that's the extent of it! There’s nothing to discuss. It’s casual, not serious, we’re just dating." Wanda narrowed her eyes, clearly suspicious. "I told her a thousand times that I can't commit right now, and she respects that." Agatha shrugged. "We are not together, not like together together."

"And why not, Agatha? She seems wonderful, totally into you. She respected your boundaries, and she’s been amazing since you gave her a chance. Don't you think she deserves a real chance?"

Agatha let out a heavy huff of air, hugging the pillow tight.

"How can I possibly give her a chance when I'm still in love with someone else?"

"Agatha, for god's sake! After everything Rio did!"

"I don't control my heart, I don't control my feelings, Wanda," Agatha said, sitting up to face her with complete seriousness. "Yes, she made a terrible mistake, and I'm hurt, but that isn't the only thing I feel. I love her, I miss her."

"She cheated on you!" Wanda almost yelled, completely indignant.

"I need to talk to her, Wanda," Agatha said, her voice sorrowful as she looked down. "You know things were bad when I left, she didn't even say goodbye. Too much was left unsaid between us, and that is not how I'm going to put a final period on everything we had."

"You are not children anymore. Not everything requires justification or clarification. Why are you setting yourself up for more pain? You don't need closure, Agatha, she already gave you that between the lines."

"I don't want it to end that way," she insisted. Wanda shook her head, muttering how foolish she was being. "I know we aren't children, and that is exactly why we need to talk, to discuss everything that was left unsaid, how she felt, how she feels, and I have so much I need to get off my chest, too. Her choice was silence, but I have a lot to say."

"And to what end, Agatha? What good will come of it?"

"Wanda, I’m twenty years old. I know that's nothing compared to the years ahead, but twenty years is my entire life, and I spent that whole life with her, since we were children, before we understood our feelings. Everything I am, I was with her, always with her. I cannot just turn my back on that."

"She already did, and you did too," Wanda insisted. "She made her choices after you left, and you’ve made yours. You have a whole life waiting outside of here, and now, you have Tessa."

"I like Tessa, but I won't dive headfirst into a relationship with someone else without first making peace with everything Rio and I shared. It wouldn't be fair, it wouldn't be right for me."

Wanda said nothing more, simply shaking her head before settling back down beside Agatha. There was nothing left to say, nothing could change Agatha's feelings or persuade her from following her own path.

After a long silence, Wanda looked at her again, sighing deeply. She saw the intensity in her friend's knit brows, the sheer weight of emotion Agatha was struggling to contain. The hurt was visible, yet underneath it, Agatha’s enduring love for Riandra was so strong that her internal conflict was plain to see.

"How is she?" Agatha finally asked. Wanda sighed again, but Agatha pressed on, pleading with her eyes. "After that letter in May, you never mentioned her again, and I know she wasn't well. My dad told me." Wanda remained silent. "Wanda, I deserve to know. I need to know. And I know you're holding back, you're dating her best friend, you know things." Wanda sighed one last time, recognizing that her only option was to be the truthful friend she was.

"She's better," she finally conceded, and Agatha let out a breath of relief. "She’s not the old Rio, but she’s definitely better. Since Javier finished the hippodrome, she’s been around more. Natasha told me she’s heavily involved with the racing, investing her own money and taking it seriously. It seems racing has given her a real sense of commitment and responsibility. She hasn't exactly turned a corner, she's still a mess, still drinks, still disappears for days, but she’s home more often, and she's back to working on the ranch. Nat said Javier is happier, and Rio seems content sometimes. They’re even working together: Rio asked Natasha to help manage the money, and she's setting up the accounts. It sounds like Rio has some future projects planned."

"What kind of projects?" Agatha asked. Wanda shrugged.

"I don't know the details, but at least she’s no longer drifting aimlessly, living every day like it's her last." When Agatha's face twisted in pain, Wanda apologized with her eyes. "I’m sorry, but she is a mess, Agatha, and I truly believe you're better off now, building your own life away from it."

"To continue building my life, I have to make peace with this, with her." Wanda grimaced, clearly disagreeing. "I need to see her, I need to talk to her, whether you like it or not, but I really wanted you to help." Agatha raised her eyebrows expectantly, and Wanda narrowed hers.

"Help with what, exactly?"

"It’s been a year since we saw each other. I'm not ready to just spring her at her house, especially with everyone there, and all eyes on us. I want to see her first, even if it's from a distance." Agatha shrugged. Wanda squinted, suspicious. "I know she's racing today, soon..."

"No," Wanda immediately refused.

"Wanda, please!"

"You're already so gooey! What kind of closure is this where you seem desperate to run into her? Absolutely not!"

"Wanda, please, I'm begging you!" Agatha insisted. "I'm going either way, with or without you, but I'd much rather have you by my side."

Wanda scoffed, shaking her head as she stared at her friend. Agatha looked like a child pleading with a parent — eyebrows knit, gaze sweet, on the verge of collapsing to her knees. When Wanda groaned in frustration, Agatha smiled, knowing she had won. But Wanda pointed a sharp finger at her:

"I am only going with you to make sure you don't do anything stupid. Let that be perfectly clear."

***

"You shouldn't drink before you race," Natasha murmured, frowning at her best friend, who was chugging beer can while walking toward the hippodrome track.

In reply, Rio simply burped in her face and tossed the empty can aside before they were within sight of the stands.

"It's a horse, not a car, Natasha," she said dismissively, immediately rushing off toward Bucky, who was fastening the final straps on her saddle. The other riders were already lined up. She was late compared to them, but she was on time and needed little preparation.

Ever since her father converted the equestrian center into a race track, Rio had been subjected to constant sermons from almost everyone around her. Even Natasha had a lecture ready — warnings about drinking too much, prohibitions against drinking before a race, and criticisms about partying out of town. It felt as if they were all trying to keep her locked in a cage, and she honestly believed they would if they could.

Nothing she did was good enough, something was always wrong, and someone was always ready to point a finger at her slightest misstep. She felt that in their collective effort to keep her in line, they forgot she was a person with her own feelings and desires. Despite their good intentions, this was her battle to fight alone. At the end of the day, all she truly wanted was space, though she couldn't articulate why.

She wished the track had no end, that she could run aimlessly for hours. She wanted to race, galloping down a path with no destination, stopping only when her horse gave out. She longed for a track that would lead her somewhere — anywhere — that could rip the constant agony from her chest. But it was a fantasy. No matter how far or fast she ran, she would always return to the same place, burdened by the same feelings and frustrations.

The harsh truth was that no matter where she went or how much ground she covered, in the end, she was still trapped inside her own skin, she still had to live her own life. This was a grief no one understood, and she simply wanted to be left alone.

"Is he ready?" Rio asked, stroking her horse's mane, and Bucky nodded.

"The way you like it," he replied with a mocking salute, and she cracked a smile. "The betting is over eight thousand on you already. It's not a fortune, but it's pretty good for a race in good ol' Darby."

"We should head to Bell Crossing later. I'm sure it won't be hard to get a good ride if we promise two or three percent of the winnings."

"I'm game," Bucky said with a huge grin.

"Don't you have a dinner to go to later today?" Natasha interrupted, addressing Rio, who merely shrugged without turning around. She was squatting by her horse, hands on her thighs, inspecting the animal.

"There's dinner at my house every night. They're totally accustomed to me skipping out now and then," was her dismissive reply.

"I thought you wanted to see Agatha," Natasha said, and Rio instantly stood up, her eyebrows knitted in confusion.

"Agatha?"

"She arrived today. Wanda told me her family is having dinner at your house," Natasha explained, as if it were obvious. Suddenly, Rio's heart began pounding uncontrollably in her chest, initiating a frantic inner race that she had no hope of controlling. "Didn't you know? I know things are rough between you two, but she's still writing, isn't she?"

Rio was frozen solid. Time seemed to warp into slow motion, and her vision and hearing blurred. Inside, everything was moving at a terrifying speed: her pulse hammered, blood surged through her veins, and her breathing became shallow.

"Rio? Are you okay?" Natasha snapped her fingers right in front of her face.

She desperately wanted to scream "no," but she was mute. She couldn't say anything. She couldn't explain that yes, Agatha was still writing, but she had no idea what the letters contained. She didn't read them — not because she didn't want to, but because she couldn't. She wanted to confess that she didn't know if anything remained between them, she had never written back. She wanted to say so much, yet the shock of the news, combined with her general anxiety, kept her silent. Some things were deeply personal — issues she kept locked away, fighting daily not to confront.

Every single day, she woke up and prayed to be better, to be good enough, to stop being so stupid, but her prayers, the same ones she'd offered since childhood, were never answered. God had no ear for her pleas. Her only choice was to feign normalcy and avoid the truth. There were things she intended to avoid until her dying day.

"Isn't that Agatha?" Bucky pointed toward the stands. Rio, still reeling, spun around to look and felt an internal explosion of fireworks when she saw her.

After nearly a year, there she stood, in all her glory, exactly as Rio remembered. She didn't have to try to recall her, she thought about her every day. Her features, the intensity of her eyes — all perfectly memorized. Not a single day passed that she hadn't seen that face in her mind. That face she loved so much.

Rio felt paralyzed, unable to draw a breath. She was even more beautiful than Rio remembered. Her hair was longer now, her skin lightly tanned, she looked like an angel. Her angel. Rio couldn't process her presence. She had assumed that after Agatha skipped her summer visit, she had put down roots in Los Angeles and wasn't coming back. Yet, there she stood, as if no time had passed at all.

An overwhelming impulse nearly sent Rio scrambling towards her. She wanted to scale the stands and cradle Agatha's face, feeling tears sting her eyes. She longed to look into those eyes, to touch her, to hold her hand. She wanted to confess that she was sorry, that she was an arrogant idiot who never learned to apologize, say goodbye, or move on. She wanted to promise she wished she had read every letter and written back, offering to kneel right there to swear her sincerity. But she couldn't. Not without revealing the devastating truth — the truth that would shatter every dream they’d built, every façade Rio had maintained while Agatha believed they would go to college, graduate, and travel the world together.

That truth was hers alone to keep.

But god, the intensity of her need was overwhelming — that agonizing longing, the urge to hug, kiss, and see her. She nearly bolted, but the starting siren cut through the moment. Bucky had to shake her, yelling that she needed to get on the horse.

But with Agatha's eyes finally fixed on hers, even from the distance, Rio was rooted to the spot. She had a race to win, but all she wanted was to stay planted there, staring at Agatha. Even from afar, she felt as if Agatha could see right through her, soul and all. She tried to smile, but it likely came out as a grimace. Agatha offered a small, acknowledging smile in return. Rio opened her mouth, intending to call out, but Bucky was quicker, dragging her away by the arm.

"Are you insane? Do you want to be disqualified?" he hissed through clenched teeth. Rio couldn't respond. Her feet shuffled across the dirt track, yet her head remained cranked backward.

Agatha was home. She had come back. She was here.

***

Rio burst into the house like a thunderclap, shoving the doors open in a chaotic rush that stood in sharp contrast to the peaceful scene before her: her father and brother calmly playing chess on large floor cushions near the living room coffee table.

"Whoa, watch out for the bull!” Benito exclaimed with a childish laugh, hugging his knees as he observed Riandra's intense expression as she marched toward them. Javier chuckled, settling back comfortably onto his cushion, supporting his weight on his arms.

"What is it, mi cielo?" he murmured to his daughter, utterly unruffled by her storm; he was long accustomed to it. "Didn't the race go well?"

"Why did nobody tell me Agatha was back?" she demanded, hands planted firmly on her hips, her indignation high. Father and brother exchanged a knowing look before turning back to her.

"And you didn't know?" Javier inquired mildly, his gentle tone only making her huff. "She wrote to everyone. She said she was returning over a month ago."

"Even I got a letter," Benito chimed in with a smile.

"Nobody asked you, asshat," she snapped, turning back to her father, still furious. "I didn't know! Why did you assume I did? Why didn't you just tell me?"

"Mi cielo, last week I took a stack of her letters to your room. She writes weekly. How was I supposed to know you didn’t know? Everyone else knew, it's no surprise. That's why I arranged this dinner tonight, and Lilia told you the Harkness were coming," he explained, stating the obvious.

"Yes, the Harkness, Richard and Evanora. I didn't think Agatha would fly all the way from California for a low-key dried-meat dinner on a weekday."

"She's on break, honey. Christmas vacation. She's spending Christmas here. Didn't she tell you?"

"I haven't read the damned letters!" she yelled, already racing for the stairs. "How could Agatha just show up and nobody mention it?! Not a soul! Not even Benito the blabbermouth. I swear to god, why did you all keep silent? What time is she arriving? I need to get ready and..." Her voice trailed off as she disappeared upstairs.

Javier and Benito looked at each other once more, and then, inevitably, burst into laughter.

"She's still not over her, is she?" Benny asked between laughs. Javier shook his head, affectionately running his hand through his son's curls.

"No, frijolito, not at all."

"I hope Agatha hasn't gotten over her either," Benito whispered hopefully. To this, Javier merely tilted his head slightly. “I miss them together.”

"That's entirely up to them, buddy. Only time will tell."

Chapter 7: nostalgia

"In another life, I would make you stay, so I don't have to say you were the one that got away" – The One That Got Away, Kate Perry

Continuation of the Flashback from the Previous Chapter — Nineteen Years Ago

Furtively, while the adults talked in the dining room, Rio leaned against the bar and took a long swig directly from the rum bottle. Her only judge was her brother, watching from the upstairs corridor, his eyes narrowed, his head shaking in clear disapproval. Rio’s silent response was a middle finger and a sour expression, a fierce signal for him to mind his own business. Internally trembling, she shook her head and let out a huff, the alcohol’s heat intensifying her agitation. Anxiety made her skin prickle, and she was beginning to sweat.

Richard, Evanora, and Lilia had arrived earlier. Their presence was a familiar constant; her father regularly hosted these joint dinners. Though the gatherings themselves were not unusual, Rio had lacked the courage to attend in a long time, not after everything that had transpired. She knew she had forfeited her right to belong at these family occasions — a fact Evanora, especially, made piercingly clear with every sharp glance. No one had forgiven her for the catastrophic end of things with Agatha, and she couldn't blame them; she hadn't forgiven herself, either. Forgiveness was unattainable; she had ruined everything, a destructive pattern that was becoming her specialty.

Although no one dared to speak up, she knew that beneath all the family cordiality, everyone was still angry with her. Honestly, while it stung occasionally, their anger meant nothing compared to the self-loathing she felt. She threw everything away because she was a coward, and though she had disappointed everyone — especially Agatha — at the end of the day, she was the one who had to face her own reflection, the one who put her head on the pillow and dealt with her own demons.

For all those years, she had been a fraud, a successful deception everyone had bought into wholeheartedly. But at the end of the day, she was just Riandra, and the ranch was the sole constant, the only life she truly understood. She was no prodigy or genius; far from it. All she truly wanted was for time to stand still, for everything to remain exactly as it was. She found contentment in staying right there in Darby, shielded from the world’s ambitious promises and challenges. She had everything she needed: a home, a ranch, family, and horses. She didn’t yearn for more, and deep down, she knew it wasn’t meant for her. She was anchored here; she wasn’t like Agatha.

Agatha, she thought, letting out a long, heavy sigh.

Agatha was like a caged bird; though she sang beautifully by the window every day, all she wanted was the freedom to soar. Agatha was so much bigger than this place, too big for the entire town. She was fiercely intelligent, brilliant, and possessed such a restless ambition that Rio could never hope to match it. For years, Rio had merely observed and complied, letting Agatha's ideas lead, catering to her every wish, and reflecting every one of Agatha’s smiles. She loved watching her little bird sing, but deep down, she knew that when the gate opened, that bird would fly away. She loved Agatha too much to keep her caged. Agatha had that fire in her eyes, that depth that thirsts for more, absorbing everything around her in search of the new. Agatha was born to explore the world, but Rio had roots.

Despite understanding Agatha’s deep desire to fly, Rio had clung to the hope that once the cage was opened, her bird might choose to rest on her branches nonetheless. But Agatha flew, and Rio couldn't blame her decision; she accepted it. While she silently endured all the judgment aimed at her current behavior, she felt their intense condemnation was unfair. Agatha chose to leave; all Rio did was stay.

She couldn't grasp why everyone condemned her for staying. No one criticized Agatha for leaving; she was, instead, praised as a prodigy — encouraged to conquer the world in California. They wanted her to go, wanted her to live, but what about Rio? Couldn't she claim the same right? Couldn't she live? She didn't want the life of big cities or universities; her existence was sacredly rooted in the town where she was born and raised. Why couldn't she claim that life for herself? Why were her choices invalid? Why did she always have to be the one to concede? Why couldn't Agatha have been the one to stay? Why was Rio expected to follow her? She wasn't a goddamn keychain or some mimicking parrot; she was an individual with her own flaws, perspectives, and principles — she wasn't merely an extension of Agatha. She bristled at the way they minimized her, framing her as a helpless dependent who needed Agatha to grow, breathe, and exist, and how openly they assumed she had no prospects without her. Perhaps there was a sliver of truth to that — she felt diminished without Agatha — but she was still something: a lie, a fraud, yes, but she still had the right to choose, or at least she should have.

The pain was a corrosive fungus, an almost imperceptible flaw that had slowly metastasized through her core. Over the years, it had spread from head to toe, leaving her a mere carrier of that emotional blight. She had striven for so long, trying to be better, trying to become someone of substance, yet she was an expert in failing at every attempt. She had even failed Agatha, the one person she desperately wanted to impress. In truth, every effort she made was ultimately for Agatha, more so than for her own father. Still, she failed. She had metaphorically swum across entire oceans only to drown right on the shore, sinking in the failure she tried so desperately to conceal. Perhaps it was a curse, an innate corruption, something born with her that prevented her from ever being complete, destined to be perpetually half while everyone else around her shone brilliantly.

Rio was a monument to the almost. She had the almost-perfect family, save for the loss of her mother; she was almost the perfect daughter, but for her involvement in racing; she had almost made things work with Agatha, but for the profound brokenness within herself. She constantly hung by a thread, a rope she felt tightening around her own neck — and she couldn't bear to let Agatha be choked by it, too. She loved her too much to condemn her to an almost life. Agatha deserved a whole, complete existence, with everything she ever dreamed of and more, a life Rio knew she could never provide, no matter how convincing her pretense.

But the hurt was searing. It hurt intensely, and she had no idea how to make it stop—no amount of running or drinking could quell the pain, which persisted, pulsing inside her, hammering as loud as her own heart. Rio had few certainties in life, but Agatha was her absolute constant, more reliable than the midday sun breaking the horizon, surer than the rain when the smell of dampness rose from the dry earth, more assured than the harvest when the vineyard leaves darkened. Letting her go felt like ripping the roots right out of her own chest, like tearing out a force of nature.

But how could it be any different? Agatha wanted to fly, and Rio had roots.

Rio genuinely didn't know much; academics had never been her strength. Simple concepts evaded her, she couldn't grasp the abstraction of numbers, and words often blurred too quickly in her mind. However, she was intimately familiar with the ways of nature. She observed enough to know when the young were ready to be weaned, when little birds instinctively knew to leave the nest. She knew her horses by sight, by every subtle movement, and through this knowledge, she recognized that people weren't fundamentally different from the animals. She understood that Agatha belonged to one species, and she to another; they had simply been unlucky enough to fall in love. But now, as adults, Rio recognized that each needed to inhabit her native environment. Agatha needed to find hers, while Rio settled for this one — a fate not chosen, only accepted.

The sudden, loud chime of the doorbell shattered her thoughts, and she nearly stumbled in her rush to answer. She knew she shouldn't; she needed to keep her distance, but the impulse was irresistible. She had to see her, to witness her presence. The excited murmurs from the dining room confirmed her arrival, and Rio needed to see her first, knowing she likely wouldn't get a clear chance later. It would be a stroke of luck just to greet her, especially after everything that had happened; she couldn't miss this moment. Reaching the door, she saw Benito running up and shoved him hard by the shoulders.

"Get out!" she hissed in a low whisper, startling the boy, whose eyes widened. He shook his head. "Now, buttface!"

"I miss her too!" he grumbled under his breath, his eyebrows furrowed in indignation.

"She's my girlfriend, not yours!"

"She's not your girlfriend anymore," he muttered with a laugh. Rio scoffed, pushing him again, this time harder.

"Thanks for the reminder, now scram!" She shoved his shoulders, listening to his protesting sneakers drag across the wooden floor.

"I’m going to tell dad she’s at the door! He’s going to come out here!"

"Then go! What are you waiting for?" she snarled. With a final huff, Benito shuffled down the long corridor. Rio took a stabilizing breath, composed herself, straightened her stance, and ran her hands through her hair before pulling the door open.

She opened the door abruptly, her eyebrows pinching in a painful grimace as she saw Agatha's blue eyes widen in shock, the smile on her lips faltering. Throughout the months of separation, Rio had occasionally dreamt of this reunion, always imagining Agatha rushing toward her, hugging her tightly, her husky laugh echoing, her face buried in the curve of Rio’s neck. She had never envisioned this: the visible shock, the way Agatha’s shoulders stiffened, as if she had been expecting anyone but Rio.

"Hi," Rio whispered, her voice weak and nervous, breaking the silence.

"Hi," Agatha replied, her brows still knitted. Rio furrowed hers as well, seeing the storm of emotion that crossed Agatha’s face and thundered in her blue eyes.

They shared a childhood habit of gazing intently into each other’s eyes. They knew each other so well that words were often superfluous; they communicated solely through glances, always perfectly synchronized, as if sharing a single mind. But now, staring into that blue sea, Rio felt they were speaking alien languages. She saw a tangle of conflicting emotions—hurt, affection, confusion, anger—all at once, rendering interpretation impossible. It was as if Agatha was silently screaming at her in a language Rio couldn’t recognize.

In silence, they were lost in each other, as if trying to recognize one another.

Agatha was as beautiful as ever, but small details about her were different, and Rio noticed every single one. Every feature of Agatha's face was imprinted on her memory, and in the charged silence, under Agatha's gaze, Rio meticulously absorbed all the subtle changes and she hoped that by looking at them, she might grasp everything that had transpired over the last twelve months. She noted Agatha's tanned skin, her shoulders almost sunburnt yet seemingly soft. She had a new, beautiful radiance. Her hair was lighter and longer, her freckles fewer, and her demeanor seemed more serious—perhaps hinted at by the faint mark of glasses on her nose. Rio’s chest painfully constricted from the realization that she didn't know, that she was observing these details without context. A hand seemed to squeeze her heart, crushing it with the knowledge that Agatha had constructed a complete life separate from hers, a life about which Rio knew nothing. She was no longer included. She was no longer a part of Agatha.

"Tesoro!" Javier's loud, warm voice flooded the house, shattering the trance between them. Both girls blinked, still staring, but they had no time to compose themselves. Rio’s father quickly nudged his daughter aside to embrace his goddaughter, hugging her so tightly he lifted her off the floor, swinging her like a little girl.

"Tio Javi!" Agatha exclaimed, laughing and hugging him fiercely in return. Rio sighed, watching Agatha close her eyes, resting her head affectionately on Javier's shoulder. She yearned for that same embrace, that affection, but deep down, she knew it wasn't deserved.

"I missed you so much, nena," he murmured, his voice thick with emotion.

"Me too." Still held by Javier, Agatha opened her eyes and looked deeply into Rio's brown, furrowed eyes. "I missed everything." She said this while staring directly at Rio, who felt a wrenching pain in her chest from the frantic pounding of her heart. "I missed you so much."

How could she? Rio wondered, her eyebrows still knit tight. After all this time, after the silence, after everything Rio had done to push her away and encourage her to move on. How was it possible she missed her? She shouldn't. Rio's heart was beating so fiercely she could feel the throb in her mouth; it was hammering so loudly she feared everyone could hear or see her chest vibrating.

The longing Rio felt for Agatha was bigger than anything in the world, beyond measure. Perhaps it was the greatest force in existence, for Rio had never witnessed anything approaching its intensity. It felt like an anchor fixed to her heart, ensuring she saw Agatha's face every time she closed her eyes to sleep. It snagged on her ribs, causing a physical ache, a feeling like a punch every time Agatha crossed her mind during a mundane moment. Agatha was the constant voice in her head, the person she thought of when she looked up at the sky, when she saw the stars and wondered — every single day — which part of the sky Agatha was observing from California, and if it could possibly be more beautiful than this one.

"Vámonos! Everyone is waiting for you!" Javier said excitedly, giving Agatha one final squeeze. As Agatha walked past Rio through the doorway, she offered a small, awkward, shy smile, just the corner of her mouth lifting, and Rio managed to smile back in return.

It was something, at least.

Letting out a drawn-out sigh, Rio closed the door. When she turned, she was met by the conspiratorial glare of her brother. The little bastard hadn't gone to the kitchen; he had climbed the stairs to watch their entire interaction from the doorway. Benito shook his head in judgment, and Rio's only response was an eye-roll and a flip of the middle finger.

***

It didn't take long for the dining room to become flooded with nostalgia, as if not a single day had passed since graduation, as if this were just another random evening where they gathered out of habit. Even Rio caught herself smiling faintly, feeling the warmth of familiarity in her chest while exchanging furtive, shy glances with Agatha, who was seated directly across the table. She wondered how it was possible that things had changed so drastically when, right now, everything seemed to be in its rightful place, just as it had always been.

But it wasn't the same; it only seemed so — it was just another almost.

If things genuinely were as they once were, Agatha would be sitting beside her, laughing while piling food onto Rio’s plate, who would nod with an arm draped over Agatha's chair, telling her to add just a little more. And someone would surely joke that by forty, Rio would have a round belly from her girlfriend stuffing her face. Instead, Agatha passed the potato salad across the table, avoiding her eyes, and Rio mechanically filled her own plate without any appetite.

Only they seemed to register the difference. The others, if they noticed — and they certainly must have — made sure not to let it show. Even with the distance between them, it did feel a little like the way things used to be. Everyone was there, right where they should be. Agatha was home, laughing at her father's jokes, enthusiastically endorsing all of Benito's wild ideas, and complimenting Lilia's cooking. Everyone was eating, drinking, and talking simultaneously. Rio was the only one silent, feeling like she was watching a scene from her favorite comfort show. Agatha was smiling in her house, as if no time had passed and nothing had happened, as if everything was in its most perfect order. Rio felt her shoulders slump. This was precisely what she had always wanted — for Agatha to accept that this place was hers — but what truly hurt, especially seeing her there, comfortable and at home, was knowing that Agatha did not agree. Rio knew Agatha did not believe this was her rightful place.

Despite her silence, Rio paid rapt attention to the conversation, straining to catch every detail out of curiosity. Apparently, her father hadn't been exaggerating; Agatha really did write almost every day, and not just to Rio, but to everyone. Of course, Rio was the only one who hadn't read the damned letters, because everyone else seemed to know exactly what Agatha was doing in Los Angeles and how her life was unfolding. Rio tried to piece things together from the conversational fragments. She now knew Agatha was a disastrous surfer, played on the volleyball team, had taken a road trip mid-year, and had visited several towns, even other states near California. When Agatha started mentioning someone named Alex, Rio's eyebrow lifted, but she glanced at Benito, who shook his head, signaling that it was nothing to worry about.

Agatha spoke with animation, unable to suppress her laughter, a smile a practically permanent fixture on her lips. Rio could clearly see her genuine happiness, how much she was thriving in that new life. Rio had never witnessed her so excited, her eyes truly sparkling. When Agatha began discussing college, her face ignited with a glow Rio had never seen before — she spoke with zest, with palpable passion. She was living her dream in a way she never had at home. She had never been this radiant in Darby; she was clearly blossoming. It was beautiful to witness. Rio felt a deep ache in her chest, thinking that Agatha had never been this happy back home, yet simultaneously found profound joy in seeing her this way.

Agatha needed to fly; Rio would never cage her.

The entire dinner revolved around her, as it should, and Rio forced a façade of normalcy, pretending to feel nothing at all, though in reality, she felt on the verge of tears. Her intense longing for Agatha — her voice, her scent — made her heart hammer wildly as she absorbed all the stories, her mind frantically filling in the unspoken gaps. It was overwhelming, and she felt increasingly suffocated. At times, their eyes met, and it felt as though Agatha was speaking solely to her, smiling faintly in her direction, wanting her to know, wanting to share everything. Yet, even as Rio desperately wished to hear and know every detail of her life, those words felt like powerful hands squeezing her throat, punishing her for her absence, making her physically feel the distance between them — both the literal mileage and the emotional chasm Rio herself had created.

"You went to Vancouver?" Javier asked, his thick accent slightly mangling the pronunciation. Agatha nodded, swallowing a piece of roast beef.

"Alex's family is from there; that's where we spent the mid-year break. It's incredibly beautiful, padrinho; you would love it."

"And where else did you go?" he asked, interested, and Agatha tilted her head in thought. Rio watched her, trying to mask the rush of adoration, the urgent need to know everything. "You’ve become quite the traveler."

"She’s going to New York," Evanora stated proudly, making Agatha’s face light up. "She’s spending New Year’s Eve in Times Square with Tessa."

Tessa. That was a name Rio hadn't heard before. When she felt the atmosphere at the table tense, her father quickly looking at her with wide eyes and Richard looking down, wiping his lips with a napkin, Rio frowned, feeling a stab in her chest that left her almost breathless.

Agatha's blue eyes, now alarmed, met hers, the smile instantly vanishing; she looked startled, as if caught red-handed. Their gazes locked, the astonished blue facing the stormy brown. Rio had never heard that name and instantly suspected it wasn't a coincidence — perhaps they had deliberately shielded her from this knowledge. She recognized that look, the thundering confusion in Agatha's expression, having seen it countless times when Agatha did something she knew would upset her: eyes filled with regret.

Agatha had moved on.

Jerking her gaze away, Rio pressed her lips together tightly, her face flushing as her vision threatened to blur with tears — she absolutely could not cry, not here. But internally, a hurricane raged, her thoughts shaken by thunder and screams, leaving her feeling she wouldn't survive the turmoil. She couldn't fault Agatha for moving on, not after everything Rio had done; it was foolish to assume Agatha wouldn't find someone else — surely there was an eager line of hopefuls in California — yet the pain was intense, a knife plunged deep into her chest, a knife she herself had wielded.

The conversation continued, but Rio heard nothing; the voices were reduced to a distant, meaningless buzz. Her eyes, fixed rigidly on a spot on the table, saw nothing but the tragedy unfolding inside her. For the rest of the night, she did not utter another word.

***

The customary finale to every family dinner was the gathering around the backyard bonfire to drink some of the house vintage wine. It was an almost sacred ritual for her father; he loved to talk, tell stories, sing, and listen to the night. He often did this with her and Benny, teaching them to listen to what nature had to say and how the voices of the wilderness had much to teach. When the Harknesses joined, it became a full-fledged celebration, sitting around the fire and talking for hours. Rio remembered how it used to be: she and Agatha nestled close in the hammock, listening and laughing, whispering about their parents' convoluted conversations.

But now, what was before no longer existed.

As soon as dinner concluded, they quickly began clearing the table to commence the usual ritual — it was tradition. However, instead of rushing to grab beer and bury herself in the hammock, Rio simply nodded and walked straight out the door while Agatha remained inside washing dishes. What Rio didn't know was that, through the window, blue eyes were watching her leave.

"Mi cielo!" When she was well past the main house's perimeter fence, Rio heard her father call out. She looked over her shoulder, turning to face him while continuing to walk backward. "¿Adónde vas?” Rio merely shrugged and kept walking across the ranch, not looking back, leaving behind a sighing Javier, who shook his head.

"It's hard for her, brother," Richard said, gently patting Javier's shoulder. Javier shook his head, let out a long breath, and sank deep into his large rocking chair. Richard joined him, sitting in the armchair nearby, filling the wine glasses that rested on a wooden stump beside the crackling bonfire.

"I know. I wish it wasn't this way," Javier lamented, chewing on a toothpick. "She used to be so happy, running around these fields, smiling from ear to ear, and now, even though she's right in front of me, I don't know where my daughter went."

"She's a tough nut to crack," Richard murmured, handing a glass to his friend, who accepted it gratefully. "She just needs time; both of them need time."

"At least Agatha is happy."

"She's finding herself," Richard said, nodding in agreement. Javier took a long sip of wine and nodded back. Both men knew that despite Agatha's happiness in her long-dreamed-of life in California, she still carried a heavy burden from what she had left behind. "Rio will find herself too, she always had a knack for it." He laughed lightly, prompting an inquiring raised eyebrow from Javier. "She spent her entire life getting herself lost out here in the brush, and she always managed to find her way back. She's home, Javi. If there's anywhere for her to find herself, it’s here. Give it time, brother."

Javier looked over his shoulder, making sure the women were still in the kitchen before he spoke. He disliked discussing the subject in front of Evanora, knowing her strong feelings.

"Who would have thought it would end up in this mess, huh?" Javier murmured, shaking his head as he recalled simpler times when the two girls ran hand-in-hand across the ranch, their lives revolving around one another. "Our girls... they truly made a mess."

"Yeah, but that's what girls do.”

"Where's Rio?" Benito ran up, leaning against the side of the large wooden gate, breathless as if he'd just completed a marathon, clutching his sister's guitar.

"Solo dios lo sabe, mijo," Javier replied, settling deeper into his chair and watching out of the corner of his eye as the boy's euphoric expression wilted.

From the large kitchen window, Agatha, who had seen and heard the entire exchange, took a deep breath, gripping the porcelain plate under the faucet with both hands. She felt her heart hammer painfully in her chest. They truly had made a mess, and even though she knew it wasn't her responsibility to fix it, she couldn't stop the urge to run after Rio.

***

Agatha knew that this mess was not hers. In truth, she had done absolutely everything for things to remain in their most perfect order; if it depended on her, everything would be the same, nothing would have changed. God is her witness—and so is Alex Cabot, who makes sure she doesn't forget—of how she spent weeks and months writing to Rio, and how she tried to ensure their connection remained constant, striving to make the distance purely physical. She honestly did everything she could, and had there been anything more, she would have done it. Yet, she couldn't suppress the urge to fix everything — there had to be a solution; they could work this out.

She felt foolish marching through the tall brush in flat sandals in the dead of night, the leaves pricking her ankles as she muttered on her way to the stables. Damn the brush, damn the sandals, damn the shorts, and damn Riandra. She felt ridiculous for failing to resist the impulse to chase after her, for believing they could repair things, for wanting everything returned to the way it was. She felt like an idiot for craving Rio's love again, and deep down, she was furious knowing that Rio did want her, knowing Rio was hurting, yet still created the disaster that tore them apart.

Rio chose this; she deliberately opted for a silence that spoke louder than any letter could. She wanted the separation. Rio was the one who put the chasm between them, who pushed Agatha away when all Agatha desired was to pull her close. Her silence was a loud, clear message, and Agatha had finally understood. Riandra had no right to look at her with those stormy brown eyes, no right to frown upon learning Agatha had moved on when Rio was the first to walk away. Riandra had no right to open that door with such tenderness and expectation in her eyes. She did not have the right. All Agatha had done was move forward despite her; she hadn't chosen this separation.

Agatha felt foolish because even now — after suffering alone, sending letters into the void, and inventing excuses for Rio's absence — she felt that urgent pull to go to her, to understand the truth, and to force Rio to articulate everything bottled up in that months-long silence. She urgently needed to be near her, to look into her eyes, to nestle in her arms. The intensity of missing her was enough to bring tears to her eyes. And she hated herself for it, hated the knot in her throat that pleaded to hear the sound of Rio's voice, her laugh. She hated herself for still wanting them to reconcile. She hated herself even more for knowing exactly where Rio was, hated knowing that even in her stubbornness, Rio was hurting, yet still chose silence. She hated knowing her so intimately that it hurt to know Rio was in pain, and she wanted, more than anything, to stop the suffering, both her own and Rio's.

It was when she reached the large stable doors that she felt her shins burning. She had been stomping the entire way without realizing it, marching in a volatile mix of rage, longing, frustration, and so many other feelings that blended into a nameless thing. Everything was exactly as it had always been. The wooden structure rose high, its walls weathered and stained by time. Everything was dark save for the faint yellow light visible through the round window near the ceiling. Rio was there, exactly where Agatha knew she would be, which made Agatha let out a frustrated huff that dissolved into a long sigh.

Carefully, she pushed the large doors open with both hands, wincing at the loud creak that announced her presence. But if Rio heard it, she gave no sign — the stable remained utterly silent except for the soft snorts and deep breathing of the sleeping horses. Following the hay-strewn path, Agatha felt a pang of nostalgia, remembering the countless afternoons and nights she had spent there with Rio. When she reached the stairs leading up to the loft, she sighed again. Nothing had changed, only them.

Rio was lying on a mound of hay, her body nearly submerged in the straw, lost in thought as she stared up at the large skylight. Agatha sighed one more time — it was a precise journey back in time.

"I didn't know if you were going to come," Rio broke the silence so abruptly that Agatha nearly jumped. Her heart roared in her chest, not from the fright, but because of Rio, because of seeing her there like that, and the deep, almost melancholic tone of her voice.

Despite speaking, Rio didn't look up; she kept staring at the sky.

"Did you want me to come?" Agatha asked, crossing her arms, feeling small and swallowed by the space that had been theirs for so long.

Rio finally turned her face toward her, and Agatha felt the air violently rush from her lungs as she saw tears streaming down Rio's face, her brown eyes overflowing with a sad tenderness that reached out and hooked her heart. But Agatha didn't take a single step closer; she couldn't. If she did, she would rush to Rio and bury herself in her arms.

"I never wanted you to leave," was all Rio said. Agatha closed her eyes, her chest now consumed by sadness mixed with a certain bitterness that soured her mouth.

"Why did you do this?" Agatha demanded, the tone far more accusatory than she intended. Rio sat up, frowning at her. "You knew I was going. You always knew; we planned this our entire lives. You knew." She practically growled under Rio’s intense gaze. "Why did you give up on us? Why did you give up on me?"

"You think I gave up on you?" Rio countered with a bitter, humorless laugh, shaking her head as she stood up to face her. "I'm right here, Agatha, in the same place as always. I didn't leave; you did."

"To follow my dreams!" Agatha yelled, and Rio nodded without hesitation.

"Your dreams," she emphasized, and Agatha frowned. "What about me, Agatha? What about my dreams?" Rio stared at her with furrowed brows, her tone not accusatory but genuinely questioning, making Agatha's breathing quicken.

"How many times did we talk about this, Riandra? You knew I was going to college, and then—"

"And then what, Agatha?" Rio interrupted, her gentle tone contrasting sharply with Agatha’s exasperation. "You were going to come back to Darby? You were going to live here? On the ranch?" Agatha opened her mouth to protest, but Rio cut her off again.

"You know that's not true. You always knew."

The painful hammering of Agatha's heart made any denial impossible. "You said you were coming to college with me, you—" Agatha started to shout, but Rio cut her off once more.

"You said I was going to college, I never said that. When you asked me what I wanted, I always said my home was here, that my heart is here. You wanted this—college, California—you always wanted this. But me? Agatha, for God’s sake, I want you to look me in the eye and tell me if one day, any day, just once, I said I wanted this."

Agatha hadn't noticed Rio closing the distance; they were now face-to-face, mere inches apart. Looking into those desperate brown eyes, all words vanished in her throat. It was true.

They had always been fundamentally different. Everyone used to joke that oil and water had finally mixed. When they were younger, Rio joked that they were flowers from different trees, and Agatha would foolishly laugh, saying they made a beautiful bouquet. They had always been polar opposites, but their entire lives that had never posed a problem because they always complemented each other; they had never clashed. This was the first time.

She knew Rio loved the ranch—it was more than simple love, in fact. Even after months in California, meeting people from every corner of the world, she had never encountered anyone like Rio. People usually had dreams and passions, but Riandra was different; she breathed the ranch. It wasn't just affection; it was integral to her being. Rio blended seamlessly into the brush, naturally camouflaged. She knew the animals by their eyes, swam in every lake, and that defined her completely—she was a force of nature tied to this land. Agatha wasn't like that; she never had been. She tried—Rio always claimed she did everything to see Agatha smile—but it was Agatha who had spent years immersing herself in the brush, galloping on horseback, spending afternoons by waterfalls, and cleaning stables, bathing cows. She thought Rio would understand, that she would try, too.

Agatha had always believed they would find a compromise, yet she could never envision a plausible one. There was no horizon where their futures converged; they were opposites, just like their dreams.

"What do you want me to say?" Rio asked, exasperated by the silence, and Agatha looked back, her blue eyes brimming with tears.

"I am sorry. I truly am, but what else could I do? You left, Agatha. And you are happy."

"I am not happy!" she yelled, but Rio lowered her head.

"You are; you're just hurt," Rio countered, her eyebrows knit in an expression overflowing with love. Agatha wondered how love, something so beautiful, could inflict such pain. "I wish you could see yourself: the way you smile talking about life in California, how passionate you are about college, the way your eyes sparkle when you describe your trips. This is everything you ever wanted, and you know you're happy, but you're hurt." Rio's voice was now choked, the words almost physically trapped, and Agatha felt tears stream freely down her face. "You're hurt. I'm hurt too. This hurts like hell because I love you. I love you, Agatha! I have never loved anyone but you, not like this. I love you in a way I can't even comprehend; it's the biggest thing inside me, I swear! But what choice do I have but to let you go? I want to see you happy; I want to see those eyes shining like they did at dinner. I want you passionate about your life. And how am I supposed to achieve that by trying to keep you here? By trying to trap you with me?"

Agatha was speechless; everything she had intended to say was now a painful knot lodged in her throat. She wanted to scream, to demand why Rio hadn't answered her letters, to fling accusations that she had ruined everything, broken her heart, and abandoned the best thing that ever happened to either of them. She wanted to push her, to scream so loudly that Rio would feel like an idiot for letting her leave, for giving up everything they were. But she couldn't. As tears silently tracked down her face, she felt the resentment that had built up melt away, because, tragically, Rio was right.

If it weren't for their relationship, for what they had, Agatha would be living her best life. She truly was happy in California; that was the life she had always envisioned. She always wanted to study, go to college, pursue an academic career while establishing herself professionally. She wanted to debate in large courtrooms, see justice served, and change lives. She wanted to travel, see the world, live in big cities. She loved the constant motion, the beach, the noise of cars and people rushing around. She loved experiencing new things, meeting unique people, and hearing their stories. She wanted to collect moments and live something different every day, and life in California was precisely that. She was happy. But her heart was broken.

Her heart was broken because she couldn't resist the dream of freedom, yet her home had roots. Rio was far more than her first love; she was her home, her safe harbor, her person. Though not religious, she sometimes prayed and gave thanks, certain that god had made Rio just for her — she was hers, out of all the people in the world, she had one person who was entirely hers, made perfectly for her. It hurt because despite wanting her freedom, she wanted to live that freedom with Rio. She wanted to live all those dreams with her; she wanted to be happy with Rio. And it hurt even more to know that she could be happy without her. Because now that she had everything she dreamed of, she knew that no matter how much she ached and protested, she wouldn't surrender it for Riandra.

She had made a choice, and only now did she clearly see it. She couldn't have everything; she had to choose one over the other, and she had done so without hesitation. The worst part was knowing she would choose it again if given the chance. She loved Rio, but she loved life even more — she loved the idea of everything that lay ahead. And Rio had made her choice, too. She could yield and learn to be free, but she wouldn't give up who she was for Agatha. They had both chosen this path.

"How can I be happy without you?" Agatha whispered, the question meant more for herself than for Rio, but Rio simply shrugged.

"You love me, Agatha, but you love so many things much more than me," Rio said, tilting her head and looking at her in that endearing way that only made Agatha cry harder. Then, when Rio gently held her face, wiping away her tears with her thumbs, Agatha sobbed uncontrollably. "How would you feel if I went with you, knowing all I wanted was to come home? How do you think I would feel making you stay, knowing all you wanted was to leave? I don't blame you for leaving. I let you go because what else was there for me to do? I want you to be happy." Rio released her face with a sigh, and Agatha looked down, breathing deeply.

"Are you happy here?" she asked when she finally met Rio's eyes.

"This is my home, Agatha." Rio shrugged, and Agatha knit her brows. "I'm hurting right now, but it will pass eventually. It will pass for you too."
