With her head still nestled against Agatha’s shoulder, Rio frowned in thought. “Me being here, out of nowhere, making breakfast for you all as if nothing happened...”

"He'll love it, I'm sure," Rio said, and Agatha smiled. "What did you tell your mom?"

"I didn't tell her anything, I just came," Agatha shrugged. "It's not like we'll be able to hide this for long."

"She's going to kill me when you leave."

At that, Agatha put the bowl down, turned to face Rio, and wrapped her arms around Rio's shoulders while Rio held her by the waist.

"Can we not talk about that?" she pleaded, her eyebrows knitted together. "I don't want to talk about leaving." Rio simply nodded and pressed her lips against Agatha's.

Instantly, Lilia, holding Benito firmly by the shoulders, pulled him back to give the girls privacy, covering his mouth so he wouldn't protest or draw attention, and quickly dragged him toward the living room.

"Are they back together?" Benito whispered with a huge grin when she released him, and Lilia just shrugged, nearly exasperated, as confused as he was.

"I don't know, neno," she replied, trying to hold back a laugh.

"Of course they are!"

"You don't say a word, understood?" she warned, one hand on her hip. He looked at her in exasperation, indignant. "Leave them be!"

***

The breakfast that morning was a dramatic contrast to the welcoming dinner three days earlier. Javier chose to play dumb, joining the conversation and letting himself be swept up by the familiar atmosphere, all while observing the scene with a spark of joy that swelled in his chest. It had been a long time since he had seen his daughter smiling like that — so light and genuinely content. The entire house felt joyful; it was infectious to have that feeling back, his two girls so comfortable with each other, just as they had always been.

From his end of the table, he watched Agatha laugh and roll her eyes while cutting an enormous slice of cake for Rio, who grumbled that she didn't just need the slice — she intended to eat the whole thing. Benito was busy arguing with her, demanding a piece for himself. Javier exchanged a questioning look with Lilia, who simply shrugged; no one had any idea what was truly happening, but it was clear the house had woken up full of light that morning.

After breakfast, once Benito had bolted out to the ranch, Javier watched the two girls through the window while Lilia washed the dishes. They were talking on the porch, sharing a bottle of grape juice, leaning against the fence side-by-side, lost in a conversation that belonged only to them. They were inside that familiar bubble he had known for many years. He watched how Agatha leaned against Rio, her body resting on Rio's shoulder, and how his daughter occasionally stroked Agatha's back or arm. It was like stepping straight back in time, exactly twelve months.

"What in the world is going on right under my nose, Lilia?" he asked, intrigued, peering through a gap in the curtain.

"I have no idea," she replied, laughing heartily. "When I woke up, the two of them were all lovey dovey in the kitchen."

"I can't decide if I should be happy or worried," he murmured, watching his daughter laugh so hard she threw her head back while Agatha spoke excitedly, gesturing as if trying to explain something. "These two... Ojalá que Santo Antonio resuelva este lío”

***

Rio proposed the idea, and as soon as she told Agatha, Agatha instantly accepted it, heading straight to Wanda's house. Wanda nearly yelled at her, calling it the most ridiculous, half-baked plan she could have conceived, much less agreed to. Agatha, however, was completely unfazed, spending hours explaining herself, grinning from ear to ear and looking like a teenager again. She was happy. She knew it was a total mess and that she was probably making things worse, but she couldn't stop. She couldn't say no; she couldn't pull away. She desperately wanted to spend every available second by Rio's side because she knew their time together was limited.

Agatha claimed she was simply making the most of the time she had, wanting to enjoy Rio and feel that connection one last time before facing reality.

To Wanda, this reasoning made no sense. It wasn't that Wanda disliked Rio — before the breakup, she was one of the few friends who genuinely liked her and made an effort to include her, despite Rio being somewhat disconnected from their social group. Wanda knew they loved each other and had always supported them, but after everything, she found it absurd that Agatha kept getting involved. Rio deserved silence; she deserved to suffer the way she had made Agatha suffer. Furthermore, Agatha had a trip planned in a few days with someone else, someone she liked and was getting to know. How could she possibly be playing house with Rio, knowing someone was waiting for her miles away?

To Wanda, they were only making a difficult situation exponentially worse. It was obvious they were passionately in love, but why prolong that if Agatha was leaving and Rio was staying? Wanda knew her friend wouldn't abandon her life plans, just as Rio was too proud to ever leave her family or the ranch. Both knew perfectly well they had no future together, and pretending for two weeks that none of it mattered would only increase their suffering. Wanda didn't want that for either of them.

In Wanda's view, the only sensible choice was to accept that they wouldn't work out, that they wanted different things. Despite their beautiful connection, neither was willing to sacrifice their own deepest desires for the other — they were simply heading in opposite directions. What they were doing was reckless; they were deluding themselves when everyone knew how the story would end; they had seen this film before.

Despite her strong protests, Wanda found herself being pulled toward Natasha's house that Friday evening. She carried an apple pie, while Agatha, buzzing with excitement beside her, clutched a large bag filled with cookies, snacks, and finger foods. It was a double date.

Natasha's relationship with her immediate family — her mother and stepfather — was strained, bordering on hostile. She had been primarily raised by her grandmother and couldn't recall her last visit to her parents' home. However, her grandmother would periodically travel to Boston to visit her other granddaughter, Yelena — a child from the current marriage, the one her family actually doted on, and someone Natasha didn't even know. Luckily, her grandmother was leaving for a full two weeks, giving Natasha the entire house to herself, which was ideal for the planned gathering.

Rio opened the door with a huge smile, immediately enveloping Agatha in a tight bear hug and planting a quick kiss on her lips. She then turned to Wanda, who offered a polite smile and accepted a brief hug in greeting.

"Dinner is almost ready, I swear!" Natasha's voice boomed from the kitchen.

"You made dinner? But we brought pie," Wanda said, already walking toward the kitchen; she was more than used to being in that house.

As Wanda and Natasha's conversation drifted away, Agatha and Rio exchanged a significant look, grinning foolishly at each other. Rio slipped her arms around Agatha's waist, and she melted into her embrace, allowing Rio to pull her into a deep kiss. They had only been apart for less than twelve hours, yet Agatha already missed her.

"How was your day, cariño?" Rio asked, gently stroking her face.

"I didn't do much. I spent the morning reading, helped my mom make lunch, and then went over to Wanda's house," she recounted, quickly pecking Rio's lips. "And yours?"

"I spent mine counting the minutes until I could see you again," Rio replied with her most charming smile.

Agatha let out a soft laugh and rolled her eyes. "Dork."

"You make me this way."

They were leaning in for another kiss when Wanda's voice cut through the moment:

"Wine?" she asked, holding up a bottle, pretending she hadn't just interrupted anything.

The rest of the night unfolded as smoothly as the wine they drank — the tension easing with every sip amidst the continuous flow of conversation and laughter that filled the house. They finished an entire bottle while Natasha finished dinner, surprising everyone with her delicious bacon and broccoli risotto. Their discussion spanned everything from school memories to gossiping about old classmates.

They barely noticed time passing, completely absorbed in their bubble, talking and laughing. Rio felt a comforting warmth in her chest from the familiarity of it all. It was so easy, so delightful — it felt right, as if they had done this a million times before. Rio wished intensely that this was their life — seeing Agatha every day, enjoying every moment together with their friends. She wanted to freeze this moment and live here forever, unable to bear the thought that this feeling of completeness would soon end.

After clearing the dinner table, they decided on a competitive round of Pictionary, couple against couple, and the battle lasted for hours. Whenever Natasha made a disastrous attempt at drawing, prompting Wanda to groan in frustration, Agatha would burst into laughter, sprawled across the sofa. Her body rested against Rio, whose arms were wrapped securely around her. Slightly tipsy, they laughed at everything, taking the competition far more seriously than necessary.

When Agatha correctly guessed Rio's word on the very first try, securing yet another win, the couple erupted in cheers. Agatha threw herself into Rio's embrace as Wanda and Natasha grumbled, immediately demanding a rematch. Rio and Agatha barely heard the protests, too busy celebrating their victory as Rio twirled her around the room, both of them euphoric as if they had just won a historic prize.

With Rio's arms wrapped tightly around her, Agatha felt a powerful surge of euphoria, a feeling of completeness she hadn't experienced in years. It was as if all the blank spaces that usually troubled her thoughts about the present and future had suddenly been filled. More than anything, she wished she could spend a lifetime like this, safe in Rio's arms. She longed for a way to make their relationship work, even though she knew this hope was just her heart's desperate attempt to bury the crushing weight of reality, which drew nearer with the close of every day.

***

Evanora was sitting on the porch, crocheting alongside Lilia. They enjoyed the cool afternoons that way, chatting away while making rugs from yarn. They were talking about Benito, how he was turning into a young man, and Lilia mentioned he even had a girlfriend, the baker's daughter from the small street fair below the square.

"Her name is Viviane, isn't it?" Evanora asked, finishing a stitch without looking up from her work. "She's adorable, a sweet girl. But isn't she too young for—"

Her sentence was abruptly cut short as Agatha dashed past them like an arrow. She didn't bother to close the door or offer a greeting. Evanora jumped, startled, clutching a hand to her chest at the sight of her daughter racing off like a wild tomboy. Her gaze followed Agatha down the dirt road, where she spotted Rio mounted on her horse, prompting a heavy sigh.

"Agatha!" she called out loudly. Her daughter stumbled to a stop, turning back with an exasperated, clearly annoyed expression. "May I ask where you are going?"

"I'm going out," Agatha yelled back, already turning to run again. Evanora rolled her eyes. "I'll be back before dinner, I promise!"

From her horse, Rio waved a greeting, a wide smile lighting up her face. Evanora watched Rio effortlessly help her daughter mount the horse. Before Evanora could utter a warning or a scolding, Agatha was perched behind Rio, and they shot off instantly.

"I knew this was going to happen," Evanora lamented, shaking her head as they disappeared from sight, but Lilia tsked in disagreement.

"They care about each other, Eva," she interceded for the two of them, but Evanora merely let out a puff of disapproval. "Both of them were suffering apart, and now they're so happy. I missed this, seeing them like this, like two little girls again.

"We've seen this movie before, Lilia. Soon Agatha will leave, and then what?" Lilia looked back at her, a serious expression on her face. "Rio spent months going from bad to worse; she transformed into someone completely different. I still don't know how my daughter forgave that. And now they're back in this bed of roses as if nothing happened. This won't end well."

"It was difficult for both of them," Lilia countered. "Even though Agatha spent her whole life waiting for this, the reality of it is something else. Neither of them was prepared for the shock of the distance. But look how much they love each other. I'm sure they'll find a way."

"I don't know what way that is," Evanora said, shaking her head. "Rio won't budge from here even for a miracle, and Agatha, if she could, would already be on the other side of the world. This has no future." She continued, "I supported them when they were girls, but now they are women, and their desires are completely mismatched. Each is pulling the rope from a different end; they don't want to move in the same direction. Love isn't the only thing that matters in life; you need to compromise with the other person, and neither of them can do that right now."

"It's just a phase," Lilia insisted. "Agatha just started college; she's discovering herself, living. Soon, she'll tire of this restless life. She talks constantly about wanting to live everywhere and how she can't stand this place, but look how happy she is when she's here. She'll end up coming back."

"To become a housewife? With a diploma in hand?" Evanora scoffed in disbelief. "I highly doubt it; I know my own daughter. Agatha is a free spirit with too many dreams. She would never give up that life for Rio, and honestly, I think that's right. She's far too smart to settle for a quiet life; she has a brilliant future ahead."

"Rio does too," Lilia said, and Evanora let out a dry laugh.

"Running around and drinking in every corner? Please, Lilia."

"She's making good money with the racing. She's more involved with the ranch. In the last few months, she's even started engaging more with the family business. She may not be book smart, but she knows everything here like the back of her hand. Javier himself said she has what it takes to run the ranch, that he trusts the business will continue to prosper in her hands."

"I don't know, Lilia, that girl is too unstable," Evanora said thoughtfully. "Despite everything, I love her, and I truly hope she gets her life together, but I just can't see it happening, and I know my daughter won't abandon her own path for her."

"That's for them to figure out, Eva," Lilia said gently, and Evanora offered a reluctant nod. "I believe they can find a middle ground. Their feelings run deep; this isn't just a fleeting girlhood crush. This isn't temporary."

"If Rio would just get her act together, maybe," Evanora conceded.

"I have faith in them," Lilia said with determined optimism.

Evanora let out a small, unconvinced puff of air. "I just don't want to see my daughter hurting anymore. I hope they work things out one way or another. They need to realize they aren't two girls anymore; life has to move forward."

***

Agatha was smiling, her hair flying in the wind as she held tightly to Rio's waist. Rio was galloping, slapping the reins to make Gaia accelerate further down the road. Their bodies shook together, and Agatha closed her eyes, savoring the feeling: the breeze on her face, the warmth of Rio's back against her body, the rocking gallop, and the scent of the brush. She had missed this so much — she felt limitless.

Seven days had already flown by, and slowly, a bitter taste was starting to form in her throat, a reminder that she would soon have to confront the reality of her choices. The week had been perfect. She had spent most of her time either riding Rio's horse, accompanying her around the ranch, relaxing on her bed, or sitting with her on the porch. She was so happy that every sunset brought with it a surge of apprehension in her chest, feeling like she was watching an hourglass about to bury her in sand. In seven more days, the protected bubble they had created would finally burst.

Deep down, Agatha knew they were both avoiding the inevitable, circling the one fact neither of them had the courage to voice: What would become of them once these two weeks were over?

In truth, Rio had tried to bring up the subject, but each time, Agatha either diverted the conversation or offered a vague reply, lacking the courage to state what was already a certainty. She avoided the discussion because she knew she would have to say precisely what Rio didn't want to hear. Her priority was to savor these final days, collecting sweet memories for a happy conclusion. She simply couldn't bear to break Rio's heart right now, knowing it would shatter her own as well. She knew the relationship wouldn't work; Rio wouldn't uproot her life for California, nor would she abandon the ranch, just as Agatha herself would never surrender her dreams. Everything Rio had said in the stable was true, and no matter how much Agatha wished to make it work, she knew forcing it would only lead to greater pain for both of them. She resolved that they should cherish the time they had and remember this period fondly.

Her thoughts were interrupted as the horse slowed from a gallop to a trot. They had reached the crest of the ridge, and from that height, she could see the vast vineyard stretching for miles across the land. It was breathtaking. From this vantage point, she could appreciate the entire ranch, seeing how extensively Rio's world spread out. As much as she resented Rio's decision to stay, Agatha recognized that this place truly was her world — it was an integral part of her identity.

Rio dismounted first and secured Gaia to a stump, pausing to stroke the horse's muzzle before offering both hands to help Agatha down. Hand-in-hand, they walked down the slope toward the vineyard. Although Agatha was familiar with the path, she rarely took it. Plants weren't her expertise; she wasn't much help with the work and didn't enjoy navigating the dense vines. Besides, she knew this was a place Rio often visited with her father, spending hours there together. Still, she liked being here now, enjoying the deep shadows and the sweet, intoxicating scent that drifted from the vines.

As they walked along the trail that bordered the vines, Rio exchanged greetings with some of the workers. Agatha recognized a few from previous years, and they smiled warmly, commenting that it was good to see her back. Rio's smile, as she held Agatha's hand, grew even wider, offering a moment of comfort even as a familiar pang tightened Agatha's chest. Rio began talking about her father's plans to expand the crop, detailing his big visions for the business. They now employed more than twice the number of men; Javier wanted to start exporting internationally, and they were collaborating on new wine catalogs. Agatha smiled with pride, witnessing Rio's genuine enthusiasm and involvement. Rio had a clear future here, and Agatha was happy for her, knowing that she would find fulfillment on her own terms. Rio had always dreamed of running that ranch with her own hands, and it was lovely to hear her speak with such pride.

At the end of the trail stood a large stone building. This was the production house, where the wine was actually made and all the barrels were stored for fermentation before bottling and maturation. It was a massive, three-story stone structure, a mix of gray and green where ivy climbed every surface. Rio led her up the exterior stairs to the third floor, and Agatha's smile widened as she saw a tablecloth spread out, ready with a complete picnic just for them.

"When did you have time to do this?" she asked, cupping Rio's face and pressing a quick, affectionate kiss onto her lips.

"I came this morning," Rio shrugged, pulling her forward. They both settled side-by-side against the stone railing. "You haven't been here in a while; I thought you'd enjoy it." Agatha nodded approvingly and immediately opened the basket, knowing it was filled with Lilia's delicious treats. Meanwhile, Rio picked up a wine bottle and turned the label toward Agatha. "And this one just matured. It's one of the new ones, short maturation — it took two months, and I made it with my father."

"You made it?" Agatha asked, her smile impressed, looking at Rio with enchantment. This was a new side of Rio, and she realized that despite critics saying she never grew up, she was maturing at her own pace. She suppressed a heavy sigh.

"With my father," Rio emphasized, unwilling to take all the credit, but Agatha shook her head as Rio filled their glasses.

"I'm drinking the first wine made by Rio Vidal? That's an honor!" She accepted the glass and clinked it against Rio's. "What is it called?"

As Agatha swirled her glass, examining the wine's body, Rio offered a shy, awkward smile. Agatha looked at her inquiringly, raising an eyebrow.

"Tell me, what is it?"

"Calcedo."

"Is that Spanish? What does it mean?" she asked while observing the robust texture of the white wine. Its color was a pale, clear yellow that seemed to shimmer, and the scent was fresh, carrying notes of citrus and flowers.

"It's not Spanish; it's inspired by chalcedony, the mineral," Rio explained, her eyes fixed shyly on the glass she swirled between her fingers. Agatha furrowed her brow, noting Rio's sudden bashfulness. "Agates, or agatas as I prefer to call it, vary from chalcedony."

Agatha's eyes instantly met hers. She grinned foolishly, feeling her heart thump in her chest while Rio pressed her lips together, looking awkward and sweet. In the same moment, Agatha leaned in, tenderly caressing Rio's face before joining their lips. Rio smiled into the kiss as Agatha tried to deepen it, but soon they were just smiling against each other's mouths.

"Before you say you like it, you have to try it," Rio murmured, trying to pull away from the stream of kisses while slightly tilting her glass. Agatha continued to kiss her, smiling, savoring the warmth flooding her chest.

Agatha felt loved, whole — she felt as though the entire world had settled perfectly inside her heart.

"It's beautiful, my love," she said, her eyebrows softening. Rio shrugged. "It's the most beautiful thing anyone has ever done for me."

"Try it," Rio urged, tilting the glass toward her. Rio took her first sip just as Agatha took hers.

Agatha melted into the flavors. The wine was smooth and vibrant on the tongue, effervescent, with a clean freshness that finished with a velvety coating on her palate. It had a soft, mild salinity, creating an almost synesthetic experience—a mix of grapes and white fruits that seemed to peel back layers with every sip. Having grown up tasting every wine her family produced, Agatha had never encountered anything so unique.

All she could do was smile widely, the sound of Rio’s laugh like music to her ears as she filled another glass, sighing in satisfaction. Rio smiled proudly, then launched into an explanation of the entire production process and the inspiration behind the bottle. She had blended pears and green apples, fresh herbs, jasmine, and honeysuckle. Agatha watched her, fascinated, realizing that for Rio, this was truly an art form, far more than just a business. Agatha listened, smiling, absorbed in Rio's monologues—which were far more intricate than she would have ever imagined—as Rio explained each flavor nuance through the complex formations of agates (or agatas, as she called them in Spanish).

Agatha knew Rio had turned a corner months after her departure; Wanda had written to her specifically, detailing how Rio spent more time at home and had become involved with the ranch after the hippodrome was built. But Agatha hadn't expected to see her flourishing like this. She finally understood what Rio meant when she talked about finding her path. Here, Rio was fully herself; she had direction, passion, and was accomplishing extraordinary things. With every story Rio shared—about their current projects, and more ideas she was developing with her father—Agatha recognized that, contrary to popular belief, Rio had an incredible future right here. Her heart was poured into everything she did. For a moment, Agatha felt like crying, overwhelmed by a mix of pride and sadness, because this was definitive proof that this was Rio's place—not necessarily by Agatha's side, but where she could find herself and do what she loved.

Rio then talked about flowers, explaining that beyond the vineyard, they were planting different species to build a portfolio with floral notes; she intended to expand their entire wine portfolio and create her own line. As Rio spoke of her honeysuckles and chrysanthemums, Agatha realized that Rio was very much like a flower—beautiful, yes, but she needed her roots firmly planted in the earth, or she would quickly wither.

They spent long hours discussing the vineyard, Rio's ideas, and her projects, just as Agatha spoke passionately about her semester—the subjects she enjoyed most, explaining basic legal concepts, talking about the books she read, the debates she participated in, and the area of law she most identified with. Rio listened with deep attention, asking pointed questions about complex topics, eager to know where Agatha envisioned herself and what she hoped to gain from the coming years of study. They spoke as if their individual goals were not diametrically opposed, simply discussing the things they truly loved and what motivated them.

"And that internship you mentioned?" Rio asked, resting her head in Agatha's lap while Agatha stroked her hair and took another sip of the wine. "Have you started it yet?"

"Not yet," Agatha explained, finishing her sip and setting the glass aside. "But I'm incredibly excited. I'll start right at the beginning of the next semester. It's in contractual law. I don't know much yet, but based on the concepts I've learned, I find it really interesting, and it's at one of the biggest firms in all of California. They advocate for clients all over the world; it’s truly an unbelievable opportunity."

"They advocate for the whole world?" Rio repeated, impressed, and Agatha nodded with a smile. "And you got the spot? I always said you would be the biggest lawyer in all of California. You hooked a big fish in just two semesters."

Agatha shook her head, rolling her eyes. "It’s not much credit to me, actually. It was Tes—" She stopped instantly, feeling the sudden tension in Rio's body, who was now staring at her intensely. "I'm sorry, I—"

"It was Tessa," Rio finished, her expression flat. "You can say her name, Agatha."

"I don't want this to—"

"It's okay, cariño," Rio interrupted softly, yet her expression remained unreadable. "It's your life, and if you're happy... I'm glad you're finding your path. Like you said, it's going to be a great opportunity for you, and I want to know about it. You can tell me."

Agatha felt her heart sink under that intense brown gaze that seemed to penetrate her soul. A mixture of feelings rushed through her—a warm numbness, a cold knot in her stomach. It hurt, and she knew that even if Rio wouldn't admit it, it hurt her too.

"We don't have to talk about this."

"But I want to know. I want you to tell me. Please."

Agatha took a deep breath, feeling her chest tighten. "Her father is a very famous jurist; her whole family works in law and is highly renowned. Her uncle owns this firm, and when a position opened up, she recommended me."

"She knows you're good," Rio said, letting out a heavy sigh, causing Agatha to knit her eyebrows in concern. "What is she like?"

"Rio..." Agatha groaned, shaking her head.

"What is she like, Agatha?" It wasn't a demand; it was almost a plea, in that sweet, gentle tone that broke Agatha's heart. "I want to know what she's like. If you like her, I'm sure that—"

"Rio, please," she murmured softly. Rio slid off her lap, moving across the floor to sit directly in front of her. She cupped Agatha's face, her eyebrows knitted together in worry. "I don't want to talk about this. I don't want to talk about her."

"Do you like her?" Rio asked, caressing her cheeks.

"What does that matter, Rio?" Agatha lamented, placing her hands over Rio's wrists. "I'm here right now, with you. What does any of that matter if I love you?"

With a heavy sigh, Rio gave in, pressing her lips to Agatha's.

***

"Hello!" Rio yelled, walking right in. She knew Evanora was in the greenhouse and Richard was roaming the ranch; only Agatha was home, and as usual, running late.

Her race was scheduled to start in half an hour. Normally, she would already be at the hippodrome, checking her horse, studying the competitors, and listening to Bucky's directives, as he always knew the best strategy for the highest betting success. Beyond her own victory, she needed to account for her opponents' performance based on the day's betting odds—if she couldn't win, it was crucial to study others' strengths and weaknesses to steer the race favorably.

While waiting for Agatha to get ready — she couldn't understand the need for so much preparation since Agatha would look gorgeous no matter what — Rio wandered through the house, completely at home there. She opened the refrigerator, grabbed one of Richard's beers, nodded in approval at the brand, and opened the bottle on her belt buckle. Taking her first long swig, she continued walking, slowly pacing, until a stack of photos on the dining table caught her eye.

Holding the brick of pictures, Rio smiled at a photo of Agatha proudly biting a medal with her volleyball team, then flipped through shots of Agatha smiling broadly in front of towering city buildings, and another at a beach with a surfboard. She was smiling and flipping until she froze, her fingers trembling as she frowned at a particular photograph.

It was Agatha, smiling so widely her eyes were closed, her face pressed close to a girl her age — a girl with big blue eyes and a picture-perfect smile. She was fair-skinned like Agatha, with light brown, slightly blonde hair. She was beaming, a sparkle in her eyes that Rio recognized all too well. It was the same goofy, melting look she knew she had when she was with Agatha. They looked profoundly happy together, and Rio felt her heart plummet.

Throughout the week, she had successfully buried this deep insecurity, choosing instead to focus on the joy and feelings they shared. But she knew that, deep down, this was just a temporary reprieve. Eventually, she would have to start gathering the broken shards that had cut her for months — the gaping wound of knowing that no matter how much she loved Agatha, she would never have her completely, not in the way she wanted. What hurt most was seeing how happy Agatha was, how carefree and light she looked living her life. Agatha already had a full life outside of here, away from Rio. What was she thinking? That they would somehow find a way? In just a few days, Agatha would be in New York with someone else — someone she liked. Someone who would, eventually, become to her what Rio had been for a lifetime.

The knot in her throat felt physically painful, and her vision blurred with tears, but she squeezed her eyes shut to hold them back just as she heard hurried footsteps on the stairs:

"Sorry! I swear I tried not to be late!" Agatha shouted, her face alight with excitement, but she stopped abruptly when she saw Rio standing in the kitchen, the photo clutched in her hands. Agatha's eyes widened, looking utterly caught. "Rio..."

"Is this her?" was all Rio managed to whisper. Agatha sighed, stepping closer and taking Rio's hands in hers, causing the photo to flutter onto the table. "Is this her, Agatha?"

"Yes," Agatha replied, lowering her gaze.

Rio simply nodded. "She's pretty."

"Rio..." Agatha started, reaching out to cup her face, but Rio took a step back, shaking her head.

"Let's go. I can't be late."

***

Rio was running blind; she saw nothing — not the track, not the competing horses, nor the cheering stands. She saw only red, consumed by a scorching heat, a blind rage that overwhelmed her senses; it was as if she were racing outside of herself. The only tangible sensations were the wind against her face and the anchored rhythm of the pounding earth and the horse's gallop. She ran, whipping the reins harder and harder, screaming at the horse, throwing her body into the curves, running as if there were no finish line, as if the laps would never end. She ran until her heart hammered in her throat, until she felt absolutely nothing but the rush of adrenaline coursing through her veins.

As she completed the final lap, she let out a raw, gut-wrenching scream, hearing the enthusiastic applause from the stands below cheering her on. She kept screaming and ran for another entire lap, and the euphoria of the crowd intensified—they assumed she was celebrating her victory. She wanted to laugh at the bitter irony: it looked to everyone like she was winning everything—the trophy, the girl—but in reality, she was left with absolutely nothing; it was a hollow triumph. The one thing she truly wanted, she couldn't possess completely, not genuinely.

Stepping onto the podium to hoist the trophy above her head, she saw Agatha standing next to her brother. Both were jumping and screaming, wide smiles plastered across their faces. All Rio wanted to do was cry.

***

Agatha sat at her desk, attempting to get a jumpstart on her reading for the next semester, but the harder she tried to concentrate, the more chaotic her thoughts became. She glanced at the calendar once more—only three days remained before her departure. With a frustrated groan, she tossed the calendar aside and squeezed her eyes shut.

She was overwhelmed by a whirlwind of emotions, unable to pinpoint any one of them; all she knew was that it hurt, and it hurt deeply, though she couldn’t articulate why. Her mind raced with a cacophony of feelings, and she longed to scream until her voice gave out.

For months, Agatha had been postponing her return home, harboring no desire to go back. If it were up to her, she would have invited her family to Los Angeles, avoiding the suffocating grip of the ranch—a place that felt like the end of the world, surrounded by nothing but dirt. She had been eagerly counting down the days until she reached New York, dreaming of exploring neighboring cities, wandering the state with a backpack and Tessa by her side before classes began. Yet now, the last thing she felt was a desire to leave.

In the beginning, she struggled to feel at home, but soon, she found herself waking up in tranquility, inhaling the fresh scent of the damp brush, nurturing her mother’s plants, sharing laughter with Lilia while preparing lunch, eagerly anticipating her father’s return with his muddy boots, enjoying bonfires with the Vidals, and cherishing her moments with Riandra. Time seemed to stand still in Rio; it felt as though it simply didn’t exist. Agatha couldn’t quite grasp how, but whenever she was with Rio, time transformed into a mere illusion—she felt infinite.

Rio, with her big brown eyes and infectious laughter, her strong accent, her leather hats, thick belts, and hands calloused yet so gentle. Rio, who smelled like fresh earth, whose voice was soft, whose thoughts were delightfully jumbled, and whose country ways led her to appear daily with freshly picked flowers, to put Agatha on her horse, and to ride for hours. Rio, who found meaning in every aspect of nature, who understood the sounds of the animals, who knew every corner of the ranch, who felt most at home barefoot on the dirt ground, and who judged time not by a clock she couldn't read, but by the changing colors of the sky. Rio, who looked at her with an affection so palpable it warmed her heart, whose arms were the perfect length to hold her close, who touched her with devotion, who was impressed by her every word, who thought she was brilliant simply for being herself, and who saw the world with a simplicity Agatha had never encountered.

Rio who loved her family above all else, turned grapes into wine, ran like lightning on a horse, sang with a voice more beautiful than a nightingale, and saw life through the nuances of the enchanting world around her—as if that ranch was all that existed. Rio who made that end-of-the-world place the most incredible spot on planet Earth.

Staring at the books on her desk, Agatha wondered how this was possible, how she had cornered herself into this paradox, desiring two things so fundamentally distinct. She couldn't understand her own heart, unable to distinguish her true desires; everything she wanted seemed to be in a completely different place. She longed to return to college, attend all her classes, spend afternoons at the beach, and go exploring aimlessly on weekends, yet she also craved being on Rio's horse, laughing as Rio stumbled over rocks near the waterfall, shouting for her at her races, and cuddling in the hammock at sunset. She wanted to go to New York and photograph every street corner, chasing Tessa through the crowds, but she also wanted to hear the cicadas singing while sitting around the bonfire, listening to Rio play guitar and sing with Benito. She felt stranded at a crucial fork in the road, knowing she had to choose just one path.

The truth was, she couldn't stay even if she wanted to; she had to go back to California for her classes and would spend entire months until she could return to the ranch. Her heart weighed the options, remembering Rio's silence, her aversion to Agatha's choices, her disdain for the city and everything that made her happy. She didn't know if she could make it work. Rio hadn't even read her letters; Agatha had seen them all, unopened, stacked in a basket in her closet. It was a shot in the dark to think they could make it work—she knew they would eventually argue about the same things, and in the end, neither would yield.

And then there was Tessa, whom Agatha had consciously avoided thinking about during her time back home. It would be hypocritical to deny her feelings for Tessa, because she liked her, very much, more than she had anticipated. They shared similar thoughts, liked the same things, and had common goals. Over the past months, as Agatha tried to fill the emptiness in her chest, Tessa had been there with her sharp smile and her ambitious ideas. Tessa had written during the week, missing her and eager to meet her at the airport, and Agatha hadn't had the heart to reply, not while she was immersed in the sea of Rio and a love she couldn't tame or measure. She liked Tessa, but she loved Rio.

She felt foolish, like a teenager convinced her first love would last forever. Her mother had told her countless times: first love is the most beautiful and the hardest to release, but it is not necessarily the last; it’s simply the first. Yet Agatha couldn't imagine loving like this again, not with this intensity. She felt she would love Rio for the rest of her life, that she would never truly be able to let her go. She didn't want to; she felt she simply couldn't. She yearned for Rio by her side for the rest of her life, traveling the world, exploring and discovering together. She wanted Rio to see the world through her eyes, even while acknowledging the unfairness that she herself didn't see the world through Rio's.

She desperately wanted to think rationally, but her heart was screaming in her chest.

A sudden tapping at her window—then another and another—interrupted her turmoil. Agatha let out a heavy breath, wiping away her tears because she knew exactly who it was. When she pulled back the curtains, she was met by Rio’s face pressed against the glass in a silly grimace as she hung from the almond tree branch. However, the amusement on Rio's face vanished instantly when she saw Agatha's tear-streaked, red eyes.

The moment Agatha opened the window, Rio leaped into the room, her eyebrows knitted with a mixture of confusion and concern. She immediately pulled Agatha into her arms, squeezing her tight. Agatha allowed herself to be completely enveloped, burying her face in the curve of Rio's neck, inhaling her familiar scent of fresh earth. She clung to Rio's back while Rio gently swayed them, rocking her in a tight hug, her head resting against Agatha’s.

"¿Qué pasa, mi cariño?" Rio asked with that gentle voice, soft as honey, and Agatha only sobbed harder against her, breathing deeply of her scent and shaking her head. "Háblame, cariño, puedes contarme lo que sea."

Agatha swallowed hard, taking a ragged breath. She pulled back just enough to look into Rio's eyes, tightening her grip around Rio’s body and pressing her forehead against hers. Her tears continued to trace paths down her face as she let herself drown in the warm brown eyes that watched her with such palpable affection.

"I love you," was all Agatha could say, her voice choked. Rio smiled faintly, nodding.

"Te amo con cada latido de mi corazón, te amo tan grande como este mundo, tan grande como todo lo que puedo ver.” Rio said, pulling back just to hold her face, stroking her cheeks with her thumbs, wiping away her tears. "Te amo tanto que eres lo más grande que hay en mí. Te amo desde aquí hasta California.”

"I love you from here to the end of the world," Agatha replied, and Rio sealed their lips together, pressing their foreheads together again. "I love you the size of the sky, every little bit of it. I love you like the sky, which is always above us, no matter where we are."

"Every time I look at the sky, I think of you," Rio confessed. "I wonder if you're seeing the same sky as me, what your little piece looks like far away—if it's the same shade of blue, if it's lighter or darker. And no matter what it looks like, I know we are under the same sky, and that’s how I fall asleep every night."

Agatha sank into her embrace, and Rio squeezed her tight, closing her eyes fiercely and swallowing hard. She desperately didn't want this to be a farewell. Deep down, she still hoped Agatha would stay, not forever, but at least until January—that she would give up Tessa, give up New York. She yearned for a way forward, her heart pleading for a solution.

"You are here right now, with me, and that's what matters," Rio said, speaking as much to reassure herself as to comfort Agatha.

"You know I'm leaving," Agatha murmured, her face buried in Rio's neck. Rio nodded, hugging her even tighter, as if trying to merge their bodies into one.

"You're not leaving right now. We don't have to think about what comes next," Rio insisted, arching back to look at her. Agatha met her gaze, her eyebrows furrowed. "Besides, how am I supposed to give you a present with you crying like this?"

"What present?" Agatha sniffled, rubbing her face. Rio offered a faint smile.

With a sly grin, Rio reached into the pocket of her cargo pants and presented a closed fist. When Agatha tried to reach for it, Rio pulled her hand away, raising an eyebrow.

"You have to smile first."

Agatha rolled her eyes but managed a faint, watery smile.

When Rio opened her hand, Agatha brought both hands to her mouth in delight, seeing the purple brooch framed in silver, featuring the white decal of three female silhouettes. It was beautiful. Agatha loved brooches and had a particular fondness for stones—perhaps influenced by Rio's frequent talk of them and their meanings—and though she had a collection, she had never seen one like this.

"It's beautiful, my love," she whispered, carefully taking it between her fingers. Rio beamed.

"I found it at an antique store outside town," Rio explained. "The man said they represent three matriarchs, and I immediately thought of you, your mother, and Lilia. I thought it would be a nice reminder." This explanation made Agatha smile even wider. "Open it. It’s a locket."

Agatha carefully opened the locket and tenderly took the small lock of hair between her fingers, looking back at Rio with gentle fondness.

"It's mine," Rio said with a shrug. "That way, you can take me with you too."

With eyes shining with tenderness, Agatha closed the locket and pinned the brooch to her shirt, directly over the left side of her chest. She then threw herself back into Rio's arms, closing her eyes, her heart pounding unevenly, certain that regardless of distance, memory, or any locket, she would always carry Rio with her, deep in her heart.

Rio would forever have a piece of her heart.

***

Rio despised crying. When tears welled up, she felt a profound loss of control over her own body, forced to tangibly expel the overwhelming emotions she kept bottled inside. For her, weeping marked the boundary of despair, the point where she became so completely full that she simply overflowed.

Overflowing was a state she rarely allowed herself to reach. Her typical defense mechanism was withdrawal: whenever feelings caused her discomfort, she would retreat, seeking refuge in solitude. She found this preferable to being engulfed by uncontrollable sensations, grappling with her own confusion, or battling the frustration of emotions that shouted down her logic. When she felt too much, her chest would tighten, a cold numbness would set in, and she'd be gripped by anguish—at those times, running away felt like the easier solution.

She had spent all those days running, maintaining a facade of casual ease while circling a raw wound that had been torn open before it could properly heal. She refused to think, unwilling to face the full weight of the situation or contemplate what it meant for their future. She knew she would eventually overflow, but she planned to deal with that rupture a few days later. Deep down, she recognized the inevitability of the ending, even though a tiny spark of hope still pleaded for them to find a way to make it work.

She had overflowed all night, unable to sleep as she sobbed into her pillow—but not because of that, not because of Agatha.

It was December twenty-fourth, and this was her first Christmas without her mother.

Rio wept while tracing the portrait on her bedside table: her mother, Maria, smiling widely, embracing Rio’s shoulders while Rio hugged Benito, the three of them forming a small, beloved staircase. Her tears spilled over as she sank into memories that, though vivid, remained far out of reach.

Her mother adored Christmas; Christmas Eve and the twenty-fifth were her favorite days of the year. She would wake up before Javier, hide all the gifts, and then start singing, rousing Rio and Benito before beginning her work. Maria would spend the entire day in the kitchen while Rio decorated the tall pine tree planted out back, always the largest one her father could find. Rio would spend the day covering it with ornaments until Agatha woke up and rushed over to their house, and then they would do everything together. They hung banners and garlands, strung up the lights, and arranged flowers while the women laughed in the kitchen, preparing an endless array of sweets that the two girls furtively stole throughout the day. It truly was the most magical time of the year. When Benito was younger, Rio would dance all over the house with him in her arms, hearing her mother shout warnings to be careful while Agatha laughed loudly at their antics.

Now, the dew had already lifted, and Rio was curled up in her hammock on the porch, staring at the purplish pre-dawn sky. Her coffee mug steamed in her hands, and she inhaled the warmth, slowly listening to the ranch wake up. She tried to absorb the serenity, feeling embraced by the damp morning breeze. She hadn't slept a minute, but she slowly felt a revitalization from the rustling of the dry leaves, trying to convince herself that, like the wind, this pain too would pass. She didn't know how to pray, but she hoped that, just this once, God would hear her heart and bring comfort to her and her family that day.

Rio was lost in thought when an unusually loud noise startled her, causing her to shake her head and narrow her eyes. As she focused, her frown dissolved into confusion: she saw a figure approaching with dragging steps, pulling two wheelbarrows at once, a large bag slung over her shoulder. Rio launched herself out of the hammock, gripping the wooden railing, stretching to confirm what she was seeing. Yes, it was Agatha—wearing a green sweater with a reindeer print and a fuzzy red beanie pulled over her head.

"What are you doing?" Rio yelled, watching her struggle to quicken her pace, clearly using all her strength to pull the overflowing wheelbarrows.

"We have to decorate the house," Agatha shouted back, her steps heavy. "Did you think I would forget?"

Suddenly, Rio felt a warm glow spread through her chest. An involuntary smile—her first of the day—lit up her face as she stared at Agatha, her eyebrows knitted in disbelief at the sight.

"Agatha, we aren't doing anything this year," Rio countered, her smile fading slightly. "Everyone is still sleeping."

"Well, you better wake up Benito!" she shouted, panting. "I already woke up Lilia, and she and my mom will be here soon to take over that kitchen. ¡Vámonos!"

Rio laughed, shaking her head, meeting Agatha's indignant expression as she continued pulling the wheelbarrows:

"Riandra, either you help me or you wake up Benito! I'm not kidding!" she yelled.

Rio rolled her eyes, letting out a sharp groan when she was hit by a small rock. "Agatha!" she shouted in reprimand.

Agatha immediately dropped the bag and the wheelbarrows and started running toward her. She was only a few meters away, so as soon as she was about to step onto the porch, Rio set her mug on the railing and dashed through the house, laughing, with Agatha hot on her heels, shouting one threat after another. Rio nearly tripped on the stairs, with Agatha right behind. They burst into Benito's room, laughing, and the boy screamed in surprise in his deep sleep when the two girls jumped onto his bed.

Suddenly, the cloud of uncertainty and grief that had been hanging over the house completely dissipated.

A subdued Javier woke up to the shouting, but he couldn't help but laugh when he saw all three of them wearing matching sweaters—and worse, Agatha had brought one for him, too, handmade by her mother. By the time they came downstairs, Lilia and Evanora were already busy in the kitchen, and Richard was waiting on the porch for his old friend for some last-minute errands, their truck blaring country Christmas songs. The Vidals, who had felt vulnerable and insecure about facing this day, were now flooded with Christmas spirit—they were a complete, big family again.

Rio, Agatha, and Benito dashed around the house, decorating everything in sight in a wonderfully chaotic mix of banners, garlands, colorful ornaments, and reindeer of every size. Rio fetched a wooden ladder to hang streamers over the door frames, and every time she wobbled, with her brother holding the base and Agatha calling out "a little more to the left" or "a little more to the right," they erupted in laughter.

Once they had finished decking out the entire house, they moved to the porch. Richard and Javier had already returned with an enormous pine tree—even larger than the previous year's—and had secured it near the railing. The men were now drinking beer and chatting while Agatha, Rio, and Benito completely decorated the tree, hanging all the ornaments Agatha had brought, just as they did every year.

The tree soon overflowed with baubles, string lights, colored balls, miniature candies, and reindeer. Rio was already dragging the ladder over to perform the final ritual: placing the golden star right at the top point of the pine.

As always, she offered the star to Benito. He loved making the wish; it was their mother's tradition. Maria used to say the Christmas star always granted the wish of whoever placed it, and as childish as it seemed, they always believed her. However, as soon as Rio passed the star to her brother, he gently pushed it back:

"Your turn. You make the wish this year," he said, smiling broadly.

Rio frowned. "Why? You do it every year."

He simply shrugged. "Make the wish, Rio."

"Make the wish, Rio," Agatha echoed excitedly, already positioning herself to hold the ladder steady. Benito urged her on.

Smiling, Rio climbed the ladder, shouting for them to hold tight. When she finally fastened the star to the top of the pine, she closed her eyes fiercely.

She wished that Agatha would stay—so that every day could be as magical as this one.

***

On the twenty-fifth, they ate until they were stuffed, everyone talking and laughing around the table. Bottles of wine were emptied as everyone shared opinions on the presents and praised the food in a shared familiarity—they were simply content to be together, savoring the moment.

The gift exchange was always everyone's favorite part. The living room was piled high with wrapped presents, and Benito was the first to dive in, rummaging through them one by one to hand them out. Javier had bought his son a new red guitar, exactly what he wanted, and the boy was ecstatic, thrilled also by the harmonica he received from Richard. Agatha received book after book—for college, chronicles, and a stack of the romance novels she loved. Javier got a bottle of wine, a handmade sweater, and a "Best Dad in the World" mug. Rio had received a new pair of boots, a leather hat, and, from Agatha, a camera. Quietly, however, she longed for the gift from her father, who was deliberately acting oblivious.

"Come on, Javier," Lilia muttered, taking a sip of her wine. "The girl is in agonies to know what you bought her." Everyone nodded, laughing in agreement.

"Riandra is a bit too grown up for presents now," he murmured with a dismissive sound, crossing his arms. "Don't you think so, Rio?" he asked, turning to her.

Caught off guard, Rio just shrugged. But her father let out a chuckle, pulling a small box from his pocket and tossing it toward her.

"Merry Christmas, mi cielo," he said, smiling as everyone watched her with anticipation, as if they were privy to a secret she didn't know.

When she opened the box, revealing a key, she looked back at her father with wide, questioning eyes. He was smiling broadly.

"It's outside," he said, gesturing with his head for her to turn around.

Agatha had already flung open the living room window, and when Rio spotted the bright red pickup truck in the distance, parked just beyond the house fence, she gasped in disbelief, leaping instantly off the sofa.

"Is it mine?" she practically shouted. Benito was already glued to the window, his face pressed against the glass, looking as stunned as she felt.

"Aren't you going to take it for a spin?" her father asked.

Rio didn't bother to reply; she bolted out the door, with Agatha and Benito sprinting close behind.

Rio walked in stunned circles around the truck, her hands on her head and her mouth wide open, completely unable to process the sight. It was exactly the one she had dreamed of, and she hadn't known she was getting one. The bodywork gleamed, brand new, and it sat high on huge tires that reached past her knees. It had a massive truck bed and a sliding window for the front seats; the entire interior was lined with leather. She laughed in sheer disbelief.

How?" was all she managed to gasp.

Agatha laughed too. "That's why your dad left town yesterday. He told me, but I couldn't say anything; it was a surprise."

"And how did he know which one I wanted?" Rio asked, wide-eyed. Benito already had one foot on a tire, stretching to jump into the truck bed.

"I told him," Agatha shrugged, and Rio shook her head, still not believing it.

"How did you know?"

"I know you, Riandra," she said with a smug smile.

"How did he—how did I not see this huge truck?!" she practically yelled, throwing her arms wide, still laughing in disbelief.

"He left it parked in the square. He drove it here when we were all on the porch, that's why everyone was distracting you, to keep you inside."

"What are we waiting for? Let's go for a ride!" Benito shouted, already settled in the truck bed.

Rio grinned broadly, opening the driver's door and running her hand over the dashboard, the radio, every detail of the vehicle. When she opened the glove compartment, she found several music tapes.

Agatha planted one foot on the tire, hopped into the truck bed, and opened the sliding window to the cab. Rio turned the radio up full blast, making the truck visibly tremble with the heavy country music blaring from the speakers.

"Where are we going?" Rio asked, shouting to be heard.

"Wherever you want!" Agatha yelled back, sitting next to Benito, who was impatiently slapping the truck's body, urging her to step on the gas immediately.

And so Rio did, starting the engine, putting it in gear, and accelerating down the dirt road.

In the truck bed, her hair flying in the wind, singing "God Bless Texas" at the top of her lungs, with Benito beside her pretending to play an invisible guitar and Rio singing along from the driver's seat—exchanging glances with her in the rearview mirror and flooring the gas pedal—Agatha felt infinite.

Who would have thought that end-of-the-world place was so vast? The more Rio accelerated, the more the dirt road seemed to stretch out, as if the horizon embraced their journey of freedom. She saw the horses running, scattered cattle, and the trees blurred by speed, her eyes tearing up from the cold wind. She had lived her whole life in this place, but for some reason, now it felt like she was exploring a new world, and it was beautiful. Although she couldn't stop smiling, she felt a certain melancholy deep in her chest. It would be difficult to say goodbye.

But that world was not hers.

***

The fourteen days had been perfect, and Agatha felt happier than she had ever been, yet she carried a sharp, bittersweet sensation within her—the universe had handed her the most flawless gift, knowing she couldn't keep it for long. It was merely a tantalizing glimpse of the life she had once belonged to. She knew she couldn't stay; it wouldn't be fair to herself, to all the dreams and expectations she held for her future. They had been fourteen perfect days, but life was much bigger than that, and the world was much bigger than that ranch.

It was like dulce de leche—with the first spoonful, you swear you could eat it forever, but eventually, you tire of the sweetness. She knew that if she stayed, the euphoria would inevitably fade. Everything had felt like a "bed of roses" precisely because her departure was imminent, and because Rio was doing everything possible to make her want to stay. But daily life wouldn't mirror these fourteen days. Eventually, they would clash over the same old issues. She would long for the city, for the beaches, she would crave new people, and the chance to explore the four corners of the globe, while Rio would remain rooted to that ranch.

She was immensely proud of Rio, seeing her flourish, become deeply involved in the family business, commit to her goals, do what she loved, and finally find her path. But Agatha wanted the same kind of fulfillment, and she knew she would only find true happiness far from there—at her college, in her dorm five minutes from the beach, in the vibrant city where everything happened. In Darby, time stood still; every day felt interchangeable, and no matter how pleasant it was, something vital was missing for her—that burning restlessness in her chest, the craving for something she couldn't quite name, but which she knew lay elsewhere, in new horizons. She wanted to know the whole world, to see every piece of the sky; she couldn't possibly settle for just one.

As much as Rio might blame her for leaving, Rio herself had been the first to make a definitive choice: the ranch was Rio's home, it was the life she wanted, and since Rio wasn't willing to give that up, Agatha wouldn't give up hers either. If she had to choose between the life she dreamed for herself and Rio’s dream, she would choose her own. Rio chose first, and now, Agatha was choosing.

Agatha was finishing closing her last suitcase when a sharp tap pulled her from her silence. She looked up at the door, where a confused Rio was leaning against the frame.

"What are you doing?" she asked, staring at the closed suitcases scattered across the room. Agatha sighed, lowering her head. She knew what was coming.

"Finishing packing."

"But why? You aren't leaving until the beginning of the year," she questioned, genuinely confused. When Agatha looked at her, she saw the question mark written all over her face.

Agatha let out a heavy sigh, looking down:

"Rio, I'm leaving tomorrow."

The moment she said it, she watched Rio's expression transform from questioning to shock, then to sadness and hurt, almost in slow motion. Rio took steps forward, staring at the floor as if Agatha had said something profoundly complicated or nonsensical.

"What do you mean, you're leaving tomorrow?" she asked, her face distorted in disbelieving confusion, scratching the back of her neck and shaking her head.

"You already knew, Rio. I told you I was staying for two weeks."

"You—" Rio began, cutting herself off, her expression shifting rapidly as she struggled to comprehend. "But how—I don't—I don't understand. You're going to New York?" she finally managed to ask, her eyes wide.

"I am. Tomorrow."

"Why?" she burst out in clear frustration, her brow furrowed, her eyebrows knit. With every word, every stumble, Agatha felt a tightening in her chest and the knot in her throat growing. It was physically painful.

"You already knew, Rio," Agatha said with a long sigh. She couldn't even meet Rio's eyes; she already felt them burning with the tears she was fighting back. "Don't make this harder than it has to be."

"Yes, I knew you were leaving, but it's different now."

"What is different, Rio?" she asked, feeling emotionally exhausted.

"What's different?" she echoed, indignant. "Agatha, these two weeks—did that mean nothing to you?"

Agatha knew it would be difficult, but nothing had prepared her for this. Even though she knew from the start that there would be a definitive end, no one could have prepared her for how much this hurt. She looked up, blowing air across her face, trying not to cry while Rio stared at her in exasperation, waiting for her to say something—anything.

"You said it yourself, Rio, on the first day. You said we wouldn't work out, and that postponing it would only cause suffering for both of us.”

"Look how well we work, Agatha! We just spent two amazing weeks together. I love you, you love me, so how can you—Agatha!" she burst out in utter frustration. "We made this work! It is working! It’s working right now!"

"And for how long will it work?" Agatha countered, her voice choked, staring into those exasperated brown eyes that were practically begging her. "Who are we trying to fool, Riandra? These were two incredible weeks; I’ve never been happier. But what are we after this? What happens to us when I go back to California? If I stayed and only returned for my classes, what would change? Because I left once before, and we know exactly how that ended."

"Agatha, this time is different, I—"

"You what?" she asked, her tone tired and profoundly sad. "Are you coming to California with me?" Rio froze for several long seconds, and swallowing that silence, which already gave her the answer, Agatha nodded. "How can you ask me to stay, to choose you, if you can't do the same for me? How are we supposed to make this work if you won't meet me halfway?"

"I would go to California with you, but you know I don't—"

"I know you would hate it, Rio, but do you think I love the idea of spending the rest of my life here?" Now she was speaking loudly, venting all the frustrations she had buried over those days.

"You are happy here! You spent all these days being happy here! How can you say you don't like this idea?"

"It was two weeks!"

"But you were happy!" Rio shouted.

"For two weeks, Riandra! I'm talking about a lifetime. What's the point of dragging this out without thinking about a future, about what comes next? Even if it worked out, even if we made it work long-distance, what would happen when I graduate? Would you leave here? Would you move away with me? I want you to look me in the eye and say it. I want you to say you would go, that you would be willing to build a life with me somewhere else, in a city far from here. If you say that, I'll stay."

When Agatha finished speaking, silence suffocated the room, as if the weight of the moment was crushing them. With anxious blue eyes, she stared into the stormy brown depths, seeing tears gathering as Rio stared back, her lips trembling. Rio didn't even attempt to speak, and Agatha felt her heart break into a million almost physical pieces.

"You want me to choose you, but you never chose me, Rio," Agatha broke the silence, her voice now low, yet resonating like a cannon shot in Rio's ears, a shot that struck her directly in the chest. "Long before I made my choice, you had already made yours, and you stand by it firmly. You chose to stay. You chose this life. You chose the ranch. And if you can choose what is best for you, what fulfills you inside, I have that right too. I won't sacrifice myself for your sake, not when you never even tried to do the same for me."

Rio opened her mouth to speak, but Agatha shook her head, continuing: "You didn't even open my letters. I saw them in your room." With that, Rio lowered her head. "You left me in complete silence just because I made a decision. A decision you already knew about, because just as I knew you would stay, you knew I would leave. What would be different now? Would you open my letters? Would you write back? And for how long? What would happen when the reality finally hits you that I will never want what you want?"

She watched Rio swallow hard, nodding slowly, pressing her lips together tightly.

"She wants what you want, doesn't she?" was all Rio said, her eyes narrowed, after a long silence.

Agatha let out an exasperated sigh. "Rio, this isn't about—"

"No, you're right," Rio interrupted, nodding. "If that's what you want, if that's what you think, then I—I hope you'll be happy."

In the same instant, she turned to leave the room, and Agatha hurried after her.

"Riandra!" she yelled as Rio reached the hallway. "Don't walk away like this, Rio! I don't want this to end this way—"

"It's already over, Agatha," Rio replied. When she turned around, Agatha felt as if she had been punched when she saw her eyes, which, though tear-filled, were now empty. "You don't need to keep writing. You know I won't read them anyway."

"Rio," she called one last time.

"It's good that you had fun. I hope you have fun in New York too."

***

When Agatha looked in the mirror, she sighed, seeing how puffy and strained her face was from crying all night. She hadn't slept, her heart crushed in her chest. Even though she knew she had made the most rational decision for herself, logic did nothing to alleviate the severe pain.

Deep down, however improbable, she had hoped Rio would yield, because those two weeks really were special. She could see that regardless of what Rio told herself, regardless of how much she wanted to move on, what she felt for Agatha was immense, bigger than anything measurable, and it made her happy in a way that only that feeling could provide. It wasn't that she wasn't happy in California; to say that would be hypocritical—Rio herself had noted how good it was for her. But what she felt for Rio, what they shared, was a completely different kind of happiness.

She thought of her mother, who spoke of the sheer intensity of first love, and Agatha truly hoped that, eventually, the pain would subside. Weeping, she prayed that she would be able to move on. Rio was her first love, her great love, but she didn't want her to be the last—it couldn't be. She deserved someone who loved her entirely, every part of her, who championed her dreams and was willing to traverse the world by her side. As much as she loved Rio, they were fundamentally different; they were polar opposites, and no love could survive that kind of division. In her mind, Agatha was certain that love was only worthwhile when it brought complete happiness, and if staying together required one person to surrender their self-definition, it simply wasn't worth it. It couldn't last. She tried desperately to convince herself that Rio was not the love of her life—she was her first, but not the definitive one. She would find someone who completed her entirely, every piece of her, and she knew Rio would find that happiness on the ranch too.

She thought of Tessa, and how easy things were with her. She deserved a love like that. She deserved someone who looked at her with fascination, who encouraged all her dreams, who wanted to traverse the world with her and did so with shared happiness. For Agatha, love should be that easy—it shouldn't hurt just by existing; it should be a source of joy.

Though it hurt now, she knew that if she prolonged the relationship, both of them would suffer even more. Yet, despite this knowledge, the pain was profound—it hurt so much that it filled her chest and made the air heavy, difficult to breathe. She didn't understand why it ached so deeply, why it felt so heavy—it was as if she were at war with herself, her heart and mind fighting, and she was the one taking every blow, deep in her core. Logically, she knew she was doing the right thing; there was no other path. But it felt as though something wanted to anchor her there, as if her entire being refused to leave the ranch. As she walked toward her car, she felt as if two anchors were chained to her ankles.

They didn't make grand farewells. Everyone knew it was a difficult moment and that it would be easier for all of them if they kept it simple, filled only with affection. Gathered around the rental car, she hugged her parents, then cried while saying goodbye to Lilia and Javier—who embraced her for long minutes, advising her to be careful, to return soon, and to be happy. Benito made her promise to write as often as she could, and Wanda cried with her, tears of anticipated longing, squeezing her tightly and reminding her that the world was vast and she would find great happiness everywhere. Even Natasha had come and gifted her a basket filled with bread and sweets that her grandmother had baked especially for her journey. Some of the ranch hands came to say goodbye, too. All the important people were there, except Rio.

She felt that weight on her feet, the storm in her entire body that seemed to refuse to obey her own mind—even though she had chosen to leave, her insides screamed for her to stay; it was almost as if, by going, she was defying a force of nature.

Before getting into the car, she smiled and waved, furtively looking around for any sign, but Rio was nowhere. Agatha lingered for a few more minutes, her heart in her hand. She expected anything, even for Rio to arrive screaming, crying, begging her to stay. She waited for any sign from Rio, but there was none. She should have known—and she needed to accept it; there was no alternative. The decision was made—hers, and Rio's.

She kept smiling throughout the entire departure, her cheeks aching from forcing the expression. She smiled until she was out of sight, already on the dirt road, and as soon as she was far from the eyes of those she loved, she let her tears fall in a desperate gasp, sobbing loudly, her vision blurred by the heavy tears streaming down uncontrollably.

She gripped the steering wheel with both hands, feeling that brooch weighing on her chest like a ton. Her heart was heavy, her entire body heavy, and no matter how much she cried, nothing seemed to bring relief. And now, more than ever, she needed to get out of there. She needed to pass all those trees, those horses, finish that dirt road. She needed to leave—she needed to escape that town and wash herself clean, she needed to leave it all behind.

She could already see the asphalt; she was almost at the town line leading to the highway when she glanced in the rearview mirror and saw her—Rio, galloping after her car, whipping the reins hard, trying desperately to catch up. The sob that escaped her was gut-wrenching. What was the point now?

She pressed the gas pedal harder, leaning forward, clutching the steering wheel as her tears fell, and when she finally crossed the boundary, entering the highway, she saw Rio stop in the rearview mirror. Still on her horse, still on the dirt road, Rio watched her drive away.

Even when she chased after her, she didn't have the courage to cross the dirt road to the highway, and that hurt more than any farewell moment they could have shared.
