"Rio, where are you exactly?" The worry in her tone was unmistakable now. Rio swallowed hard, tears finally beginning to prick her eyes. She squeezed them shut and took several long gulps of the beer in her lap. "Rio? Are you drinking right now?"

"Just a few beers," she murmured, dodging the question as she rested her head on the wheel. "I’m in front of the station. I thought you’d be back."

"You’re close to home," Olivia said softly. Rio nodded against the steering wheel — not in agreement, but in sheer, weary exasperation. "Put your seatbelt on and go home. Drive slow for me, okay? Please."

"Okay," Rio whispered, her voice barely a thread. She reached for the belt, pulled it across her chest, and clicked it into place.

“You promised you were going to stop.”

"It was just a few beers, Olivia."

"It doesn't matter. I’m in another town, and I’m sure nobody has any idea where you are. What if something happens? Why is it so hard for you to be careful? It’s for your own sake, Rio, for your own life."

The last thing Rio cared about right now was her own life.

“Please, just go home.”

"I’m going," she lied, starting the car.

“I’ll call you tomorrow, okay?”

“Okay,” Rio said, and the line went dead.

Of course, she wasn’t going home.

***

Stumbling in a drunken haze, Rio fumbled with the back door of Pedra Purpura, eventually throwing her weight against the solid wood to force it open. She rarely visited outside of business hours, but the winery was a second home, and she was desperate for its familiar silence. Guided by her flashlight, she traced the stone and timber walls until she reached her back office and the private cellar tucked within.

Since childhood, words had been Rio's enemy. She had never been articulate; her thoughts remained locked away until they soured into a bitter cocktail of anger and frustration. More often than not, that rage was directed inward — a punishment for her inability to speak, for her failure to grasp the world with the effortless grace everyone else seemed to possess.

She clung to routine like a lifeline. On the ranch, time was a circle: her father left in the morning and returned by sunset. That predictability was her only shield. But now, even the slightest shift sent her into a panic. She loathed change in any form, which was exactly why she couldn't bring herself to step foot in her own house.

Being home meant facing Benito. He was always there with his girlfriend, his abrasive voice a haunting echo of their father’s. She’d see him soaking up the sun on the porch or reading in the living room, a perfect, agonizing silhouette of Javier. Every glance felt like a blow to the solar plexus. It was his constant presence — those expectant brown eyes following her, the worried tone, the incessant hovering — that drove her away. She wanted to be alone — at least, that was what she tried to tell herself.

Benito was a living ghost. He had their father's mannerisms, but his eyes — the two of them had the same eyes — their mother’s eyes. Looking at him was like looking into a mirror that reflected a knot of grief she couldn't untie. She was terrified he would see right through her — that he would peel back the layers and find the raw pain and longing she tried so hard to bury. She didn't want to be understood; she wanted to be left the fuck alone.

Then there was Agatha. What the fuck was she even doing there? Rio managed to avoid her, but her presence was a phantom limb, felt in every whispered conversation between Lilia and Evanora. And then there was the boy, Nicholas, a constant shadow that made Rio feel cornered in her own home.

She saw him nearly every day — wind-blown brown curls and a laugh that seemed to drift through the air like a permanent breeze. Benito was devoted to him, parading him around the ranch and the winery, feigning interest in childish things just to keep the boy grinning. And god, he never stopped smiling. It was contagious, and it was devastating. He would dash through the vineyards and often cross Rio’s path, offering her a shy, hopeful look. It wasn't his fault; he was adorable, but the mere sight of him cut her to the core.

Rio turned on the light in her office, and as the drunken dizziness hit her, she gripped the edge of the desk, picking up the portrait of her father she kept there. She smiled — the first genuine smile she’d had in days. She loved that photo; it was just him, a recent shot, his skin weathered by the sun and his hair graying. She missed him with a ferocity that stole her breath.

"I wish you were here," she whispered to the portrait, clutching it to her chest as she shuffled toward the cellar and sank onto the floor between the shelves.

Her head throbbed, and not just from the alcohol. Her mind always ached when she thought or felt too much — a heavy, familiar burden she’d carried since childhood. It was a heat at the base of her neck, a sharp stinging at her temples; she felt truly assaulted by the weight of her own consciousness.

She missed her father in every mundane detail of the day, but mostly, she missed the silence he provided. With Javier, she never had to explain herself. He would just look at her and know. He understood her thoughts before she even formed them, always knowing exactly what she needed to hear. Even when she hadn't listened, she had felt safe. Now, that safety was gone.

Rio grabbed a bottle, pulled a corkscrew from her pocket, and took a long, burning swig. Setting the portrait upright beside her, she stared into his eyes as if he were actually there. "I know you’re pissed that I’m drinking," she murmured, "but I’m pissed that you’re gone. So I guess we’re even." She drank again, the wine spilling from the corners of her mouth and staining her shirt.

"I know everyone has to go sometime, but did it have to be now?" Her voice cracked, tears finally blurring her vision. "I still need you, dad. I’m completely fucking lost. I’m scared, and I don’t know how to stop... I just can't." The words thinned out into a sob as she buried her face in her hands. "I can't go home. I can't do any of this without you. I’m at rock bottom again."

Leaning her head against the cold stone wall, she let the tears stream down her face, feeling small and utterly powerless. She had always been full of fear, but the mask was finally slipping. She tilted the bottle back and drank until it was empty, the wine mixing with the salt of her tears.

"I can't go back there. Everyone is at the house," she sighed, glancing at the photo with a roll of her eyes. "I bet you’d love it, wouldn't you? The whole family under one roof. But you know how this is for me. I don't want them there."

She knit her brows in a silent plea, as if begging the portrait for an alternative. "Benny made his choice," she muttered, shrugging off the imaginary judgment in her father’s gaze. She was drunk enough now that the photo felt like a living presence, a silent witness to her unraveling. "Why do I have to be the one to accept it? Nobody ever gave a damn about my side. It’s not just that he left, it’s that he left with her."

Rio spoke through gritted teeth, trying to swallow the bitterness rising in her throat with another gulp of wine. "I spent six years in hell after mom died, caught in that endless tug-of-war. She’d come and go, promising we’d find a way, only to run back to California every single time. Back to Tessa."

She practically spat the name.

"Benito was right here. He saw what it did to me, and he still chose her? He stayed on her side. You can't tell me there are no sides when he moved in with her a year after she got married. He spent all those years with them. He was my brother, but he chose her and now he’s more her brother than mine. He’s Agatha’s shadow, her son’s godfather. He’s gone, dad. They’re all gone."

Rio was desperate for an answer, for just one word from her father. As she stared at his image and drank, she wondered what he would have said if she’d had the courage to say all this while he was still alive.

“It hurt when you chose her, too,” Rio confessed in a fragile whisper. “You’d spend weeks in LA and come back radiant, telling everyone how beautiful your family was, showing off photos to anyone who’d look. Your family...” She spat the word with disgust. “How could they be your family if I wasn't there?”

She buried her face in her hands, her head swaying. An immense pressure built in her chest, her heart hammering so hard it felt like her body might fracture — as if she simply wasn't built to carry this much weight. She let herself sob, but even with the tears flowing, she felt obstructed, as if she were slowly choking.

“What the fuck is Agatha even doing here?” she demanded of the portrait. “She already got everything she wanted. What’s left for her to take? I can’t do this, dad. Not with her in the house next door.”

Agatha had always been her greatest vulnerability, a wound that refused to scar over. Rio wouldn't lie and say she suffered every single day — she had lived her life, she had been fine — but this was different. This was the ghost of a pain; a dull ache that she always knew was there, even when she couldn't feel it.

She knew it was just a piece of paper in a frame, but she could still feel her father’s stern judgment.

“I know I shouldn’t have snapped at her like that, but you had just died!” she cried, her brow furrowed and tears hot on her cheeks. “I didn't want to talk to anyone. I didn't want to be there, and I sure as hell didn't want to see her. I was pissed! I’m still pissed! I didn't want—” Rio realized she was shouting. She let out a sharp exhale and slumped back against the stone wall. “You died, dad. I know it’s not her fault, but you’re gone and I’m fucking angry because I still need you.”

She closed her eyes and let the tears fall freely. Reaching for the bottle, she took several heavy gulps, her breathing ragged, before turning back to the photo.

“What if I break again? Like I did when mom died?”

The absolute silence of the room only made the hollow ache in her chest worse.

“I think it’s already happening. I feel myself breaking,” Rio confessed, her eyes pleading with the portrait. “I shouldn’t be so hard on Benito. I shouldn't have been so cruel to her. But I don’t know how to function anymore. I just want to disappear. I want to stop existing, dad. I want to get on a horse and ride until I hit a place where no one knows my name. I’m tired, I’m lost, and I’m just so fucking sad.” Her voice finally gave way to a sob.

She needed him. If he were there, he would have knit those thick brows of his and pulled her into a crushing embrace. He would have promised her that they’d find a way — because they always did. Together, they always found a way.

"I know you’re probably disappointed in me, but with everything going on, with you being gone... can’t you give me a break? You left, Benito moved in, and now I’ve got Agatha and that boy to deal with." Rio groaned, thumping her forehead with her palm. "River... what the hell was she thinking? Why did she give him that name?"

Her father’s steady gaze from the portrait was her only answer. She let out a long, weary sigh.

"Don’t give me that look," she said, pointing a finger at the frame. "And don't give me that 'she still loves me' bullshit. She doesn't. I’m way too old for this shit. It was guilt; pure, fucking guilt." Rio was talking to herself as much as to the photo now. "Nicholas River... My God, those eyes. It’s like looking into a mirror." She shook her head, taking several heavy swigs of wine. "I see why you loved the little runt. He’s adorable." It was meant to be a grumble, but her lips betrayed her, twitching into a faint smile. "He’s always following me. Why the hell is he always following me? I feel like you’re punishing me from up there, and I can't for the life of me figure out why."

She couldn't explain the sensation, but she felt her father’s presence as if he were truly there listening to her spiral. Maybe it was just the booze, but it was a comfort nonetheless. She felt his stare so intensely that it felt like a stern reprimand, prompting her to take another defensive gulp of wine.

"I’m not apologizing to her," she muttered, then huffed at the portrait. "Stop looking at me like that. I won’t do it. I know I shouldn’t have said those things, but they’re said. It’s done. If it’s any consolation, I won’t say them again. Besides, she never apologized to me." She fell into a sulky silence, then gasped as if the portrait had insulted her. "For what? She spent six years playing games with my head! If that hurt her too, that’s her own damn fault. She has to live with her choices." Rio crossed her arms like a pouting child and turned away, but she couldn't last ten seconds without looking back. She glanced at him out of the corner of her eye, letting out a bratty growl. "I know she loved me once. I know she got hurt too. But she still got married. She went off to live her perfect life with her perfect wife and her adorable son, and me? I never got over a single thing." Rio finished the second bottle in five long, desperate gulps. "I wouldn’t have chosen me back then either. I was a mess. And I was the only one who didn't see it. That’s why I’m so scared, dad. I don’t want to go back to that dark place again."

She picked up the photo with both hands and pressed it to her chest as if trying to pull him into a hug, her eyes squeezed shut. She stared at his face for a long time before setting the portrait back on the floor with a heavy sigh.

"I’ll apologize," she said, her voice thick with defeat. "I don’t know when. I don’t know if I can even find the words, but I promise I’ll try. I’ll try to fix things with her and with Benito. I just need time. Please, help me. I don’t want to be the person I was. I need you to show me the way, dad. I'm lost."

She stared at the photo for a few more seconds, her silent plea hanging in the air. Rio didn’t know how to pray, but she wanted to believe that if her father was anywhere in the hereafter, he was looking out for her. She was too proud to ask for help, but she was at the end of her rope. She needed a light, a sign — anything.

She reached for another bottle, uncorked it, and took a deep swig, only to spit it out instantly. It was a Calcedo.

That wasn’t the sign she was looking for.

***

Thirteen Years Ago

Rio groaned in frustration as the morning sun cut directly across her eyes. Keeping them squeezed shut, she fumbled blindly around the mattress for a pillow to bury her face in, her scowl deepening when she found nothing but empty sheets.

“What the fuck—” she started to grumble, finally forcing her eyes open. She nearly jumped out of her skin when she saw Benito standing right over her. He was perched atop a literal pile of her pillows, his eyes wide and his brows knit together as if he were staring at a ghost. “What the hell, kid? You trying to kill me? At this hour?”

“It’s noon,” he muttered, shaking his head. Rio rolled her eyes and waited for an explanation, but the boy remained pale and rigid.

“What are you doing here, pendejo?” she snapped, her patience already worn thin as she slumped back onto the mattress. Benito moved to sit on the edge of the bed beside her.

“I wanted to talk to you before you got out of bed,” he said cautiously. Rio narrowed her eyes, studying the strained, almost pained expression on his face.

“Benito, what happened?” she asked, her voice sharpening as she sat back up. The visible anguish in her brother’s eyes sent a jolt of alarm through her. “Is dad okay?”

“Yes, he’s fine—”

“Is Richard okay? Lilia? Evanora?”

“Everyone is fine, I just—”

“If everyone is fine, then why do you look like you’re about to tell me someone died?” she demanded, grabbing him by the shoulders in a burst of exasperation. He pressed his lips together, his nerves palpable. “Just spit it out, Benito, for god’s sake!”

“Everyone’s fine! I just thought it was better if I told you first, so you’d know before seeing everyone else... so you wouldn't blow up. Not that I think you will blow up, but I didn't want you caught off guard. I know you don't handle—” He started to ramble, his words tripping over each other, until Rio shook him firmly.

“Benito. Talk.”

“Agatha just got here with Tessa,” he whispered. “They’re engaged.”

If Benito said anything more, the words never reached her. Rio’s entire body went numb, and her heart felt as though it had simply stopped beating. She had known this was coming, but a stubborn, silent part of her had clung to the hope that it wouldn't happen — that Agatha would change her mind and choose to stay with her.

***

"My God, it’s gorgeous!" her mother exclaimed, her eyes welling up as she took Agatha’s hand to admire the engagement ring. "Tessa, honey, you have exquisite taste."

"Thank you," Tessa replied, her cheeks flushed with a wide, triumphant grin. When Agatha caught her eye, Tessa offered a playful wink and a small shrug. Despite having known Agatha's parents for years, she seemed uncharacteristically shy in their presence. "I just wanted to pick something she’d truly love."

"It’s perfect, babe," Agatha said, forcing a smile. Tessa beamed back at her. "I’ve probably told you that a million times already."

They had arrived in Darby less than two hours ago and had been doted on by the family from the second they stepped into town. Javier had welcomed them with a celebratory breakfast on the porch alongside Lilia and Benito, clearly thrilled by the engagement and finally meeting the famous Tessa. Despite their six-year history, Tessa had never once set foot on the ranch.

The trip had been a spontaneous decision that caught Agatha off guard. For years, Tessa had shown zero interest in visiting Agatha’s hometown. She didn't need to; once they had become official, Tessa had paid for Agatha’s parents to fly to Los Angeles, introduced them to her own social circle, and constantly encouraged them to visit the city instead. Whenever the prospect of Darby was raised, Tessa’s reaction was always the same — a polite but firm distaste for anything rustic.

Yet, as soon as they returned from Paris with Agatha’s "yes," Tessa had insisted they visit. She claimed she didn't just want their blessing; she wanted to see where Agatha had grown up now that they were building a future together.

Agatha had agreed, but only reluctantly.

It wasn't that she didn't want to see her family, but returning to Darby with Tessa felt wrong — almost dirty. The ring felt like a heavy anchor on her finger. She was happy, or she told herself she was; after all, this was what she wanted. But it was a choice made with her head, not her heart. Agatha knew perfectly well that if her heart were the one making the calls, it wouldn't have been Tessa standing there.

Tessa wasn't perfect. She was possessive and a perfectionist to a fault, always craving the center of the room. But in Agatha’s world, she was the closest thing to perfection available. Tessa was sweet, attentive, and fiercely invested in Agatha’s career. She was her loudest cheerleader, constantly reminding Agatha that they were going to conquer the world together. That was the dream Agatha had always chased.

Their six-year relationship had been a turbulent cycle of breakups and reconciliations, always stumbling over the same hurdles. Yet, Tessa had been persistent. She was the one who stayed, convincing Agatha that life was about more than the fleeting intensity of young love. She promised a life of shared achievements and stability, making it clear that no obstacle was too great for someone who truly wanted to be together.

Agatha had only just graduated, and she had been adamant that marriage wasn't on her radar — at least not for a long while. Her focus was entirely on building a career, securing a solid job, and carving out her own place in the world. But everything changed a few months ago when Tessa’s father offered her a position at his firm as a coordinator for international law — a role nearly impossible to land with less than five years of experience. Tessa had simply laughed it off, telling her that if a career was what she wanted, then a career was exactly what she would have.

Agatha had suspected a proposal was coming. She had even discussed the possibility with Rio months ago during her last visit to Darby. Though she had told Rio then that she would say yes, she hadn't truly known what her answer would be. She wasn't sure if she actually wanted this. Rationally, it was the dream life. Yet, a part of her constantly wondered if it was worth sacrificing the raw desires of her heart for a polished ideal. She told herself it wasn't a sacrifice; she cared for Tessa — she loved her — and they had built a beautiful foundation together. If this was what her future looked like, it should have been enough. She deserved a good life, a thriving career, and a partner who adored her and would go to any lengths to make her happy.

Still, a persistent unease twisted in the pit of her stomach. While Tessa sat there smiling, basking in the attention of Agatha's doting parents, Agatha found herself forcing a grin, her mind drifting elsewhere. Her thoughts were with her heart. They were with Rio.

Her heart insisted she deserved more than just a good life. It yearned for the kind of passion that hummed in her bones — a consuming love and the unique sense of relief she only found when looking into the brown eyes she loved most in the world. But she knew she couldn't live by heart alone. No one could survive on love alone, and she had already given Rio every possible chance. It hadn't worked. She couldn't spend her life chasing something that constantly failed, no matter how desperately she wanted it to succeed.

Then, as if the universe were mocking her, Agatha heard the rhythmic trot of a horse. Her eyes immediately darted toward the living room window. Though the rider was too far off to see clearly, Agatha knew exactly who it was — Rio, galloping away on Gaia, disappearing into the distance.

***

With her patience entirely spent, Natasha pounded on the door once more, pacing the porch with her hands on her hips. She was desperate to keep her cool, but she had to get Rio out of there and try, for the thousandth time, to make her best friend see reason.

"She’s not here," Bucky said, cracking the door just a sliver. The moment he tried to shut it, Natasha jammed her foot in the frame. With a surge of strength and zero patience, she shoved the door open and forced her way inside.

"Right, and I suppose her horse just decided to graze in your yard because the grass is tastier," Natasha muttered, brushing past him. "Go play in traffic, Barnes."

"Play in traffic, Natasha?" Bucky scrambled after her, eventually cutting her off at his bedroom door to block her path. "Didn't know a skank like you was working the streets these days."

"No? And how do you think your mother kept the lights on?" Without breaking a sweat, Natasha hoisted him by the collar, tossed him aside, and marched into the room. She let out a heavy sigh, shielding her eyes from the scene as Bucky let out a low, mocking chuckle behind her.

Rio was a mess of tears, slumped in a wooden chair in the center of the room. A woman — stripper or hooker, Natasha neither knew nor cared — was perched on her lap in nothing but red lace lingerie. She was cupping Rio’s face with surprising tenderness, wiping away tears with her thumbs as she listened to Rio’s drunken rambling.

"Sorry to interrupt, but the show’s over," Natasha announced, clapping her hands sharply while keeping her gaze averted from the half-naked woman.

"Natasha!" Rio exclaimed, sounding almost relieved. Natasha took a slow, deep breath to steady her temper. "Cherry, this is my best friend, Natasha."

"I thought Bucky was your best friend," the woman noted sweetly. Natasha cleared her throat.

"Was it Bucky who called you?" Natasha asked. When the woman nodded, Natasha’s jaw tightened. "Truly, he’s a hell of a friend." Rio nodded in agreement, earning herself a sharp, reprimanding smack on the back of the head from Natasha. "Get dressed. She’s done here."

"Oh, but I—"

"Settle up with Bucky outside," Natasha snapped through clenched teeth. The woman faltered for a moment, glancing at Rio, who simply shrugged like a child caught breaking the rules.

As the woman dressed, Natasha sat down with her back turned, spinning Rio’s chair around to face her. She rolled her eyes when she caught Rio still trying to peer over her shoulder at the woman’s every move.

"Rio, I am losing my goddamn patience," Natasha whispered. Rio looked back at her, her brows knit in a drunken pout. "I’m not your watchdog, and I’m tired of playing the part."

"How did you even find me?" Rio murmured, reaching for a stray beer can. Before it could touch her lips, Natasha slapped it out of her hand. The can went flying, spraying beer across the bedroom rug. "Natasha!"

"I bailed you out of jail two weeks ago. You promised that was the end of it, and I believed you because I always do," Natasha said, cupping Rio's face and forcing their eyes to meet. "I believe in you, Rio. I don't understand why you’re drowning yourself in booze, drugs, and gambling, throwing yourself into fights with strangers over things you won't even remember tomorrow. You are so much better than this. You have a good heart. You're a good friend, a good daughter, a good sister. You’re good, Rio. You have talent and the world at your feet. Why the hell are you doing this to yourself?"

"I wasn't doing anything." Rio pulled away, shoving Natasha’s hands aside and slumping back into the chair. "I just came here to drink. I didn't do anything wrong. I’m not going back to jail, Natasha! I promised. That was the last time."

"Then why did you have a hooker on your lap?" Natasha muttered through gritted teeth.

"She’s a stripper!" Rio corrected her, wagging an emphatic finger. Natasha rolled her eyes. "And I wouldn't go to jail for a hooker anyway; it’s not illegal here. Besides, I didn't even call her. Bucky did!"

"Look, I get it, Bucky was our friend in school, but—"

"He was just trying to help!" Rio interrupted, her voice rising in exasperation. "I got here crying and I didn't want to leave. I didn't want to do anything stupid. I just wanted to clear my head, to get all this shit out of my mind, and he—"

"All what shit, Rio?"

"Agatha is engaged. She brought her Barbie to the ranch to break the good news."

The words caught Natasha completely off guard. She opened her mouth to speak, then closed it, straightening her posture as she searched for what to say. This was dangerous territory.

Nearly everything was delicate when it came to Rio. She had never handled her emotions well, remaining stubbornly, almost rigidly, guarded. It hadn't hindered their friendship much in the past, but since her mother’s death and the start of Agatha’s life in California, Rio had transformed. She had become a stranger to everyone around her — utterly and dangerously lost.

Natasha understood grief. She had faced her own share of losses and a difficult family life. She knew that while she was an open book, others were not. Grief was a jagged thing; if left unaddressed, it lingered, leaving permanent scars. She could see that Rio was still blinded by her pain, and that was exactly why she refused to let go. Her best friend was still in there somewhere, trapped in the eye of the storm, needing nothing but time and a hand to hold.

It had been six years since the shift began — not six years of total failure, but a volatile cycle of highs and lows. The lows were devastating, an endless stretch of rock bottom, but the highs were brilliant enough to remind Natasha that Rio was still a person of immense potential. She just needed Rio to see it, to find a path forward without constantly glancing in the rearview mirror.

Agatha was, without a doubt, one of the lowest points.

Natasha had witnessed their relationship from the front row. They had grown up together, and she had watched their story unfold piece by piece. She liked Agatha, but once the move to California happened, everything fractured. While Rio’s spiral wasn't entirely Agatha’s fault, it was impossible not to hold her somewhat responsible for the wreckage left behind.

If Agatha had simply left and they had made a clean break, Rio might have eventually healed, no matter how long it took. But that wasn't how things went down.

Agatha returned at least twice a year, and every time she did, she and Rio inevitably fell back into each other's orbit. It was a toxic, fractured arrangement — they weren't exactly together, yet they were inseparable the moment Agatha set foot in town. And every time she left, Rio fell apart. The script never changed: Rio would beg her to stay, to quit school in California, to build a life in Darby, and to leave Tessa behind. They would cry, scream, and swear they were done for good, only for the cycle to reset. The months following Agatha’s departures were always the darkest, the deepest pits of Rio’s depression.

God forgive her, but Natasha secretly hoped Agatha would just get married and disappear for good. She felt it in her gut: it was the only way Rio would ever find peace. Rio needed to realize that life was more than a series of losses and goodbyes. Cycles had to end for life to move forward, and Rio was stuck in place.

"Rio..." Natasha began gently, scratching the back of her neck as she met her friend’s tearful gaze. "I’m sorry, but this was bound to happen eventually. You know that."

Rio squeezed her eyes shut, shaking her head in denial.

"That’s just how it is, Rio. Things don't always go our way."

"Why?" Rio asked through gritted teeth, her voice strained and heavy with grief. "Why doesn't she want me?"

"Rio..."

"Why, Natasha?" Rio screamed this time, tears streaming down her face.

Natasha took a deep breath. "Rio, I’m your best friend. I love you to death, and because I do, I have to tell you the things no one else will," she said carefully. Rio wiped her eyes and looked up. "But I don’t want to kick you while you’re down. I know this hurts. I know it sucks. So, I’m asking: do you want the truth, or do you want me to just comfort you?"

Rio leaned forward, resting her elbows on her thighs and her face in her hands. Natasha mimicked the posture, maintaining steady eye contact. They sat in the heavy silence until Rio’s sobbing subsided. Finally, she took a shaky breath and nodded.

"I want the truth," Rio whispered. "No matter how much it hurts."

Natasha swallowed hard and nodded. "You guys tried, Rio. You tried for six long years." Rio nodded, the tears welling up again. "But it didn't work. It couldn't work. Agatha wants a life beyond this town, and you can’t imagine yourself anywhere else. But to be real with you: what are you even doing with your life?"

Rio buried her face in her hands as Natasha pushed on. "She actually broke up with Tessa once to be with you, and what did you do? You kept drinking, kept starting trouble. You threw every college application in the trash, even the ones right here in Montana. What did you expect to happen? The truth is, you’re drifting, Rio, and that hurts everyone around you, not just her. She wants to build a future. What do you want?"

Rio wiped her face, a fresh sob catching in her throat. "I want her," she whispered brokenly. "I just want her, Natasha."

"Life has to be bigger than one person, Rio," Natasha replied softly, shaking her head. "Even if she gave you another chance today, what would change? What would you actually do? Just keep racing and gambling your life away?"

"I take care of the ranch, I—"

"Come on, Rio. You’re barely even there." When Rio’s brows knit in defense, Natasha simply shrugged. "You asked for the truth. I know you love that land, and I know you’re capable. Your dad told me the wines you produced are the best in his entire collection."

"He’s my father, Natasha. He has to say that."

"No, he says it because you’re talented when you actually show up. When you pull yourself together and decide to start the day right; when you get your hands dirty and actually engage with the ranch and with us, you’re incredible."

Rio looked up, her expression a fragile plea for those words to be true. It broke Natasha’s heart; she wanted so desperately for her friend to see her own worth.

"I’m sorry it didn't work out with Agatha, I really am. But sometimes the right person finds us at the wrong time. Right now, you shouldn't be with anyone, not even her." Rio shook her head, the tears falling harder. "You need to focus on yourself. I know you want to be better, and you will be, but you have to stop living in the rearview mirror. Life is happening right now. Agatha is moving on, but you’re still here, and you have so much ahead of you. A legacy, a family that adores you, and a best friend who’s never going to let you go."

Rio let out a sharp, jagged breath and tried to push her away, but Natasha caught her hand, holding it tight.

"Listen to me. I know you don't see it, but I have no reason to lie: you are amazing, Rio." Natasha nodded firmly as Rio’s brow furrowed. "I’m with you, through thick and thin. Let Agatha marry that insipid blonde. Once you get your act together and take over this estate, you’ll be the most sought-after woman in the state."

"I don't give a damn about that," Rio murmured, looking away.

"But you care about the ranch. You care about your father." Rio’s eyes snapped back to hers. "How do you think he feels watching you throw it all away? You always said you were going to stay, that you’d be his successor. So where are you? Where is his right hand?"

"I don't know," Rio whispered. "I’m lost."

"No, you’re finding yourself," Natasha said with patient conviction. "Everyone moves at their own pace, and that’s fine. But you have to admit it’s time to wake up. It's time to actually live. Please, Rio."

Rio let out a long, heavy sigh. "I don't even know where to start."

"Well," Natasha said, "I think the first step is letting go."

***

"God, how did you ever manage to live here?" Tessa murmured, her face twisted in a look of pure disgust as she pulled off her boots. Agatha rolled her eyes, taking them over to the sink to clean them while Tessa sank into one of the porch armchairs.

"It’s not as bad as you make it out to be," Agatha said with a faint laugh. Her fiancée arched an eyebrow in a way that made Agatha chuckle. "It’s just a world away from the life you’re used to."

"I have to admit, it is beautiful," Tessa said, her tone softening into something more contemplative. This time, Agatha’s smile was genuine; she watched as Tessa’s posture relaxed, her eyes fixed on the horizon, seemingly captivated by the sweeping fields and the silhouettes of horses in the distance.

Agatha set the boots aside and perched on the arm of the chair. Tessa immediately wrapped her arms around Agatha's waist, pulling her down into her lap. Agatha settled against her, nestling into the warmth of her body. She bit her lip, staring out at the skyline while the weight of the ring on her finger felt suddenly heavy as Tessa stroked her thigh.

"It really is beautiful," Tessa repeated. Agatha looked down, noticing the way Tessa’s nose wrinkled in a sharp grimace. "But it reeks of horses." Agatha rolled her eyes and shook her head. "What? Baby, it’s the truth!"

"Of course it smells like horses. Darby is literally horse country. What were you expecting? Marshmallows?" Tessa shrugged. "It doesn't reek, Tessa. It just smells like horses."

"Are you honestly trying to tell me horses don’t stink?"

Agatha laughed, but a twinge of guilt pricked at her chest. It felt wrong to laugh at her home, to treat it like a joke.

"I do get why you like it, though. It’s quiet and beautiful. It feels like time just stands still here."

"I spent my whole life wanting to leave this place," Agatha confessed, drawing Tessa’s full attention. "I always felt like I wasn't meant for a tiny town with no real future. But I still miss it. It's home." She gave a small shrug, and Tessa nodded.

"This place really isn't for you," Tessa said, a hint of disdain creeping back into her voice. Agatha’s brows knit together. "Don't take it the wrong way, I know it’s where you grew up, but you’re meant for much bigger things than this, Agatha. You were born for the world, for greatness, for the extraordinary. You’re incredible." Agatha offered a weak smile in return. "What would you even be here? This place is the middle of nowhere. It might have a history for you, but you don't belong here."

"And where exactly do I belong, Tessa?" she asked teasingly. Tessa smiled, biting her lip as she adjusted Agatha in her lap, pulling her legs to either side so they were sitting face-to-face.

"With me," Tessa said. She took Agatha’s right hand and pressed a kiss to it. Agatha rolled her eyes but couldn't help the smile that followed. "You belong with me, in every corner of the globe, in the biggest cities on earth where everyone can see you and know just how amazing my wife is."

"Your wife, huh?" Agatha murmured, a soft laugh escaping her. Tessa nodded, leaning in to trail kisses along her neck.

"Yes. My wife. Agatha Mason." Agatha’s heart swelled with tenderness as she saw the way Tessa’s blue eyes shone with adoration. She reached out, caressing Tessa’s face with a smile. "I just have one confession to make, and I hope my wife won't be too mad."

“Here we go...”

"Would you be upset if I said I never want to come back here again? Seriously, babe, this place stinks!"

***

Throughout the entire dinner, Rio felt a mounting urge to shatter a wine bottle over her own head. It was a special kind of torture, but there was no escape. She was forced to play the part of the civil guest; after all, Benito was the only one who knew she and Agatha had been carrying on an affair this whole time. So she sat there, plastering on a fake smile and nodding as Agatha’s fiancée prattled on about wedding venues, their new LA apartment, and the future they were building — all while Rio downed glass after glass of wine, pinned under the heavy weight of Agatha’s gaze.

The irony was bordering on the absurd. This dinner was a celebration of Agatha’s engagement, yet Agatha couldn't seem to look at anyone else. Despite the tension, Rio held her tongue. She didn't offer a single sarcastic jab or a whispered provocation; she remained the picture of cordiality until the moment she could finally leave.

Natasha’s words echoed in her mind, a persistent rhythm she couldn't ignore. Her friend was right.

The truth was, Rio had been adrift for years, ever since her mother died. Without her, the world stopped making sense; it was as if her own life had lost its internal compass. She had simply broken, though she hadn't realized she’d stopped functioning until it was too late. Agatha’s departure had only deepened the void. Rio had never been equipped to handle the gravity of her own emotions; she felt perpetually drained, as if every minor setback weighed three times more than it should. She was lost, and she was finally beginning to hate the feeling. She needed to find her way back.

She had always assumed taking over the family ranch would be an automatic transition, a birthright she’d eventually just step into. Now, she realized how far she had fallen from that path. She had squandered her father’s trust and neglected her duties, reducing her entire existence to the racetrack. But despite the whispers about her lack of ambition, Rio did have dreams. She wanted that ranch. She knew she could run it, if only she could find the strength to try.

The world was moving on without her. It was a bitter pill to swallow, but she had to face facts: she wouldn't be young forever, and she refused to spend the rest of her life as a burden. She was ready to find her own path, and she would do whatever it took to get there.

She was determined to move on, to finally forge her own path, and the certainty of it settled deep in her bones. She would do whatever it took.

Rio was leaning against the wooden porch railing when she spotted a figure in the distance. She squinted, half-expecting a drunken hallucination, but the image held firm. It was Agatha, cutting through the tall grass in the dead of night, heading straight for her. Rio let out a long, weary sigh, shaking her head as she took another sip of wine. It was impossible to move forward when a chain was still fastened to her ankles.

"What are you doing here?" Rio murmured, her voice thick with exhaustion. She didn't bother looking up as Agatha reached the porch and leaned against the railing beside her — not quite touching, but close enough to feel the heat radiating between them.

"I saw the light," Agatha replied softly. "I thought it might be you."

"And why did you come to find me? Shouldn't you be in bed with your fiancée right now?" Rio finally turned to face her, her expression a mask of cold indifference. Agatha’s brow furrowed as she let out a heavy sigh.

"Rio..."

"I’m serious, Agatha," Rio snapped, a hint of sharp exasperation breaking through. "What is there left to say? You’re engaged!"

"I know, and I’m sorry," Agatha whispered, her voice barely audible. Rio felt a lump form in her throat as those blue eyes began to shimmer with unshed tears. "I’m so sorry we didn't work out. I wanted us to! I wanted it more than anything." Her voice finally cracked, and Rio took a sharp breath. She was trapped in Agatha’s gaze, unable to look away as the tears began to spill over. "I wanted us to meet in the middle. I wanted you to chase me. I wanted you to put down the bottle and move to California like you promised. I wanted you to answer my letters. I wanted you to fight for me instead of just giving up, instead of losing yourself to the booze and the track. I wanted you. That’s all I ever wanted."

Rio swallowed hard. The tears streaming down Agatha’s face were now mirrored on her own as they stood in the heavy silence — blue eyes locked onto brown.

"I wanted us to make it, too," Rio said, her voice choked and raw. Agatha nodded and threw herself into Rio’s arms. Rio closed her eyes instantly, pulling her tight against her chest. "I didn't want it to end like this, I swear. I’m so sorry."

With her face buried in the crook of Rio’s neck, Agatha shook her head, her tears soaking into the collar of Rio’s shirt. After a long moment, she pulled back, wiping her eyes and looking at Rio with a troubled expression.

"I wish things had been different, too."

"I know, Agatha," Rio murmured, the words catching in her throat.

"I’m sad... and I’m so angry—"

"You’re angry?" Rio asked, her brow furrowing in disbelief. "How do you think I feel, Agatha? You are the love of my life. I’ve never loved anyone the way I love you, and I probably never will. I have to stand by and watch you marry someone else, and you’re the one who’s angry?"

"Yes, I’m angry! Because you spent years telling me that being together was all you wanted, but you never lifted a finger to make it happen. You just talked. You made me feel guilty for leaving, but you never actually—"

"It’s over, Agatha." Rio could have shouted; she could have fought, argued, or begged Agatha to throw it all away. But Natasha’s warnings were echoing in her head. "You’re engaged. What good does any of this do now?" The words felt like thorns as they scraped past her throat, but she forced them out anyway. Agatha stared at her, her expression pained. "I should have done something, but I didn't. I think that sentence sums up the last six years of my life, and I need to deal with that. I need to think about my future. You’re living your life; I need to start living mine."

Agatha shook her head, her eyes burning with the intensity of a thousand unsaid words, but Rio didn’t waver. She couldn’t afford to — not this time.

"I know I’m a mess, but I’m going to work on it. I’ll be okay, I promise. You don’t have to worry about me anymore." When Agatha frowned in doubt, Rio simply shrugged. "Can I ask you for one thing? One last thing?"

"Anything," Agatha whispered.

"Don't invite me to the wedding."

Agatha said nothing; she simply searched Rio’s eyes. Rio knew that Agatha was buried under a mountain of things she wanted to say, but the time for talking had passed. Neither of them would speak another word.

With tears streaming down her cheeks, Agatha finally nodded. She turned and walked away without looking back, disappearing into the night. It was as if she had never been there at all — as if the entire encounter had been a hallucination.

If letting go was the only way to move on, then that was exactly what Rio would do.

***

Present Day

Benito checked his watch as Kate dismounted; it was only six-thirty in the morning. A farmhand moved quickly to take the reins while his fiancée headed toward the porch, grinning from ear to ear. She sank into the armchair beside him, looking energized.

"Enjoying yourself out there?" he asked with a chuckle. Kate laughed softly, reaching for a coffee cup from the small table between them.

"You have no idea," she said, stretching contentedly. Benito nodded, trying to hide his amusement. "Who would’ve thought Darby could be this much fun?"

Laughing, he craned his neck to see if Lilia was nearby. Seeing she wasn't, he looked back at Kate, pointedly arching an eyebrow.

He glanced around to ensure Lilia wasn't within earshot before leaning in, arching a pointed eyebrow at Kate. "You need to behave," he teased, though his grin betrayed his stern tone.

Kate widened her eyes in mock innocence. "I haven't done a thing! I just woke up and went for a ride."

"Rio still doesn't know about us, not officially, anyway, so let's keep the scuttlebutt to a minimum until we get the wedding details sorted."

"I have no idea what you're talking about," she said, struggling to keep a straight face. Benito rolled his eyes as he offered her a tray of Lilia's mini croissants. "You’re the one who kept saying I wouldn't adapt to ranch life, but I love it. I'm even waking up at dawn to ride." She took a bite, nodding in satisfaction. "But seriously, Benny, how long are we staying?"

"I'm not sure," he admitted, his voice trailing off into a weary sigh. "I haven't had a real chance to talk to Rio. The business needs a total restructure, and—well, I just don't know yet."

"Are you considering staying long-term?" she asked, reading him perfectly.

"Would you hate me if I said yes?" he asked, his voice tinged with regret. Kate’s expression softened instantly. She reached out to caress his face, shaking her head. "I don't know how we’d make it work, but I feel like I need to be here right now. For my sister."

"She’s family, Benny. I support you. She can be a pain in the ass, sure, but she needs you and you need her. There's Agatha to consider, too."

Benito nodded, his face clouding with worry. "I have no clue what Agatha's plan is, but I’m honestly liable to lock her in the basement if it keeps her from running back to California."

"I’d rather be here with her," Kate admitted, surprising him. "I don't have any family left besides you guys. You both need to be here right now, and I want to be here for you."

"You're an angel," he said, smiling as he kissed her hand.

"My lovely lovebirds!" Lilia interrupted, stepping onto the porch with a fresh tray of pastries. "I made more because Monty told me Kate was out riding early. I figured she’d be hungry."

"Ma’am, you really didn't have to!" Kate said, her cheeks flushing as Benito gave her a knowing look; gossip on the ranch clearly traveled faster than a horse.

Lilia dismissed the thanks with a wave. "None of that 'Ma’am' business, dear. Just Lilia is fine." She turned to Benito, her eyes bright. "You never mentioned she was a rider! Does Riandra know? She’s going to love that."

"My dad never told you?" Benito asked. "Kate was raised on a ranch."

"Really?" Lilia turned back to Kate, who nodded through a mouthful of croissant.

"Yeah, my father is a horse breeder," Kate explained. "It’s a bit different back in Poland, always freezing and icy, but I grew up in the stables."

"Goodness, Rio is going to adore you!" Lilia beamed.

"Speaking of Rio, where is she?" Benito asked, checking the time again. "I hoped to catch her for breakfast, but she’s nowhere to be found."

"I don't think she slept at home," Kate said with a casual shrug. Both Benito and Lilia turned to her, startled. "I passed her room this morning; the door was open and the bed was perfectly made. I wasn't prying, I just noticed."

"Don't you worry about that," Lilia said, patting Benito’s shoulder dismissively. "It’s perfectly normal. She’s a grown woman, Benito." He rolled his eyes, but Lilia continued, "She never stays away too long without checking in. She’ll turn up by lunch or dinner, you mark my words."

***

Late into the night, Benito and Kate were nestled together on the living room floor, surrounded by a sea of cushions and open boxes of photo albums. Though Kate had grown close to Javier before he passed, she had never actually visited the ranch. Her entire understanding of the place was built on Benito’s stories; it only felt right that, now that she was finally here, she should see the history for herself.

“My God, is that Agatha?” Kate asked, pulling a photo from the stack. Benito leaned in, smiling at the image of himself as a baby nestled between Agatha and Rio, both girls beaming down at him.

“Yeah,” he said, sifting through another album for something specific. “She’s probably in every single picture we have.”

“It’s just so hard to wrap my head around her and your sister being a couple,” Kate murmured. She held up another photo — a candid shot of Rio and Agatha fast asleep, tangled in each other’s arms in the porch hammock. “When I met Agatha, she was already married. I never could have pictured her with anyone else.”

“Honestly? It was hard for me to see her with Tessa,” Benito admitted with a nostalgic sigh. Kate closed the album and gave him her full attention. “It was that first love kind of thing, you know?” Kate nodded softly as he continued. “My whole childhood was just the two of them. I think I was lucky, I grew up surrounded by so much love. I had my parents, her parents, and then I had them. They loved each other with an intensity I’ve never seen since.” Kate watched him, moved by the weight of his words. “When they finally ended, something in my sister just snapped. I don't know exactly what it was, but she was never the same. Sometimes I think she just... forgot how to love.”

“That’s heavy as fuck.”

“But it’s the truth. She broke,” he murmured sadly, his shoulders slumping. “And it wasn’t just the breakup. My mother died the same week Agatha left for California.” Kate’s eyes widened in shock. “Losing mom and losing Agatha at the exact same time... it was too much. Every time Rio tried to crawl out of that hole, Agatha would reappear for a visit, and Rio would sink right back in. It was a bizarre, vicious cycle.” He shook his head, the memories clearly taking a toll. “I spent my entire adolescence watching my sister disappear into a bottomless pit. She was physically there in the house, but she wasn't her. I missed her even when she was standing right in front of me. Those were the six worst years of my life.”

“What was she like before then?” Kate asked softly. “Before the breakup? Before your mother?”

Benito offered a faint, bittersweet smile. “She never stopped smiling.”

***

Twenty Years Ago

Ten-year-old Benito stood tall behind the booth's counter, adjusting the makeshift toga his mother had sewn for him. He beamed as he watched Agatha and Rio standing hand-in-hand, both stifling giggles as they waited for him to speak.

"I now pronounce you wife and wife," he declared with mock solemnity, puffing out his chest. The two leaned in for a quick kiss, and the crowd of children watching erupted into cheers.

"What is your first wish as my bride, Mrs. Agatha Harkness-Vidal?" Rio asked, sweeping into a low bow. Agatha laughed, rolling her eyes affectionately.

She was about to answer when Head Over Boots began blaring from the loudspeakers. Their faces lit up instantly.

"That’s our song!" Rio exclaimed, her smile widening. Agatha nodded enthusiastically.

"It’s perfect for our first dance," she said, catching Rio’s hand and pulling her toward the center of the square, right into the heart of the celebration.

It was the harvest festival, and the entire town had gathered in the square among rows of booths offering every homemade treat imaginable. The festivities had started early — rides for the kids, drinks for the adults, and music that never seemed to stop. That year, Benito had taken his role as the Matchmaker Saint very seriously, officiating over seven weddings, including his sister’s.

Having had his fill of the games, he was now content to swipe sweets from the booths while watching the crowd. It was nearly midnight, and a heavy sleepiness was starting to settle in, but he wasn't about to ask to go home — not while Rio was having the time of her life.

Perched on a wine barrel and working through his latest ear of sweet corn, he watched his sister dance awkwardly with Agatha in her arms. He knew Rio usually detested dancing in public, but with Agatha, she was a whirlwind of pure joy. Rio tried miserably to lead, her hands resting on Agatha’s waist, while Agatha dissolved into laughter, pressing her forehead against Rio's to try and guide their stumbling steps.

He loved seeing her like this — clumsy, happy, and radiant. Rio had large brown eyes, and though people often said they shared the same look, Benito thought his sister’s eyes were far more beautiful. They seemed to catch the light whenever she was with Agatha. It was as if they both glowed the moment they were together.

Benito didn't quite understand the complexities of love, but if anyone had asked him to define it, he would have pointed at them. To him, love was whatever made people shine like that. And Riandra was absolutely glowing.

They danced through several more songs until he noticed Rio’s expression turn to one of playful exhaustion. She was clearly begging for a break, and Agatha finally nodded, laughing as they walked over to him.

"Enjoying the party, Benny?" Agatha asked, ruffling his hair. He nodded through a mouthful of corn.

"Nice moves out there," he teased his sister. Rio, her arm still firmly around Agatha’s waist, just rolled her eyes at him.

They stood together for a while, chatting and sharing quiet moments of affection, until Richard approached to break up the party.

"Ready? It's time to head home," Richard said, his brows knit. He looked between the two girls, already bracing for the inevitable protests. Benito muffled a laugh; he knew that even though they’d see each other first thing tomorrow, the goodbye was always a drama.

"Dad, already?" Agatha groaned, pulling Rio’s arms tighter around her. Rio looked at her father-in-law with a puppy-dog pout, resting her head on Agatha’s shoulder.

"It's past eleven. You know your mother is going to have a fit."

"But it's the harvest festival!" Rio interjected. Richard just laughed and shrugged.

"You know the rules, girls."

"I have my car, Richard," Rio insisted, stepping back. "Benny and I aren't staying much longer anyway. I'll drop Agatha off."

"It wouldn't be a problem for me," Richard murmured, "but Eva doesn't want you two together past a certain hour, not after the last time." He shook his head, and Agatha’s face turned a deep shade of crimson while Rio awkwardly looked at her feet.

"Dad!" Agatha scolded. Richard let out a hearty laugh.

"Let’s go, Rapunzel," he said, patting his daughter’s shoulder. "I’m sure if you let down your hair, your prince will find her way up the almond tree to your window soon enough."

"Dad!" she repeated, mortified, while Rio finally broke into a laugh.

"You think I don't know?" Richard asked with a knowing arch of his eyebrow. Agatha opened her mouth to argue, found no words, and simply gave up. "Bye, Benny. Bye, Rio."

"See ya, Richard," Rio said. She pulled Agatha into one last embrace, ruffling her hair. "I’ll see you later," she whispered. Agatha beamed, throwing a wink over her shoulder as she walked toward the car.

Once the car pulled away, Rio sat on the barrel next to Benito, draping an arm over his shoulder. He leaned comfortably against her.

"Are you tired?" she asked, looking down at him. He nodded.

"A little."

"We can head home."

"But you have to wait a bit," he said, looking up at her. "So it doesn't look like you only left so you could sneak through Agatha’s window." Rio gave his ear a playful flick. "Hey!"

"You can't just say things like that out loud, you know."

“But it’s true!”

"Doesn't matter!" she said, trying to stay firm, but the smile tugging at her lips gave her away.

"You look like a dork when you're all in love," he teased. She flicked him again, but he just kept laughing.

"And you're only picking on me because you don't have a girlfriend yet," she said, sticking her tongue out. He mimicked her, sticking his own out in response.

"One day, I'll have one."

"Is that so?" she teased, wide-eyed. He nudged her, and she laughed. "You will, Benny. I know you will. When you're my age, you'll be a real heartbreaker."

"What's it like?" he asked, suddenly serious. "Falling in love?"

Rio’s smile softened as she scratched the back of her neck, her cheeks flushing. "It's the best thing in the world," she said, her voice dropping as if sharing a secret. "It feels like a thousand birds are fluttering in your stomach. All the bad stuff, the fear, the anxiety, it all just vanishes when she holds your hand. Sometimes I get so nervous, but then she looks at me, and suddenly everything makes sense. It’s like a piece of your heart is beating outside your chest. Agatha is a part of my heart, she’s my whole heart."

***

Present Day

"She was sweet," Benito said, his voice trailing off as his gaze drifted into the distance. "So sweet." He chuckled softly, a flood of childhood memories with his sister returning to him. "That gentleness, that light... she lost it when mom died. And over the next six years, with Agatha constantly coming and going, she lost even more pieces of herself. But she was sweet. I miss that. I miss her."

"I know I haven’t really gotten to know her yet, but it’s hard to imagine her like that," Kate admitted, her brow furrowed as she studied photos of Rio smiling beside her brother. "She seems so hardened now. I know she’s going through a lot, but I haven't seen her show a trace of kindness to anyone."

"Like I said, she changed," he murmured sadly. "When I moved to California, we drifted apart. I think she resented me for leaving; things were never the same after that. But while I was gone, my father said she transformed. Even from a distance, I could see it. I saw it during my visits, in the way she handled the ranch and the business. She completely blossomed. I don’t know what the turning point was, but something clicked, and she thrived. My father was so proud; he couldn’t stop talking about how well she was doing. And the winery... it really took off. Even when she wasn’t speaking to me, I could tell she was enjoying life. I thought—I don't know—maybe she was finally becoming herself again." He gave a helpless shrug. "But seeing her like this now? I just don't know."

"I can't imagine how painful that is, watching someone you love just shut down," Kate said softly, reaching out to stroke his hair. He nodded, taking a long, steadying breath.

"That’s why I want to stay," he told her. Kate nodded understandingly. "If she found her way back once, she can do it again. And I want to be here for her this time."

Their quiet moment was shattered by Lilia, who burst onto the porch breathless, her hands braced on her hips. Seeing her so shaken, Benito stood up, his face clouded with concern.

"Lilia, what’s wrong?"

"Did Riandra call you? Have you heard from her at all today?" she asked, her voice tight with distress. Benito instinctively checked his phone, even though he already knew the answer. He shook his head.

"No, why?"

"Neno, I think something’s wrong."

***

"No, Tommy!" It was supposed to be a scolding, but Natasha ended up laughing as her son crammed three meatballs into his mouth at once. "Honey, not like that!"

She glanced at Wanda, who was currently hiding behind her hand to stifle her own giggles. "You’re not helping," Natasha murmured, though her wife only shrugged, completely unable to contain her amusement.

"I can do it too!" Billy chirped. Before anyone could intervene, he shoved four meatballs into his mouth.

"Boys!" Wanda reprimanded through her laughter. Natasha was about to say more, but a heavy, urgent pounding at the door cut her short.

"Were you expecting someone?" Natasha asked. Wanda shook her head.

"No, Yelena wasn't coming tonight. Did you call Rio?"

"No," Natasha answered, her brow furrowing as she got up to check the door.

She walked down the hallway into the living room, her eyes widening in surprise when she opened the door to find Benito. He was soaking wet, shivering from the rain, and looked visibly shaken.

"Benito?" she asked, her confusion deepening. "Is everything okay? Come inside."

"Is Rio here?" he asked, his voice breathless and frantic. Natasha shook her head.

"No, why? What’s going on?"

"She left yesterday and hasn't come back. She’s not answering her phone, and no one has seen her," he said, the words tumbling out in a panicked rush. Natasha felt her own heart begin to race. "Lilia says she never stays out without telling someone, but she didn't sleep at home. Bucky said he saw her last night but doesn't know where she went, and Olivia is out of town."

"Okay," Natasha said, nodding to steady herself. "I'll just—" She started to turn back toward the dining room, but Wanda was already there, watching with a concerned expression.

"Go, babe," Wanda said firmly. "I’ve got the boys. Call me as soon as you know something."

"Okay," Natasha breathed. Wanda stepped closer, cupping Natasha’s face and pressing their lips together in a quick, grounding kiss.

"Just breathe, okay?" Wanda whispered, resting her forehead against Natasha’s. "She’s fine. You’re going to find her."

"Yelena’s searching the vineyard, and Lilia is waiting at the house," Benito cut in. "I thought we could look together, you know her usual spots better than I do."

"Of course. Let's go," Natasha said, grabbing her jacket from the hook. She looked back at her wife one last time. "I’ll call you." Wanda nodded, blowing her a kiss as they stepped out into the rain, her eyes closing in a silent prayer the moment the door clicked shut.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 14: choices

Chapter Summary

this one is about the weight and consequences of our choices

Chapter Notes

like I said, it’s a slow burn with a lot of baggage, and we’ll follow their journey little by little. i hope you guys can be patient with me and also, i’m not sure if you’re going to like this smut; it’s not something I’m very used to writing, and english isn’t my native language but i'm trying!!!!!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

"I never was ready so I watch you go. Sometimes you just don't know the answer 'till someone's on their knees and asks you" – Champagne Problems, Taylor Swift

It had been far too long since she had known such peace. Surrounded by the quiet rhythms of the ranch, Agatha felt a sudden, deep sense of being nurtured, realizing only then how much she had craved the simple, intrinsic warmth of family life. She was still finding her footing, lingering in the grace period of a guest because she hadn't yet found the words to tell her mother the truth about her stay. Even so, she threw herself into the daily chores; the distraction was a gift, and her family’s affection was the medicine her healing required.

Nicholas had always loved mornings. Even as a baby, he greeted the dawn with such enthusiasm that Agatha eventually adopted the habit herself. At home, she would wake early to prepare breakfast just for the two of them, guarding those quiet hours as a private ritual. Life at the farm shifted that routine in the best possible way. Now, Nicholas rose with the sun, following Lilia like a shadow to the main house. From the living room window, Agatha often watched them on the porch, his small silhouette tucked between Kate and Benito. Sometimes she joined the circle; other times, she preferred to linger over her coffee alone, only for Nicholas to eventually burst back inside like a whirlwind, eager to announce the day’s adventures or plot his next move behind his uncle.

With the weekend arrival, Benito was home, and Nicholas became his constant companion. Agatha spent the afternoon on the porch next to her mother, the rhythmic click of crochet needles providing a steady soundtrack to her reading. Every so often, she looked up to see her son charging through the brush on a stick horse or racing along the fence line, trying to keep pace with the stallions. Seeing him so safe and happy, wrapped in his own little bubble of joy, she found herself smiling with a rare, genuine ease.

By mid-afternoon, she decided to write. It was a hobby from her youth that she had abandoned as the years slipped away. She rarely had free time, and when she did, she usually dismissed the urge as silly — mostly because Tessa had always thought it was silly.

Looking back, her marriage had been doomed before it even began. She felt she had been the foolish one for insisting on the mistake, hoping that what felt right would eventually become right — that appearances could somehow be forged into reality. Agatha had always been a believer in ideals; her marriage was just one more distant dream she had desperately wanted to be real. It was the fairy tale Tessa swore they shared, and for years, Agatha had willingly believed in it because she wanted it to be true. Everything was simpler that way.

But that simplicity came at a price. She recognized now that she’d had to ignore so much, swallowing her pain and making herself small just to fit into the life she thought she wanted. What hurt most was the realization that she had chosen it herself. She had wanted to marry Tessa; she had said "yes" even when her heart begged her to say "no."

Agatha had asked for the divorce before leaving for Darby, but the truth was they had been separated for a long time. She couldn't remember the last time she had seen Tessa as a partner or a lover; wife had become a mere title, and Agatha felt like an actress playing a role. That was why she had started writing again — finding herself in the quiet moments when Tessa wasn't home.

Agatha returned to writing because she lacked the courage to tell anyone — not even Alex, Lilia, or Benito — the truth about her marriage. She couldn't bring herself to admit how small she had felt. She was haunted by her own inertia, disgusted by the memory of all those times she had allowed her wife to undress her to satisfy a role, even with a sob caught in her throat. She had endured it all in the desperate hope that things would improve, or that eventually, the two of them would make sense again. For years, the words had remained trapped in her chest, even when she wanted to scream for help. She started writing because she finally needed to give a voice to her silence.

Since arriving at the farm, she had written endlessly. She knew that ink on a page wasn't a total cure; she still needed the strength to exorcise the demons that had been consuming her for years. But for now, it was enough. Agatha would retreat to the basement for hours, her laptop balanced on her knees, reflecting on the words staring back at her from the screen. In that solitude, she digested years of pain and reached a vital realization: she wasn't the one to blame. She wasn't guilty; she was a victim. The last thing she needed was to crucify herself. She just needed time to find her footing and start over. As lost as she felt, the desire for a new beginning was real.

She had spent half her life wanting to escape Darby and the other half effectively running away from it, but now she felt there was no other place in the world she should be but here — it was home. It was a good place to start over.

These hours of writing were cathartic. After closing her laptop, she would often spend long minutes crying — not out of despair, but as a release. It was a strange sensation, but slowly, she was learning to forgive herself. She felt it every time she saw her son running with his curls catching the wind, or when the smell of her mother’s cooking made her stomach growl. She felt it during long walks with Benito and in the sound of Nicholas’s laughter. Bit by bit, Agatha was starting over.

She had just finished one of these sessions and was washing her face in the basement bathroom when she saw her son’s reflection in the mirror. He was leaning against the doorframe, his brow knitted and his large brown eyes filled with a mix of concern and curiosity.

Agatha managed a weak, reassuring smile. "Everything is okay, I promise," she said, turning to face him. He continued to stare at her suspiciously. "I swear, I was just reading. You know how sensitive I get."

He tilted his head, eyes narrowed in doubt. She laughed softly, crouching down to his level. "I'm fine, Nicky. I’ve felt better since we got here than I have in a long time."

Nicholas studied her eyes for a moment before nodding in agreement. She smiled, resting her hands on his shoulders. He looked like a different child than the polished, stiff boy of a few weeks ago. Now, he wore a rumpled flannel shirt over a dingy tank top and dirt-stained denim shorts. His curls were a wild mess, and the constant frown that once clouded his face had vanished. Seeing him so peaceful brought a cozy, lingering warmth to her chest.

"Are you hungry?" she asked.

He nodded eagerly.

"What do you think about making cookies? Just you and me?"

When his face broke into a wide, genuine grin, Agatha couldn't help but do the same.

***

Agatha nearly laughed at her reflection in the hallway mirror. Her hair was pulled into a messy, hurried ponytail, and she was swallowed by one of her father’s old flannel shirts — a fraying, oversized garment in faded shades of purple and green that hung down to her thighs. Paired with her sweatpants, she was dusted in flour from head to toe.

She and Nicholas had made a spectacular mess of the kitchen, but for once, Tessa wasn't there to scold them. Only Evanora had witnessed the chaos, and upon seeing them kneading dough in a literal cloud of flour, she had simply laughed and joined in. While her mother baked a cake, Agatha and Nicholas cut out cookies, and they transformed the fresh grapes Rio had dropped off into two pitchers of juice. They eventually moved their feast to the porch, lingering there together with full bellies and easy smiles.

Later, while Agatha cleaned the kitchen, Nicholas settled at his grandmother’s feet, mesmerized by the rhythmic movement of her crochet needles. She watched them for a moment, a quiet smile playing on her lips, before heading downstairs for a long, hot bath.

Refreshed, Agatha retreated to her basement sanctuary. Her phone vibrated on the bedside table, and her face lit up when she saw the name on the screen.

"Do you have any idea how humiliated I felt finding out from Benny that you were in Darby? What kind of best friend are you?" Alex’s voice crackled through the line, heavy with mock exasperation.

Agatha let out a soft laugh, letting herself fall back onto the bed. "Where else would I be?"

"Literally anywhere! I don't know!" Alex shot back.

"Alex, I asked for a divorce, vanished with my son and all our belongings, and practically erased our existence from that house. Where else would I go?" When silence met her question, Agatha chuckled. "The old saying never fails: the good son always returns home."

"I think it’s the prodigal son, isn't it? You went out, saw the world, and came back with nothing but your sins." Agatha opened her mouth to protest, but Alex’s laughter cut her off. "I’m kidding. Honestly, I was worried when you disappeared, but I was relieved at the same time. I knew you’d be okay anywhere, as long as you were out of that house."

Agatha sighed, the tension leaving her shoulders as Alex’s voice softened. "I'm proud of you, Agatha. I'm so proud of you for finally leaving."

Agatha closed her eyes and let out a long, heavy sigh. A familiar twinge of dread tightened in the pit of her stomach — a shadow of the fear that had haunted her for years. Even here, in the safety of Darby, she hadn't been able to shake it yet.

"It wasn't easy, Alex. It really wasn't," Agatha began, her voice trailing off into another sigh. "I don't even know how I managed it. I just..." she paused, shrugging to herself in the empty room. "I just stopped thinking. When my aunt called about the funeral, something just clicked. I hung up and tried calling Tessa a dozen times, but as usual, she didn't answer. I couldn't stop crying. Then I saw Nicholas sleeping—it was just the two of us at home, and I realized I could finally cry." She spoke like she was making a confession, her voice thick with a sob she hadn't realized she was holding back. "I could cry without being afraid, and I did. I cried for hours until I realized I just couldn't do it anymore. I'm done."

"You endured it for a long time, Agatha. Far longer than you ever should have," Alex said softly. Agatha nodded, letting the tears flow freely now. "I’m so sorry you didn't have the strength to leave sooner. You have so many people who love you, and it killed us to see you like that. But there are some things only you can do for yourself; no one could take your hand and pull you out of there. I’m just so happy you’re out. I’m here for whatever you need, you know that."

"Thank you," Agatha whispered, her voice overflowing with gratitude. "I miss you."

"I miss you too," Alex admitted. Agatha could practically see her rolling her eyes; Alex was one of the sweetest people she knew, but she had always been allergic to overly emotional displays. "I really am happy for you, but I’m also indignant that you dragged my godson to the middle of the woods. What about me? Everyone is on vacation at the farm and I’m stuck here."

Agatha let out a weak laugh, imagining the dramatic eye roll on the other end. "It’s not a vacation, Alex. But for what it's worth, he’s loving every second. I’ve never seen him like this. He spends his days chasing horses and following Benito around. He’s so calm, he hasn’t had a single breakdown since we arrived. He’s just... happy."

"That’s wonderful," Alex sighed, her voice softening with genuine relief. "I’m so glad to hear that. I was worried the sudden change in routine would be hard on him. You know how he usually gets."

"I was terrified of that too, but he hasn't withdrawn once. If anything, he’s more outgoing than ever. It’s a relief I can’t even describe. At least I did one thing right."

"You are a great mother, Agatha," Alex said firmly. "He’s doing well because he’s with you, not just because of the farm. And honestly, we shouldn't be surprised. Of course his life would improve the second he got away from that viper."

"Alex..." Agatha murmured, her voice laced with reproach.

"No, don't start," Alex shot back. "You finally got out of that marriage; you can't keep lying to yourself. You need to see her for what she really is. I know what I’ve seen is barely a fraction of what you’ve actually endured, because I know you, Agatha."

Agatha squeezed her eyes shut as a familiar lump formed in her throat.

"You need time to heal," Alex continued, "but you also need to process everything you suffered. To do that, you have to call it what it is. You have to see her for who she is, not the version of her you’ve been clinging to."

"I know," Agatha whispered. She wanted the lecture to end, unable to cope with the sharp sting of reality or the dread clouding her mind. Desperate to change the subject, she brought it back to her son. "He’s fine here. On the first day, I explained that I needed some time. He knows how much she and I used to fight, he saw it all."

"I know he did," Alex murmured in agreement.

"I told him we wouldn't be together anymore and that I needed to stay here at the farm for a while. He just nodded. He wants this too, Alex. He wants to be here with me."

"Of course he does. He loves you. You know his silence isn't a reflection of how he feels about you." Rationally, Agatha knew that, but the weight of it was still heavy. "So, what’s the plan for his treatment? Tessa isn't an obstacle anymore, thank god."

"Alex, I have no idea," Agatha murmured, sitting up and burying her face in her hands. "I know he needs professional help, a neuropsychological evaluation, a psychologist, a psychiatrist, maybe even speech therapy. He’ll likely need medication, too. I know he needs it all, but I don't even know where to begin."

"What do you mean? Is there no hospital in Darby? The specialists—"

"It’s not that. It’s just..." Agatha sighed again. "I stopped working six years ago. I don’t have a cent of my own. All I have are the cards from our joint account, and Tessa is already calling, begging me to come home, even though—"

"She’s calling?" Alex interrupted, her tone sharp with urgency. "What does she want? Why is she calling? Did you answer her? Agatha, why would you answer?"

"I have to answer, Alex! He’s her son, too!"

"Oh, what a dedicated mother!" Alex spat, dripping with sarcasm. "She’s neglected that boy his whole life. She’s only good for posing for pictures, and you know it. As far as she’s concerned, he’ll never get the help he needs."
